inciting sympathy for refugees." </ref><ref>"[http://www.spiegel.de/international/europe/european-refugee-crisis-worsens-in-mediterranean-a-964304.html Europe's African Refugee Crisis: Is the Boat Really Full?]". ''[[Der Spiegel]]''. 15 April 2014.</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=UNHCR chief issues key guidelines for dealing with Europe's refugee crisis |url=http://www.unhcr.org/55e9793b6.html |publisher=UNHCR}}"This is a primarily refugee crisis, not only a migration phenomenon".</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=European Refugee Crisis 2015: Why So Many People Are Fleeing The Middle East And North Africa |url=http://www.ibtimes.com/european-refugee-crisis-2015-why-so-many-people-are-fleeing-middle-east-north-africa-2081454 |work=International Business Times |date=3 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=What You Need to Know About Europe's Refugee Crisis: Q&A |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-09-08/what-you-need-to-know-about-europe-s-refugee-crisis-q-a |work=Bloomberg |date=8 September 2015}}</ref> was a period characterised by high numbers of people arriving in the [[European Union]] (EU) overseas from across the [[Mediterranean Sea]] or overland through [[Southeast Europe]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34131911|title=Migrant crisis: Migration to Europe explained in seven charts|website=BBC|date=4 March 2016|access-date=27 September 2020 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=EU migrant crisis: facts and figures {{!}} News {{!}} European Parliament |url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/news/en/headlines/society/20170629STO78630/eu-migrant-crisis-facts-and-figures |website=europarl.europa.eu |access-date=28 March 2019 |language=en |date=30 June 2017}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34131911|title=Migrant crisis: Migration to Europe explained in seven charts|date=4 March 2016|work=BBC News|access-date=29 May 2017|language=en-GB}}</ref> In March 2019, the [[European Commission]] declared the migrant crisis to be at an end, although displaced people continued to arrive.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/mar/06/eu-declares-migration-crisis-over-hits-out-fake-news-european-commission|title=EU declares migration crisis over as it hits out at 'fake news'|website=The Guardian|date=6 March 2019|author=Jennifer Rankin|access-date=23 November 2019}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Refugee Situations |url=http://data2.unhcr.org/en/situations/mediterranean?page=1&view=grid&Type%255B%255D=3&Search=%2523monthly%2523%7cjournal=Refugees/Migrants |website=UNHCR Operational Portal |publisher=UNHCR}}</ref>

The [[migrant crisis]] was part of a pattern of increased forced migration to Europe from other continents which is thought to have begun in 2014.<ref>{{cite web |last1=Evans |first1=Gareth |title=Europe's migrant crisis: the year that changed a continent |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-53925209 |website=BBC News}}</ref> At the peak of the crisis in 2015, The [[United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees]] (UNHCR) observed that the top three nationalities among over one million refugees arriving from the [[Mediterranean Sea]] were [[Refugees of the Syrian Civil War|Syrian]] (46.7%), [[Afghan refugees|Afghan]] (20.9%) and [[Refugees of Iraq|Iraqi]] (9.4%).<ref>{{cite journal|date=31 March 2016|title=Monthly Arrivals by Nationality to Greece, Italy and Spain|url=http://data.unhcr.org/mediterranean/documents.php?page=1&view=grid&Type%5B%5D=3&Search=%23monthly%23|journal=Refugees/Migrants Emergency Response – Mediterranean|access-date=14 May 2016}}</ref> By 2019, the number of displaced arrivals to the mediterranean had dropped to 129,663 people.<ref>{{cite web |title=Refugee Situations |url=http://data2.unhcr.org/en/situations/mediterranean?page=1&view=grid&Type%255B%255D=3&Search=%2523monthly%2523%7cjournal=Refugees/Migrants |website=UNHCR Operational Portal |publisher=UNHCR}}</ref>

Many refugees that arrived in Italy and Greece came from countries where armed conflict was ongoing ([[Syrian civil war|Syrian civil war (2011–present)]], [[War in Afghanistan (2001–present)]], [[Iraqi conflict (2003–present)]]) or which otherwise were considered to be "[[Refugee crisis#Modern and contemporary refugee crises|refugee-producing]]" and for whom [[Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees|international protection]] is needed.

Of the migrants arriving in Europe by sea in 2015, 58% were males over 18 years of age (77% of adults), 17% were females over 18 (22% of adults) and the remaining 25% were under 18.<ref name="bsUNHCR2015"/>{{Clarify|reason=What is the relevance to (the topic of) this article? If there’s no relevance, the sentence can be deleted.|date=August 2020}} The number of deaths at sea rose to record levels in April 2015, when five boats carrying approximately 2,000 migrants to Europe [[List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea|sank in the Mediterranean Sea]], with the combined death toll estimated at more than 1,200 people.<ref>{{cite news|title=Mediterranean Crisis 2015 at six months: refugee and migrant numbers highest on record|url=http://www.unhcr.org/5592b9b36.html|work=UNHCR|date=1 July 2015}}</ref> The shipwrecks took place during conflicts and refugee crises in several Greater Middle Eastern and African countries, which increased the total number of forcibly [[displaced people]] worldwide at the end of 2014 to almost 60 million, the highest level since [[World War II]].<ref name="UNHCRtrends"/><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/01/world/europe/a-mass-migration-crisis-and-it-may-yet-get-worse.html|title=A Mass Migration Crisis, and It May Yet Get Worse|author=Rod Nordland|newspaper=The New York Times|date=31 October 2015|access-date=1 November 2015}}</ref>

== Terminology ==
The [[BBC]] used the term "migrant" to represent all the people on the move during this period in its review articles published in 2016 "Migrant crisis: Migration to Europe explained"<ref>{{cite news |title=Migrant crisis: Migration to Europe explained in seven charts |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34131911 |work=BBC News |date=4 March 2016}}</ref> and 2015 "Europe migrant crisis".<ref>{{cite news |title=Europe migrant crisis |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-32395181 |work=BBC News |date=19 October 2016}}</ref> According to the BBC, the crisis included people who had not yet applied for asylum, refugees, and economic migrants.<ref>{{cite news |title=Migrant crisis: Migration to Europe explained in seven charts |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34131911 |work=BBC News |date=4 March 2016}}</ref>

==Background==
[[File:Immigration in the EU.png|thumb|Immigration of non-EU nationals (green),<ref name="Immigration in the EU">{{cite web |title=Immigration in the EU |url=http://ec.europa.eu/dgs/home-affairs/e-library/docs/infographics/immigration/migration-in-eu-infographic_en.pdf |publisher=European Commission}}</ref> asylum applicants (orange)<ref>{{cite web |title=Asylum and first time asylum applicants by citizenship, age and sex Annual aggregated data (rounded) |url=http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do |publisher=EUROSTAT}}</ref> and illegal border-crossings (blue)<ref>{{cite web |url=http://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annual_Risk_Analysis_2015.pdf#14 |title=Annual Risk Analysis 2015 |publisher=[[Frontex]] |date=27 April 2015}}</ref> in the European Union, 2010–2014]]
[[File:Migranti sbarcati in Italia 1997-2016.png|thumb|Migrants arriving in Italy by sea, 1997–2015<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ismu.org/irregolari-e-sbarchi-presenze/|title=Sbarchi e richieste di asilo 1997–2014|publisher=Fondazione Ismu}}</ref>]]

According to the [[UNHCR]], the EU countries with the biggest numbers of recognised refugees at the end of 2014 were France (252,264), Germany (216,973), Sweden (142,207) and the United Kingdom (117,161).<ref name="UNHCRtrends"/>

Prior to 2014, the number of unofficial border crossings by sea and land detected by [[Frontex]] at the external borders of the EU peaked at a total of 141,051 in 2011.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annual_Risk_Analysis_2015.pdf |title=Annual Risk Analysis 2015 |publisher=[[Frontex]] |date=27 April 2015}}</ref>

[[Eurostat]] reported [[Member state of the European Union|EU member states]] received over 1.2 million first-time asylum applications in 2015, more than twice as the previous year. Four states (Germany, Hungary, Sweden and Austria) received around two-thirds of the EU's asylum applications in 2015, with Hungary, Sweden and Austria being the top recipients of asylum applications per capita.<ref name="asylum2015" /> More than 1 million migrants crossed the [[Mediterranean Sea]] in 2015, considerably dropping to 364,000 in 2016,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/01/number-refugees-reaching-europe-plunged-2016-170106132732972.html|title=Number of refugees reaching Europe plunged in 2016|website=aljazeera.com}}</ref> before decreasing further in 2017.<ref name="NebehayIOM">{{cite news |last1=Nebehay |first1=Stephanie |title=Half as many migrants landed in Europe in 2017 as 2016: IOM |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-un/half-as-many-migrants-landed-in-europe-in-2017-as-2016-iom-idUSKBN1EU1KP |access-date=16 July 2018 |work=Reuters |date=5 January 2018}}</ref> According to the UN, an estimated 362,000 refugees and migrants risked their lives crossing the Mediterranean Sea in 2016, with 181,400 people arriving in Italy and 173,450 in Greece. In the first half of 2017, over 105,000 refugees and migrants entered Europe.<ref name="Commissioner">{{cite web |last=Commissioner |first=United Nations High |title=Europe situation |website=UNHCR |url=https://www.unhcr.org/europe-emergency.html |access-date=2020-09-29}}</ref>

=== Migrant smuggling ===
{{See also|Timeline of the European migrant crisis|List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea|List of migrant vehicle incidents in Europe}}
Several serious accidents and deaths occurred in Europe as a result of [[migrant smuggling]] since 1997: two in the Mediterranean Sea due to the [[capsizing]] of crowded and unseaworthy migrant smuggling vessels, and some on European soil due to the use of standard cargo trucks by smugglers to transport illegal migrants. The vast majority of deaths occurred while persons were being illegally smuggled across the Mediterranean and [[Aegean Sea]]s. More than 34,000 migrants and refugees have died trying to get to Europe since 1993.<ref>{{cite news |title=It's 34,361 and rising: how the List tallies Europe's migrant bodycount |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2018/jun/20/the-list-europe-migrant-bodycount |work=The Guardian |date=20 June 2018}}</ref>

==Causes of increased number of asylum seekers==
According to the UNHCR World Migration Report 2020, two of the main drivers for the increased displacement of people are disasters and conflict.<ref name=IOFM>{{cite news |last1=Staff |title=WORLD MIGRATION REPORT2020 |url=https://www.un.org/sites/un2.un.org/files/wmr_2020.pdf |access-date=5 October 2020 |publisher=UN (International Organization for Migration) |date=2019}}</ref>{{Dubious |date=October 2020}}

===Escaping from natural disasters===
{{Expand section |date=October 2020}}
Some of the economic migration from West Africa originated from the consequences of land degradation due to climate change.<ref>{{cite news |title=Climate refugees account for more than a half of all migrants but enjoy little protection |url=https://www.eesc.europa.eu/en/news-media/news/climate-refugees-account-more-half-all-migrants-enjoy-little-protection |access-date=7 October 2020 |work=European Economic and Social Committee |date=17 April 2020 |language=en}}</ref>

===Escaping from conflicts or persecution===
According to the [[United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees]], most of the people who arrived in Europe in 2015 were [[refugees]] fleeing war and [[persecution]]<ref name="UNHCRarrivals" /> in countries such as [[Syria]], [[Afghanistan]], [[Iraq]] and [[Eritrea]]: 84 percent of Mediterranean Sea arrivals in 2015 came from the world's top ten refugee-producing countries.<ref name="UNHCRarrivals1">{{cite news|date=30 December 2015|title=Over one million sea arrivals reach Europe in 2015|work=UNHCR|url=http://www.unhcr.org/5683d0b56.html|access-date=28 December 2016}}</ref> Wars fueling the migrant crisis are the [[Syrian Civil War]], the [[Iraq conflict (2003–present)|Iraq War]], the [[War in Afghanistan (2001–present)|War in Afghanistan]], the [[Somali Civil War (2009–present)|War in Somalia]] and the [[War in Darfur]]. Refugees from Eritrea, one of the [[Human rights in Eritrea|most repressive]] states in the world, fled from indefinite military [[conscription]] and [[forced labour]].<ref name="origins">{{cite news|date=10 September 2015|title=Refugee crisis: apart from Syrians, who is travelling to Europe?|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/10/refugee-crisis-apart-from-syrians-who-else-is-travelling-to-europe}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|date=22 July 2015|title=It's not at war, but up to 3% of its people have fled. What is going on in Eritrea?|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jul/22/eritrea-migrants-child-soldier-fled-what-is-going}}</ref> Some ethnicities or religions are more represented among the migrants than others; for instance, [[Kurds]] make up 80 to 90 percent of all Turkish refugees in Germany.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Auffallend viele kurdische Flüchtlinge|url=https://www.tagesspiegel.de/politik/asyl-in-deutschland-auffallend-viele-kurdische-fluechtlinge/14446010.html|website=tagesspiegel.de}}</ref>

Refugees coming from the Middle East tended to seek asylum in Europe.<ref>{{Cite news|title=A region-by-region guide to the Middle East's migrant crisis|language=en-US|newspaper=PBS NewsHour|url=https://www.pbs.org/newshour/updates/your-guide-to-europes-migrant-crisis/|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref> In 2015, over 80 percent of the refugees who arrived in Europe by sea came from Syria, Iraq, and Afghanistan.<ref>{{Cite news|date=3 March 2016|title=Why is EU struggling with migrants and asylum?|language=en-GB|newspaper=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-24583286|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref> Routes in which these refugees face while attempting to arrive in Europe are usually extremely dangerous.<ref>{{Cite journal|last=Daynes|first=Leigh|date=1 October 2016|title=The health impacts of the refugee crisis: a medical charity perspective|journal=Clinical Medicine|language=en|volume=16|issue=5|pages=437–440|doi=10.7861/clinmedicine.16-5-437|issn=1470-2118|pmc=6297302|pmid=27697805}}</ref> The jeopardy to endure such routes supported the arguments behind certain refugees' preferential motivations of seeking asylum within European nations.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Refugees|first=United Nations High Commissioner for|title=The sea route to Europe: The Mediterranean passage in the age of refugees|newspaper=UNHCR|url=http://www.unhcr.org/en-us/protection/operations/5592bd059/sea-route-europe-mediterranean-passage-age-refugees.html|access-date=17 November 2016}}</ref>

Below are the major regions of conflict that have resulted in the increase of asylum seekers in the European region.

==== Syria ====
The greatest number of refugees fleeing to Europe [[Syrian Arab Republic|originate from Syria]].{{Citation needed|date=March 2020}} [[Refugees of the Syrian Civil War]] are citizens and permanent residents of Syria, who have fled their country over the course of the [[Syrian Civil War]] (begin:2011). Since the start of the [[Syrian Civil War]] in 2011 more than six million (2016) were [[Internally displaced person|internally displaced]], and around five million (2016) had crossed into other countries,<ref>{{Cite web |url = http://www.unocha.org/syria|title=UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs 16_02_2016 }}</ref> with most seeking [[right of asylum|asylum]] or placed in [[Syrian refugee camps]] established in [[Refugees of the Syrian Civil War in Turkey|Turkey]], [[Refugees of the Syrian Civil War in Lebanon|Lebanon]], [[Refugees of the Syrian Civil War in Jordan|Jordan]], [[Refugees of the Syrian Civil War in Egypt|Egypt]], and EU. [[#Illegal border crossings by nationality|Detected illegal border crossings to the EU by Syrians]] was 78,887 in 2014, 594,059 in 2015, 88,551 in 2016, and 19,452 in 2017.

Syrians established diaspora in [[Syrians in Denmark|Denmark]], [[Syrians in Finland|Finland]], [[Syrians in Austria|Austria]],  [[Syrians in Germany|Germany]], [[Syrians in Greece|Greece]], [[Syrians in Norway|Norway]], [[Syrians in Sweden|Sweden]] and [[Syrians in the United Kingdom|United Kingdom]]. Their migration stems from severe socio-political oppression under [[Bashar al-Assad]]. Civil war ensued with clashes between pro and anti-government groups. In 2011, a group of pro-democracy Syrians protested in the city of [[Daraa]]. [[Bashar al-Assad|Al-Assad]] responded with force and consequently, more protests were triggered nationwide against the Assad regime. By July 2011, hundreds of thousands of people were protesting against President Assad. An early violent crackdown was enacted in an attempt to mitigate the uprisings, only to be met with more unrest. By [[Arab Spring|May 2011]], thousands of people had fled the country and the first refugee camps opened in Turkey. In March 2012, the UNHCR decided to appoint a Regional Refugee Coordinator for Syrian Refugees—recognising the growing concerns surrounding the crisis. Just a year later, in March 2013, the number of Syrian refugees reached 1,000,000. By December 2017, the UNHCR counted 1,000,000 asylum applications for Syrian refugees in the European Union. As of March 2018, UNHCR has counted nearly 5.6 million registered Syrian refugees worldwide.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://data2.unhcr.org/en/situations/syria|title=Situation Syria Regional Refugee Response|website=data2.unhcr.org|language=en|access-date=2018-03-17}}</ref>


{{Image array

| image2 = Syria-foreignborn-sw.png | caption2 = Syria-born persons in Sweden by sex, 2000-2016 ([[Statistics Sweden]])
}}

Anti-government forces were supported by external governments (including the US, UK and France<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.enca.com/hollande-confirms-french-delivery-arms-syrian-rebels|title=Hollande confirms French delivery of arms to Syrian rebels|date=21 August 2014|work=AFP|access-date=25 January 2015}}</ref>) in an effort to topple the Syrian government via classified programs such as [[Timber Sycamore]] (begin: 2012 or 2013 end: 2017) that effectively delivered thousands of tons of weaponry to [[Syrian opposition|rebel groups]].<ref name=":8">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/06/27/world/middleeast/cia-arms-for-syrian-rebels-supplied-black-market-officials-say.html|title=C.I.A. Arms for Syrian Rebels Supplied Black Market, Officials Say|access-date=2018-10-04|language=en}}</ref><ref name=":9">{{Cite web|url=http://www.janes.com/article/59374/us-arms-shipment-to-syrian-rebels-detailed|title=US arms shipment to Syrian rebels detailed {{!}} IHS Jane's 360|date=2016-12-05|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161205081205/http://www.janes.com/article/59374/us-arms-shipment-to-syrian-rebels-detailed|archive-date=2016-12-05|url-status=dead|access-date=2018-10-04}}</ref><ref name=":10">{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/trump-ends-covert-cia-program-to-arm-anti-assad-rebels-in-syria-a-move-sought-by-moscow/2017/07/19/b6821a62-6beb-11e7-96ab-5f38140b38cc_story.html|title=Trump ends covert CIA program to arm anti-Assad rebels in Syria, a move sought by Moscow|website=Washington Post|language=en|access-date=2018-10-04}}</ref><ref name=":11">{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/what-the-demise-of-the-cias-anti-assad-program-means/2017/07/20/f6467240-6d87-11e7-b9e2-2056e768a7e5_story.html|title=Opinion {{!}} What the demise of the CIA's anti-Assad program means|website=Washington Post|language=en|access-date=2018-10-04}}</ref><ref name=":13">{{Cite news|url=http://www.politico.com/story/2017/07/21/tony-thomas-syria-secret-program-cia-240818|title=Top general confirms end to secret U.S. program in Syria|work=POLITICO|access-date=2018-10-04|language=en}}</ref><ref name=":14">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2017/08/02/world/middleeast/cia-syria-rebel-arm-train-trump.html|title=Behind the Sudden Death of a $1 Billion Secret C.I.A. War in Syria|access-date=2018-10-04|language=en}}</ref><ref name=":15">{{Cite web|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/national-security/plans-to-send-heavier-weapons-to-cia-backed-rebels-in-syria-stall-amid-white-house-skepticism/2016/10/23/f166ddac-96ee-11e6-bb29-bf2701dbe0a3_story.html|title=Plans to send heavier weapons to CIA-backed rebels in Syria stall amid White House skepticism|website=Washington Post|language=en|access-date=2018-10-04}}</ref><ref name=":16">{{Cite web|url=https://www.csis.org/analysis/creeping-incrementalism-us-forces-and-strategy-iraq-and-syria-2011-2016-update|title=Creeping Incrementalism: U.S. Forces and Strategy in Iraq and Syria from 2011 to 2016: An Update|website=csis.org|language=en|access-date=2018-10-04}}</ref>

====Afghanistan====
[[Afghan refugees]] constitute the second-largest refugee population in the world.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.unhcr.org/en-us/afghanistan.html|title=Afghanistan|publisher=United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees|access-date=2018-03-17|language=en}}</ref> According to the UNHCR, there are almost 2.5 million registered refugees from Afghanistan. Most of these refugees fled the region due to war and persecution. The majority have resettled in Pakistan and Iran, though it became increasingly common to migrate further west to the European Union. Afghanistan faced over 40 years of conflict dating back to the [[Soviet–Afghan War|Soviet invasion in 1979]]. Since then, the nation faced fluctuating levels of [[War in Afghanistan (1978–present)|civil war]] amidst unending unrest. The increase in refugee numbers has been primarily attributed to the [[Taliban]] presence within Afghanistan. Their retreat in 2001 led to nearly 6 million Afghan refugees returning to their homeland. However, after [[Taliban insurgency|civil unrest and fighting alongside the Taliban's return]], nearly 2.5 million refugees fled Afghanistan.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rescue.org/article/afghanistan-what-you-need-know-about-one-worlds-longest-refugee-crises|title=Afghanistan: What you need to know about one of the world's longest refugee crises|date=2016-09-08|work=International Rescue Committee (IRC)|access-date=2018-04-07|language=en}}</ref> Most Afghan refugees, however, seek refuge in the neighboring nation of Pakistan. Increasing numbers, though, have committed to migrating to Turkey and the European Union.

====Kosovo====
[[File:Preference.png|thumb|Preferences for emigration of Kosovars after Germany<ref>{{cite journal|author=Ivļevs, King|title=Kosovo - winning its independence but losing its people?|date=September 2009|url=http://www.cepr.org/meets/wkcn/2/2405/papers/ivlevs_king_hamburg_tom.pdf|website=Cepr.org}}</ref>]]
[[emigration from Kosovo|Migration from Kosovo]] occurred in phases beginning from the second half of the 20th century. The [[Kosovo War]] (February 1998-June 1999) created a wave. On 19 May 2011, Kosovo established the Ministry of Diaspora. Kosovo also established the Kosovo Diaspora Agency (KDA) to support migrants. Migrants from [[Kosovo]] newly arriving in the EU, detected but not over an official border-crossing point, was around 21,000 in 2014 and 10,000 in 2015.<ref name="Frontex2015,p.19,22,24" /> At the same period detected illegal border crossings to the EU from Kosovo was 22,069 in 2014 and 23,793 in 2015.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Risk_Analysis/Risk_Analysis_for_2018.pdf|author=Frontex|title=Risk Analysis for 2018|year=2018|access-date=9 March 2020}}</ref>

In 2015 there was sudden surge, which Kosovo became helpless to stem.<ref name="Kosovo2015">{{cite news |title=Kosovo helpless to stem exodus of illegal migrants |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-kosovo-eu-immigration/kosovo-helpless-to-stem-exodus-of-illegal-migrants-idUSKBN0LA1XH20150206 |work=Reuters |date=6 February 2015 |language=en}}</ref> More than 30,000 caught in Hungary between September 2014 to February 2015, which was only 6,000 for the year 2013.<ref name="Kosovo2015" /> This was 7% of the country's population. Kosovo’s president urge residents to stay while his top ally said “gates must be shut” to economic immigrants to Europe.<ref name="Kosovo2015" />

==EU's management of the crisis==
===Political positions===

| quote = Europe needs to fulfil its humanitarian duty, helping those fleeing for their lives, and as a Christian-Democrat, I want to reiterate that is not Christian rights, but human rights that Europe invented. But we also need to better secure our external borders and make sure that asylum rules are used properly and not abused.
| source = —[[Manfred Weber]], leader of the [[European People's Party]] in the European Parliament.

}}
[[File:Praha, Václavské náměstí, říjnová demonstrace proti přijetí uprchlíků, Tomio Okamura.jpg|thumb|Czech politician [[Tomio Okamura]] speaks at the anti-immigration rally in [[Prague]], 17 October 2015]]
[[File:Salvini Centinaio Giorgetti.jpg|thumb|right|[[Matteo Salvini]] with League's delegation at the [[Quirinal Palace]] in April 2018]]
The [[European Commission]]er for Migration, Home Affairs and Citizenship, [[Dimitris Avramopoulos]], said that the European Commission "does not care about the political cost 'of its handling of the migration crisis" as re-election does not drive the commissions vision.<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/eu/11896827/Cost-of-migration-crisis-means-nothing-to-us-says-top-EU-official.html Cost of migration crisis means nothing to us, says top EU official]". ''The Daily Telegraph''. 28 September 2015.</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=EU migration chief: Forget the 'political cost'|url=http://www.politico.eu/article/migration-news-political-europe-cost/|work=Politico|date=25 September 2015}}</ref>

[[Angela Merkel]], German [[Chancellor of Germany|Chancellor]], used some of her strongest language on the migrant crisis and warned that freedom of travel and open borders among the 28 member states of the EU could be jeopardised if they did not agree on a shared response to this crisis.<ref name="StrainedOpenBorders" />

[[Nicolas Sarkozy]], president of [[The Republicans (France)|the Republicans]] and former French president, compared the EU migrant plan to "mending a burst pipe by spreading water round the house while leaving the leak untouched".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/nicolas-sarkozy/11686558/Nicolas-Sarkozy-compares-EU-migrant-plan-to-fixing-a-burst-water-pipe-with-water.html |title=Nicolas Sarkozy compares EU migrant plan to 'fixing a burst water pipe with water' |work=The Daily Telegraph |date=19 June 2015 |access-date=18 October 2015|last1=Samuel |first1=Henry }}</ref> Sarkozy criticised Merkel's decision to allow tens of thousands of people to enter Germany, saying that it would attract even greater numbers of people to Europe, of which a significant part would "inevitably" end up in France due to the EU's free movement policies and the French welfare state. He also demanded that the Schengen agreement on borderless travel should be replaced with a new agreement providing border checks for non-EU citizens.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.lefigaro.fr/politique/2015/09/09/01002-20150909ARTFIG00427-crise-des-migrants-le-plan-de-sarkozy.php |title=Crise des migrants : le plan de Sarkozy |trans-title=Migrant crisis: Sarkozy's plan|work=Le Figaro|language=fr|date=9 September 2015 }}</ref>

[[Italian Prime Minister]] and [[List of Secretaries of the Democratic Party (Italy)|Secretary]] of the Italian [[Democratic Party (Italy)|Democratic Party]] [[Matteo Renzi]] said the EU should forge a single European policy on asylum.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34106343 |title=Migrant crisis: Austria holds suspected people smugglers |work=BBC News |date=31 August 2015}}</ref> [[French Prime Minister]] [[Manuel Valls]] of the French [[Socialist Party (France)|Socialist Party]] stated, "There must be close cooperation between the European Commission and member states as well as candidate members."<ref>{{cite web |url=http://m.euronews.com/en/312599/ |title=French PM Valls urges EU solidarity amid unprecedented migrant crisis |publisher=euronews.com |date=31 August 2015 |access-date=1 September 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150901010323/http://m.euronews.com/en/312599/ |archive-date=1 September 2015 |url-status=dead |df=dmy-all }}</ref> [[Sergei Stanishev]], President of the [[Party of European Socialists]], stated:

{{Quote
 |quote= At this moment, more people in the world are displaced by conflict than at any time since the Second World War. ... Many die on the approach to Europe – in the Mediterranean – yet others perish on European soil. ... As social democrats the principle of solidarity is the glue that keeps our family together. ... We need a permanent European mechanism for fairly distributing asylum-seekers in European member states. ... War, poverty and the stark rise in inequality are global, not local problems. As long as we do not address these causes globally, we cannot deny people the right to look for a more hopeful future in a safer environment.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.pes.eu/en/news-events/news/detail/European-response-to-dire-refugee-crisis-urgently-needed|title=European response to dire refugee crisis urgently needed|work=Party of European Socialists|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref>}}

According to ''[[The Wall Street Journal]]'', the appeal of [[Eurosceptic]] politicians had increased.<ref name="Troianoski">{{cite news |last1=Troianovski |first1=Anton |title=Migration Crisis Pits EU's East Against West |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/migration-crisis-pits-eus-east-against-west-1439957453 |access-date=19 August 2015 |work=The Wall Street Journal |date=19 August 2015}}</ref>

[[Nigel Farage]], leader of the British anti-EU [[United Kingdom Independence Party]] and co-leader of the Eurosceptic [[Europe of Freedom and Direct Democracy]] group, blamed the EU "and Germany in particular" for giving "huge incentives for people to come to the European Union by whatever means" and said that this would make deaths more likely. He claimed that the EU's Schengen agreement on open borders had failed and that Islamists could exploit the situation and enter Europe in large numbers, saying that "one of the ISIL terrorist suspects who committed the first atrocity against holidaymakers in [[Tunisia]] [had] been seen getting off a boat onto Italian soil".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/nigel-farage/11844290/Thousands-of-Isil-fighters-could-use-migrant-crisis-to-flood-into-Europe-Nigel-Farage-warns.html |title=Video: Thousands of Isis fighters could use migrant crisis to 'flood' into Europe, Nigel Farage warns – Telegraph |date=4 September 2015 |work=The Daily Telegraph}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/nigel-farage/11836131/Nigel-Farage-EU-has-opened-doors-to-migration-exodus-of-biblical-proportions.html |title=Nigel Farage: EU has opened doors to migration exodus of biblical proportions |date=1 September 2015 |work=The Daily Telegraph|last1=Wilkinson |first1=Michael }}</ref> In 2013, Farage had called on the UK government to accept more Syrian refugees,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2013/dec/29/nigel-farage-syrian-refugees-uk |title=Nigel Farage calls on government to let Syrian refugees into UK |newspaper=The Guardian|date=29 December 2013 }}</ref> before clarifying that those refugees should be Christian due to the existence of nearer places of refuge for Muslims.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Mason|first1=Rowena|title=Nigel Farage rows back on call to grant asylum to Syrian refugees|url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2013/dec/30/nigel-farage-asylum-syrian-refugees-christians|access-date=20 September 2015|work=The Guardian|date=30 December 2013}}</ref> [[Marine Le Pen]], leader of the French far-right [[National Front (France)|National Front]] and co-president of the former [[Europe of Nations and Freedom]] (EMF) group, accused Germany of looking to hire "slaves" by opening its doors to large numbers of asylum seekers at a debate in Germany whether there should be exceptions to the recently introduced minimum wage law for refugees.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.welt.de/regionales/baden-wuerttemberg/article145573021/BWIHK-Praesident-will-Mindestlohn-fuer-Fluechtlinge-aufweichen.html |title=BWIHK-Präsident will Mindestlohn für Flüchtlinge aufweichen |work=Die Welt |language=de |trans-title=President wants to soften Minimum Wage Rules for Refugees}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.n-tv.de/wirtschaft/Landkreise-wollen-Mindestlohn-senken-article15853956.html |title=Ausnahmen für Asylbewerber – Landkreise wollen Mindestlohn senken (Exceptions for Asylum Seekers – Organization of Districts wants to lower Minimum Wage) (in German) |work=N-TV.de}}</ref> Le Pen also accused Germany of imposing its immigration policy on the rest of the EU unilaterally.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/09/06/us-europe-migrants-france-farright-idUSKCN0R60TF20150906 |title=French far-right leader says Germany seeking 'slaves' in migrants |work=Reuters (US)|date=6 September 2015 }}</ref> Her comments were reported by the German<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.tagesspiegel.de/politik/newsblog-zu-fluechtlingen-muenchen-stoesst-an-grenzen-seiner-aufnahmefaehigkeit/12282848.html |title=Newsblog zu Flüchtlingen (in German) |work=Der Tagesspiegel}}</ref> and Austrian press;<ref>{{cite web |url=http://diepresse.com/home/politik/aussenpolitik/4814935/Le-Pen_Deutschland-sieht-in-Fluchtlingen-Sklaven- |title=Le Pen: Deutschland sieht in Flüchtlingen "Sklaven" (in German) |work=Die Presse}}</ref> the online edition of ''[[Der Spiegel]]'' referred to them as "abstruse claims".<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.spiegel.de/politik/ausland/front-national-unterstellt-deutschland-interesse-an-arbeitssklaven-a-1051675.html |title=Front National unterstellt Deutschland Interesse an Arbeitssklaven |work=Der Spiegel|date=6 September 2015 }}</ref> The centre-right daily newspaper ''[[Die Welt]]'' wrote that she "exploit[ed] the refugee crisis for anti-German propaganda".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.welt.de/politik/ausland/article146112084/Berlin-will-mit-Fluechtlingen-Sklaven-rekrutieren.html |title=Berlin will mit Flüchtlingen "Sklaven rekrutieren" (in German) |newspaper=Die Welt|date=7 September 2015 }}</ref>

[[Geert Wilders]], the leader of the Dutch [[Party for Freedom]] and a member of the former EMF known for his [[criticism of Islam]], called the influx of people an "Islamic invasion" during a debate in the Dutch parliament and spoke of "masses of young men in their twenties with beards singing ''Allahu Akbar'' across Europe".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/09/10/us-europe-migrants-netherlands-idUSKCN0RA0WY20150910 |title=Wilders tells Dutch parliament refugee crisis is 'Islamic invasion' |work=Reuters (US)|date=10 September 2015 }}</ref> He also dismissed the idea that people arriving in Western Europe via the [[Balkans]] are genuine refugees, and statedː "Turkey, Greece, Macedonia, Serbia are safe countries. If you flee them then you are doing it for benefits and a house."<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.jpost.com/Middle-East/Wilders-tells-Dutch-parliament-refugee-crisis-is-Islamic-invasion-415828|title=Wilders tells Dutch parliament refugee crisis is 'Islamic invasion' |newspaper=Jerusalem Post}}</ref>

===Initial proposals===
After the migrant shipwreck on 19 April 2015, Italian Prime Minister Renzi held a telephone conversation with French President [[François Hollande]] and Maltese Prime Minister [[Joseph Muscat]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.lasiciliaweb.it/articolo/128414/esteri/renzi-chiama-hollande-salvini-attacca-tragedia-annunciata |title=Renzi chiama Hollande Salvini: "Tragedia annunciata" |language=it |author=La Sicilia Multimedia |publisher=lasiciliaweb.it |access-date=19 April 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150907010136/http://www.lasiciliaweb.it/articolo/128414/esteri/renzi-chiama-hollande-salvini-attacca-tragedia-annunciata |archive-date=7 September 2015 |url-status=dead }}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://m.ilmattino.it/primopiano/cronaca/strage_migranti_renzi_vertice_ministri_ue/notizie/1305206.shtml |title=Renzi: "Subito un vertice Ue, siamo pronti a bloccare la partenza dei barconi" |language=it |work=Il Mattino |access-date=19 April 2015}}</ref> They agreed to call for an emergency meeting of European interior ministers to address the problem of migrant deaths. Renzi condemned human trafficking as a "new slave trade"<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-32374027 |title=Italian PM Matteo Renzi condemns 'new slave trade' in Mediterranean |work=BBC News |access-date=19 April 2015}}</ref> while Prime Minister Muscat said the 19 April shipwreck was the "biggest human tragedy of the last few years". Hollande described smugglers as "terrorists" who put migrant lives at risk. [[Aydan Özoğuz]], the [[German government]]'s representative for migration, refugees, and integration, said that emergency rescue missions should be restored as more migrants were likely to arrive as the weather turned warmer. "It was an illusion to think that cutting off [[Operation Mare Nostrum|Mare Nostrum]] would prevent people from attempting this dangerous voyage across the Mediterranean", she said.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cbc.ca/news/world/migrants-ship-headed-for-italy-capsizes-north-of-libya-1.3039401 |title=Migrants' ship headed for Italy capsizes north of Libya |publisher=[[Canadian Broadcasting Corporation]] |date=19 April 2015}}</ref><ref name="BoatDisaster">{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/live/world-32372351 |title=Med migrant boat disaster |date=18 April 2015 |publisher=BBC}}</ref><ref name="EmergencyTalks" /> [[Federica Mogherini]], [[High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy|High Representative of the EU for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy]], called for collective EU action ahead at a meeting in Luxembourg on Monday 20 April.<ref name="EmergencyTalks" /><ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.yahoo.com/eu-states-back-action-protect-migrants-mediterranean-mogherini-114546548.html |title=Europe should back action to protect migrants in Mediterranean: Mogherini |publisher=Reuters/Yahoo |date=19 April 2015}}</ref>

In a press conference, Renzi confirmed that Italy had called an "extraordinary European council" meeting as soon as possible to discuss the tragedy;<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/prime-minister-matteo-renzi-defends-italys-response-migrants-drowning-mediterranean-1497254 |title=Prime Minister Matteo Renzi defends Italy's response to migrants drowning in the Mediterranean |newspaper=[[International Business Times UK]] |access-date=19 April 2015|date=19 April 2015 }}</ref> various European leaders agreed with this idea.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.antena3.com/noticias/mundo/naufraga-barco-700-inmigrantes-190-kilometros-lampedusa_2015041900016.html |title=Naufraga un pesquero con 700 inmigrantes a bordo cerca de la costa de Libia |publisher=Antena3.com |access-date=19 April 2015|date=19 April 2015 }}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.channelnewsasia.com/mobile/world/eu-s-tusk-considers/1794426.html |title=EU's Tusk considers special summit after migrants drown |publisher=[[Channel NewsAsia]] |access-date=19 April 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150427143419/http://www.channelnewsasia.com/mobile/world/eu-s-tusk-considers/1794426.html |archive-date=27 April 2015 }}</ref> Then-[[Prime Minister of the United Kingdom]] [[David Cameron]] tweeted on 20 April that he "supported" Renzi's "call for an emergency meeting of EU leaders to find a comprehensive solution" to the migrant crisis in the Mediterranean.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.ansa.it/english/news/politics/2015/04/20/med-faces-humanitarian-crisis-renzi_f7f22df2-27a1-496e-8f96-481bbcff8a20.html |title=Med faces humanitarian crisis, not just wreck, says Renzi |publisher=ANSA.it |access-date=20 April 2015|date=20 April 2015 }}</ref> He later confirmed that he would attend an emergency summit of European leaders on Thursday.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-32382962 |title=Mediterranean migrant deaths: PM calls for action after boat disaster |work=BBC News |access-date=20 April 2015 |date=20 April 2015}}</ref>

On 20 April 2015, the European Commission proposed a 10-point plan to tackle the crisis.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_IP-15-4813_en.htm |title=European Commission – PRESS RELEASES – Press release – Joint Foreign and Home Affairs Council: Ten point action plan on migration |publisher=Europa (web portal) |access-date=21 April 2015}}</ref>

In 2016 the European Commission began reforming the Common European Asylum System (CEAS) which was initially designed to created a unified asylum system for the EU. In an attempt to create measures for safe and managed paths for legal migration to Europe, the European Commission created five components that sought to satisfy the minimum standards for asylum.<ref name=":03">{{Cite news|last=Raithel|first=Silvia|date=2016-02-09|title=The Common European Asylum System: Its History, Content, and Shortcomings – The Michigan Journal of International Law|language=en-US|work=The Michigan Journal of International Law|url=http://www.mjilonline.org/the-common-european-asylum-system-its-history-content-and-shortcomings/|access-date=2017-11-30}}</ref>

On 13 July 2016, the European Commission introduced the proposals to finalise the CEAS' reform. The reform sought to create a just policy for asylum seekers while providing a new system that was simple and shortened. Ultimately, the reform proposal attempted to create a system that could handle normal and impacted times of migratory pressure.<ref name=":22">{{cite web|url=http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_IP-16-2433_en.htm|title=European Commission – PRESS RELEASES – Press release – Completing the reform of the Common European Asylum System: towards an efficient, fair and humane asylum policy|website=europa.eu|language=en|access-date=2017-11-30}}</ref>

===Securing borders===
{{Further|Operation Triton|EU Navfor Med}}
{{See also|Operation Mare Nostrum|Operation Triton}}
[[File:Migrants in Hungary 2015 Aug 018.jpg|thumb|Migrants crossing illegally into Hungary underneath the unfinished [[Hungary–Serbia border fence]], 25 August 2015]]
[[File:RIMG0257.JPG|thumb|In June 2015, [[Royal Navy]] ship {{HMS|Enterprise|H88|6}} replaced {{HMS|Bulwark|L15|6}} in the [[EU Navfor Med|mission]] to rescue migrants crossing the Mediterranean from Libya to Italy<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/uknews/defence/11962766/HMS-Richmond-and-HMS-Enterprise-rescue-541-migrants-from-the-Med.html HMS Richmond and HMS Enterprise rescue 541 migrants from the Med]". ''[[The Daily Telegraph]]''. 29 October 2015.</ref>]]
[[File:Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg|thumb|[[Hungarian border barrier]] ]]
The [[2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck]] involved "more than 360" deaths and led the Italian government to establish [[Operation Mare Nostrum]], a large-scale naval operation that involved [[search and rescue]], with migrants being brought aboard a naval [[amphibious assault ship]].<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.marina.difesa.it/EN/operations/Pagine/MareNostrum.aspx |title=Mare Nostrum Operation |publisher=Marina Militare}}</ref> The Italian government ended the operation in 2014 amid an upsurge in the number of sea arrivals in Italy from Libya, citing the costs were too large for one EU state alone to manage; Frontex assumed the main responsibility for search and rescue operations under the name [[Operation Triton]].<ref name="European Commission">{{cite web |url=http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_MEMO-14-566_en.htm |title=EC MEMO, Brussels, 7 October 2014, Frontex Joint Operation 'Triton' – Concerted efforts to manage migration in the Central Mediterranean |publisher=European Union, European Commission |access-date=15 April 2015}}</ref> The Italian government had requested additional funds from the EU to continue the operation but member states did not offer the requested support.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://news.vice.com/article/italy-is-about-to-shut-down-the-sea-rescue-operation-that-saved-more-than-90000-migrants-this-year |title=Italy Is About to Shut Down the Sea Rescue Operation That Saved More Than 90,000 Migrants This Year |work=[[Vice News]] |access-date=19 April 2015}}</ref> The UK government cited fears that the operation was acting as "an unintended 'pull factor', encouraging more migrants to attempt the dangerous sea crossing and thereby leading to more tragic and unnecessary deaths".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.theguardian.com/politics/2014/oct/27/uk-mediterranean-migrant-rescue-plan |title=UK axes support for Mediterranean migrant rescue operation |newspaper=[[The Guardian]] |access-date=20 April 2015}}</ref> The operation consisted of two surveillance aircraft and three ships, with seven teams of staff who gathered intelligence and conducted screening/identification processing. Its monthly budget was estimated at €2.9&nbsp;million.<ref name="European Commission" /> In the first half of 2015, Greece overtook Italy in the number of arrivals and became the starting point of a flow of refugees and migrants moving through [[Balkan]] countries to [[Northern Europe]]an countries, mainly Germany and Sweden in the summer of 2015 .

''The Guardian'' and [[Reuters]] noted that doubling the size of [[Operation Triton]] would still leave the mission with fewer resources than Operation Mare Nostrum which had a budget thrice as large, four times the number of aircraft,<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/20/two-more-mediterranean-migrant-boats-issue-distress-calls-as-eu-ministers-meet |title=Two more migrant boats issue distress calls in Mediterranean |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=21 April 2015|date=20 April 2015 |last1=Kirchgaessner |first1=Stephanie |last2=Traynor |first2=Ian |last3=Kingsley |first3=Patrick }}</ref> and a wider mandate to conduct search and rescue operations across the Mediterranean Sea.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/20/us-europe-migrants-idUSKBN0NA07020150420 |title=Migrants' bodies brought ashore as EU proposes doubling rescue effort |work=Reuters |access-date=21 April 2015 |date=20 April 2015}}</ref>

On 23 April 2015, a five-hour emergency [[Summit (meeting)|summit]] was held and EU heads of state agreed to triple the budget of Operation Triton to €120&nbsp;million for 2015–2016.<ref name="auto4">{{cite web |url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/eu-triple-funding-operation-triton-tackle-mediterranean-migrant-crisis-1498100 |title=EU to triple funding for 'Operation Triton' to tackle Mediterranean migrant crisis |work=IBT |access-date=24 April 2015|date=24 April 2015 }}</ref> EU leaders claimed that this would allow for the same operational capabilities as Operation Mare Nostrum had had in 2013–2014. As part of the agreement the United Kingdom agreed to send the {{HMS|Bulwark|L15|6}}, two naval patrol boats, and three helicopters to join the Operation.<ref name="auto4" /> On 5 May 2015 Irish Minister of Defence [[Simon Coveney]] announced that the [[LÉ Eithne (P31)|LÉ Eithne]] would participate in the response to the crisis.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Pollak |first1=Sorcha |title=LÉ Eithne to be dispatched in migrant search on May 8th |url=https://www.irishtimes.com/news/world/europe/lé-eithne-to-be-dispatched-in-migrant-search-on-may-8th-1.2200382 |work=The Irish Times |date=5 May 2015}}</ref> Amnesty International immediately criticised the EU's response as "a face-saving not a life-saving operation" and said that "failure to extend Triton's operational area will fatally undermine today's commitment".<ref name="auto3">{{cite web |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2015/04/face-saving-not-a-lifesaving-operation/ |title=Europe's response: "Face-saving not a life-saving operation" |publisher=Amnesty International |access-date=21 October 2016}}</ref>

On 18 May 2015, the European Union launched a new operation based in Rome, named [[EU Navfor Med]], under the command of the Italian Admiral [[Enrico Credendino]],<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.eeas.europa.eu/csdp/missions-and-operations/eunavfor-med/pdf/cv_credendino_en.pdf|title=Operation SOPHIA IT Navy Biography (pdf)}}</ref> to undertake systematic efforts to identify, capture and dispose of vessels used by migrant smugglers.<ref name="Kanter 2015">{{cite news | last=Kanter | first=James | title=E.U. Agrees to Naval Intervention on Migrant Smugglers | website=The New York Times | date=18 May 2015 | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/05/19/world/europe/european-union-human-trafficking-military.html | access-date=28 November 2015}}</ref> The first phase of the operation launched on 22 June 2015 and involved naval surveillance detecting smugglers' boats and monitoring smuggling patterns from Libya towards Italy and Malta. The second phase, called "Operation Sophia", started in October and was aimed at disrupting the smugglers' journeys by boarding, searching, seizing, and diverting migrant vessels in international waters. The operation used six EU warships.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: EU to begin seizing smugglers' boats|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34461503|work=BBC News|date=7 October 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Europe gears up to seize smugglers|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/blogs-eu-34454392|work=BBC News|date=7 October 2015}}</ref> As of April 2016, the operation rescued more than 13,000 migrants at sea and arrested 68 alleged smugglers.<ref name="auto11" />

The EU sought to increase the scope of EU Navfor Med so that a third phase of the operation would include patrols inside Libyan waters in order to capture and dispose of vessels used by smugglers.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/eu-approves-military-action-against-mediterranean-people-smugglers-083904759.html|title=EU backs military action against Med people smugglers|date=14 September 2015|work=Yahoo News|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://euobserver.com/justice/130258|title=EU to expand Mediterranean anti-smuggler force|work=EUobserver|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> Land operations on Libya to destroy vessels used by smugglers had been proposed, but commentators note that such an operation would need a UN or Libyan permit.

Eleni Rozali reported in 2016 that the Greek islands (Kos, Leros, Chios, for example) served as main entry points into Europe for Syrian refugees.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://muep.mau.se/bitstream/handle/2043/21323/EMR%20DP2016%20-%20v2.pdf?sequence=2|title=Host Communities and the Refugee Crisis A Case Study of Kos Island, Greece|last=Rozali|first=Eleni|date=2016|access-date=February 4, 2018}}</ref>

The entry routes through the Western Balkan experienced the highest intensity of border restrictions in the 2015 EU migrant crisis, according to ''The New York Times''<ref name="BorderCrackdowns">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/09/15/world/europe/migrant-borders-europe.html|title=Closing the Back Door to Europe|author1=Sarah Almukhtar |author2=Josh Keller |author3=Derek Watkins |newspaper=The New York Times|date=16 October 2015|access-date=28 November 2015}}</ref> and other sources, and are as follows:
