===Carriers' responsibility===
Article 26 of the [[Schengen Convention]]<ref>[http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=CELEX:42000A0922%2802%29:en:HTML Official Journal L 239, 22 September 2000]. ([[s:Convention implementing the Schengen Agreement|The Schengen acquis – Convention implementing the Schengen Agreement]])</ref> states that carriers which transport people who are refused into the Schengen area shall pay for both penalties and the return of the refused people.<ref>{{cite web|title=Carrieri sanctions |url=http://www.ecre.org/topics/areas-of-work/access-to-europe/7-carrier-sanctions.html |publisher=[[European Council on Refugees and Exiles]] |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160310200237/http://www.ecre.org/topics/areas-of-work/access-to-europe/7-carrier-sanctions.html |archive-date=10 March 2016 }}</ref> Further clauses on this topic are found in EU directive 2001/51/EC.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=OJ:L:2001:187:0045:0046:EN:PDF|title=COUNCIL DIRECTIVE 2001/51/EC supplementing the provisions of Article 26 of the Convention implementing the Schengen Agreement}}</ref> This prevented migrants without a visa from being allowed on aircraft, boats, or trains entering the Schengen Area, and caused them to resort to [[People smuggling|migrant smugglers]].<ref>[http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/refugee-crisis-smugglers-offer-discount-refugees-willing-cross-bad-weather-1526441 Refugee crisis: Smugglers offer 'Bad weather discount' to migrants] (International Business Times, 25 October 2015)</ref> Humanitarian visas are generally not given to refugees who want to apply for asylum.<ref>[https://www.hrw.org/report/2015/11/16/europes-refugee-crisis/agenda-action Europe's Refugee Crisis, An Agenda for Action] (Human Rights Watch, 16 November 2015)</ref>

The laws on [[migrant smuggling]] forbid helping migrants pass any national border if the migrants do not have permission to enter. This has caused many airlines to check for visas and refuse passage to migrants without visas, including through international flights inside the Schengen Area. After being refused air passage, many migrants attempted to travel overland to their destination country. According to a study carried out for the European Parliament, "penalties for carriers, who assume some of the control duties of the European police services, either block asylum-seekers far from Europe's borders or force them to pay more and take greater risks to travel illegally".<ref>{{cite web|title=Analysis of the external dimension of the EU's asylum and immigration policies|url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/meetdocs/2004_2009/documents/dt/619/619330/619330en.pdf|publisher=European Parliament}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.actnownews.com/refugee-crisis/|title=Way to Future of the Refugee crisis|work=Act Now News|access-date=29 April 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151114085750/http://actnownews.com/refugee-crisis/|archive-date=14 November 2015|df=dmy-all}}</ref>

It has been argued that the official policy (at least in some countries like Sweden) of free right to apply for asylum, is counteracted by the Carriers' responsibility, forcing refugees to use an illegal  and dangerous route by using criminal smugglers, to exercise a right that many say should not be denied.<ref>[https://blog.petrieflom.law.harvard.edu/2015/09/12/why-do-refugees-risk-the-deadly-boat-crossing-to-europe-its-the-law/ Why Do Refugees Risk the Deadly Boat Crossing to Europe? It’s the Law]</ref> A suggestion of humanitarian visas (refugees would be able to get an entry permission before travelling if have reason for asylum) has been turned down because of the number of people who would arrive.

On the paper the Carriers' responsibility law does not prevent the free right to asylum, because the penalty on airlines is not given if the person is actually granted asylum. But the airlines can't know who will be given asylum or not and do therefore block everyone without right to enter.

The [[International Organization for Migration]] (IOM) and the UN refugee agency, [[United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees|UNHCR]] urged to disembark the more than four hundred rescued migrants and refugees rescued in the Central Mediterranean Sea on board three vessels. The IOM also emphasized on the need of a regional agreement for the safe disembarkation of migrants and refugees amid [[COVID-19 pandemic]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/08/1071332|title= UN agencies call for urgent disembarkation of hundreds rescued in the Mediterranean|access-date=29 August 2020|website=UN News}}</ref>

===Migration policies===
====Migration Partnership Framework====
[[File:FAMILY PHOTO 2016-09-20 (29519477920).jpg|thumb|3rd Prague Process Ministerial Conference]]

The Tampere Program started in 1999 outlines the EU's policy on migration and presents a certain openness towards freedom, security, and justice.<ref name=":25">{{Cite journal|last=European Parliament|date=2018|title=Migration and Asylum: A Challenge for Europe|journal=Asylum Policy}}</ref> It focuses on two issuesː the development of a common asylum system and the enhancement of external border controls.<ref name=":25" /> The externalization of borders with Turkey is essentially the transfer of border controls and management to foreign countries, which are in close proximity to EU countries.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://privacyinternational.org/news-analysis/3224/new-report-underlines-eus-strategy-war-migration-border-externalisation|title=New Report Underlines the EU's Strategy in the War on Migration: Border Externalisation|website=Privacy International|language=en-GB|access-date=2019-12-09}}</ref> The EU's decision to externalize its borders puts significant pressure on non-EU countries to cooperate with EU political forces.<ref name=":19">{{Cite journal|last=Bennett|first=M.B|date=2018|title=The Refugee Crisis and the EU's Externalisation of Integrated Border Management to Libya and Turkey|journal=EU Diplomacy Papers}}</ref>

The Migration Partnership Framework introduced in 2016 implements greater resettlement of migrants and alternative legal routes for migration.<ref name=":25" /> Its goals align with the EU's efforts throughout the refugee crisis to deflect responsibility and legal obligations away from EU member states and onto transit and origin countries.<ref name=":25" /><ref name=":19" /> By directing migrant flows to third countries,{{clarify|date=December 2019}} policies place responsibilities on third-world countries{{clarify|date=December 2019}}.<ref name=":19" /> States with insufficient resources are legally mandated to ensure the protection of migrants' rights, including the right to asylum.<ref name=":19" /> Destination states under border externalization strategies are responsible for rights violated outside their own territory.<ref name=":19" /> Fundamental rights of migrants can be impacted while externalizing borders;<ref name=":19" /> for example, child migrants are recognized to have special status under international law, though they are vulnerable to trafficking and other crimes while in transit.

====Africa Agreement: Emergency Trust Fund====
The [[Valletta Summit on Migration]] between European and African leaders was held in [[Valletta]], [[Malta]], on 11 and 12 November 2015 to discuss the migrant crisis. The summit resulted in the EU creating an Emergency Trust Fund to promote development in Africa, in return for African countries to help out in the crisis.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migration summit: "We are in a race against time to save Schengen" – Tusk|url=http://www.timesofmalta.com/articles/view/20151112/local/watch-valletta-summit-concluding-press-conference.591885|access-date=12 November 2015|work=[[Times of Malta]]|date=12 November 2015}}</ref>

====Angela Merkel====
At a time of diplomatic tensions with the [[Third Orbán Government|Hungarian government]], Merkel publicly pledged that Germany would offer temporary residency to refugees. Combined with television footage of cheering Germans welcoming refugees and migrants arriving in Munich,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/05/refugee-crisis-warm-welcome-for-people-bussed-from-budapest|title=Cheering German crowds greet refugees after long trek from Budapest to Munich|author=Emma Graham-Harrison|newspaper=The Guardian|access-date=24 October 2015|date=5 September 2015}}</ref> large numbers of migrants were persuaded to move from Turkey up the Western Balkan route.<ref name="EightSlyReasons">{{cite news |last=Sly |first=Liz |author-link=Liz Sly |title=8 reasons Europe's refugee crisis is happening now|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/worldviews/wp/2015/09/18/8-reasons-why-europes-refugee-crisis-is-happening-now/|access-date=18 September 2015|work=[[The Washington Post]]|date=18 September 2015}}</ref>

On 25 August 2015 ''The Guardian'' reported "Germany's federal agency for migration and refugees made it public, that 'The #Dublin procedure for Syrian citizens is at this point in time effectively no longer being adhered to'". During a press conference, Germany's interior minister, [[Thomas de Maizière]], confirmed that the suspension of the Dublin agreement was "not as such a legally binding act", but more of a "guideline for management practice".<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/aug/25/it-took-on-a-life-of-its-own-how-rogue-tweet-led-syrians-to-germany|title='It took on a life of its own': how one rogue tweet led Syrians to Germany|author1=Philip Oltermann |author2=Patrick Kingsley|newspaper=The Guardian|access-date=25 August 2016|date=25 August 2016}}</ref> Around 24 August 2015, Merkel decided to stop following the rule under the [[Dublin Regulation]] such that migrants "can apply for asylum only in the first EU member state they enter";<ref name="DropsRules" /> the Regulation actually holds that the migrant should apply for asylum in the first EU country where they were formally registered).{{citation needed|date=March 2020}} Germany ordered its officers to process asylum applications from Syrians if they had come through other EU countries.<ref name="DropsRules">{{cite news|last1=Holehouse|first1=Matthew|last2=Huggler|first2=Justin|last3=Vogt|first3=Andrea|date=24 August 2015|title=Germany drops EU rules to allow in Syrian refugees|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/11821822/Germany-drops-EU-rules-to-allow-in-Syrian-refugees.html|work=The Telegraph|access-date=16 June 2017}}</ref> On 4 September 2015, Merkel decided that Germany would admit the thousands of refugees who were stranded in [[Hungary]]<ref name="NRC6Sep2015">{{in lang|nl}} [https://www.nrc.nl/nieuws/2015/09/06/1061000-a1413393 'Wenen verwacht vandaag weer 10.000 migranten – paus doet oproep' (Vienna today expects another 10,000 migrants – Pope issues an appeal)]. ''[[NRC Handelsblad]]'', 6 September 2015. Retrieved 15 July 2019.</ref>  and sent to the [[Austria]]n border under excessively hot conditions by Hungarian prime minister [[Viktor Orbán|Orban]].<ref name="politico15Sep">[https://www.politico.eu/article/merkel-changed-her-mind-migration-crisis-eu-schengen-border-control/ 'Why Merkel changed her mind']. ''Politico'', 15 September 2015. Retrieved 18 July 2019.</ref><ref name="Trouw3Sep16">{{in lang|nl}} [https://www.trouw.nl/nieuws/duitse-wilkommenskultur-is-ver-in-het-geheugen-weggezakt~bd698aa1/ 'Duitse 'Wilkommenskultur' is ver in het geheugen weggezakt' (German welcoming culture has sunk deep in our memory)]. ''[[Trouw]]'', 3 September 2016. Retrieved 15 July 2019.</ref> With that decision, she reportedly aimed to prevent disturbances at the German borders.<ref name="Trouw3Sep16" /> Tens of thousands of refugees traveled from Hungary via [[Vienna]] into Germany in the days following 4 September 2015.<ref name="NRC6Sep2015" /><ref name="politico15Sep" />

Analyst Will Hutton for the British newspaper ''The Guardian'' praised Merkel's decisions on migration policies on 30 August 2015: "Angela Merkel's humane stance on migration is a lesson to us all… The German leader has stood up to be counted. Europe should rally to her side… She wants to keep Germany and Europe open, to welcome legitimate asylum seekers in common humanity, while doing her very best to stop abuse and keep the movement to manageable proportions. Which demands a European-wide response (…)".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2015/aug/30/immigration-asylumseekers-refugees-migrants-angela-merkel|title=Angela Merkel's humane stance on immigration is a lesson to us all|author=Will Hutton|work=The Guardian|access-date=19 September 2015|date=30 August 2015}}</ref>

====Turkey Agreement: Locating migrants to safe country====
[[File:Sea arrivals to Greece and Italy, 2015.png|thumb|upright=2|Mediterranean sea arrivals to Greece and Italy from January 2015 to September 2016, according to UNHCR data<ref name="UNHCR2015">{{cite web|title=Arrivals to Greece, Italy and Spain. January–December 2015|url=http://reliefweb.int/sites/reliefweb.int/files/resources/MonthlyTrendsofNationalities-ArrivalstoGreeceItalyandSpain-31December2015.pdf|publisher=UNHCR}}</ref>]]

The EU proposed a plan to the Turkish government in which Turkey would take back every refugee who entered Greece (and thereby the EU) illegally; in return, the EU would accept one person into the EU who is registered as a Syrian refugee in Turkey for every Syrian sent back from Greece.<ref name="a">{{cite web|url=http://www.psca.eu/uploads/MleCMS/Issue%20VII_complete.pdf|title=The EU's response to the so-called refugee "crisis"}}</ref> 12 EU countries have national lists of [[Safe country of origin|safe countries of origin]]. The [[European Commission]] proposed one, common EU list designated as "safe" across all [[Future enlargement of the European Union#Recognised candidates|EU candidate countries]] ([[Albania]], [[North Macedonia]], [[Montenegro]], [[Serbia]] and [[Turkey]]), plus [[Future enlargement of the European Union#Potential candidates that have not yet applied for EU membership|potential EU candidates]] [[Bosnia and Herzegovina]] and [[Kosovo]].<ref name="safe">{{cite web|url=http://ec.europa.eu/dgs/home-affairs/what-we-do/policies/european-agenda-migration/background-information/docs/2_eu_safe_countries_of_origin_en.pdf |title=An Eu 'Safe Countries of Origin' List |access-date=18 October 2015}}</ref> The list would allow for faster returns to those countries, even though asylum applications from nationals of those countries would continue to be assessed on an individual, case-by-case basis.<ref name="safe" /> International Law generated during the Geneva Convention states that a country is considered "safe" when there is a democratic system in a country and there is generally no persecution, no torture, no threat of violence, and no armed conflict.<ref name=":0">{{Cite web|url=https://ec.europa.eu/home-affairs/sites/homeaffairs/files/what-we-do/policies/european-agenda-migration/background-information/docs/2_eu_safe_countries_of_origin_en.pdf|title=AN EU 'SAFE COUNTRIES OF ORIGIN' LIST.|website=European Commission|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20171009225639/https://ec.europa.eu/home-affairs/sites/homeaffairs/files/what-we-do/policies/european-agenda-migration/background-information/docs/2_eu_safe_countries_of_origin_en.pdf|archive-date=2017-10-09}}</ref>

In November, Turkish president [[Recep Tayyip Erdoğan]] reportedly threatened to send the millions of refugees in Turkey to EU member states if it was left to shoulder the burden alone.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/feb/12/turkish-president-threatens-to-send-millions-of-syrian-refugees-to-eu|title=Turkish president threatens to send millions of Syrian refugees to EU|newspaper=The Guardian|date=12 February 2016|author=Agence France-Presse}}</ref> On 12 November 2015, at the end of the Valletta Summit in Malta, EU officials announced an agreement to offer Turkey €3 billion over two years to manage more than 2 million refugees from Syria who had sought refuge there in return for curbing migration through Turkey into the EU.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/13/world/europe/european-union-refugees-migrants-sweden.html?ribbon-ad-idx=5&rref=world/europe&module=Ribbon&version=origin&region=Header&action=click&contentCollection=Europe&pgtype=article|title=Europe Nears Accord With Turkey to Stem Tide of Refugees|author=James Kanter|newspaper=The New York Times|date=12 November 2015|access-date=14 November 2015}}</ref> The €3 billion fund for Turkey was approved by the EU in February 2016.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: EU approves 3 bn-euro fund for Turkey|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35486655|work=BBC News|date=3 February 2016}}</ref>

In January 2016, the Netherlands proposed a plan that the EU take in 250,000 refugees a year from Turkey in return for Turkey closure of the Aegean sea route to Greece, which Turkey rejected.<ref>{{cite news|title=Turkey dismisses EU plan to resettle refugees in return for sealing sea route|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/feb/10/turkey-dismisses-eu-plan-to-resettle-refugees-in-return-for-sealing-sea-route|work=The Guardian|date=10 February 2016}}</ref> On 7 March 2016, the EU met with Turkey for another summit in [[Brussels]] to negotiate further solutions of the crisis. The original plan was to declare the Western Balkan route closed, but it was met with criticism from Merkel.<ref>{{cite web|title=Feilschen um Formulierungen|url=https://www.tagesschau.de/ausland/eu-gipfel-fluechtlinge-113.html|publisher=[[Tagesschau (Germany)|Tagesschau]]|access-date=7 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307210627/http://www.tagesschau.de/ausland/eu-gipfel-fluechtlinge-113.html|archive-date=7 March 2016|language=de|date=7 March 2016}}</ref> Turkey countered the offer by demanding a further €3 billion in order to help them supply aid to the 2.7 million refugees in Turkey. In addition, the Turkish government asked for their citizens to be allowed to travel freely into the Schengen area starting at the end of June 2016, as well as expedited talks of a possible [[accession of Turkey to the European Union]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Harte Verhandlungen über türkische Vorschläge|url=https://www.tagesschau.de/ausland/eu-gipfel-fluechtlinge-121.html|publisher=[[Tagesschau (Germany)|Tagesschau]]|access-date=7 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307211020/http://www.tagesschau.de/ausland/eu-gipfel-fluechtlinge-121.html|archive-date=7 March 2016|language=de|date=7 March 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|last1=Rankin|first1=Jennifer|title=Resettling Syrians, aid and visa changes on table at EU-Turkey migration summit|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/mar/07/eu-offers-another-3bn-to-turkey-at-emergency-migration-summit|newspaper=[[The Guardian]]|access-date=7 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307210858/http://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/mar/07/eu-offers-another-3bn-to-turkey-at-emergency-migration-summit|archive-date=7 March 2016|date=7 March 2016}}</ref> The plan to send migrants back to Turkey was criticized on 8 March 2016 by the United Nations, which warned that it could be illegal to send the migrants back to Turkey in exchange for financial and political rewards.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-idUSKCN0WA1D4|title=U.N., rights groups say EU-Turkey migrant deal may be illegal|author1=Stephanie Nebehay |author2=Gabriela Baczynska |date=8 March 2016|work=Reuters|access-date=8 March 2016}}</ref>

On 20 March 2016, an agreement between the [[European Union]] and [[Turkey]] was enacted to discourage migrants from making the dangerous sea journey from Turkey to [[Greece]]. Under its terms, migrants arriving in Greece would be sent back to Turkey if they did not apply for asylum or their claim was rejected, whilst the EU would send around 2,300 experts, including security and migration officials and translators, to Greece in order to help implement the deal.<ref name="bbc.com">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35854413|title=Migrant crisis: EU-Turkey deal comes into effect|newspaper=BBC News|access-date=21 March 2016|date=20 March 2016}}</ref>

It was also agreed upon that any irregular migrants who crossed into Greece from Turkey after 20 March 2016 would be sent back to Turkey based on an individual case-by-case evaluation. Any Syrian returned to Turkey would be replaced by a Syrian resettled from Turkey to the EU; they would preferably be the individuals who did not try to enter the EU illegally in the past. Allowed migrants would not exceed a maximum of 72,000 people.<ref name="a" /> Turkish nationals would have access to the Schengen passport-free zone by June 2016 but would exclude non-Schengen countries such as the UK. The talks about Turkey's accession to the EU as a member began in July 2016 and $3.3 billion in aid was to be delivered to Turkey.<ref name="bbc.com" /><ref>{{cite web|title=EU-Turkey Agreement: Questions and Answers|url=http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_MEMO-16-963_en.htm|publisher=European Commission}}</ref> The talks were suspended in November 2016 after the [[2016 Turkish coup d'état attempt]].<ref>{{cite news|url= https://www.reuters.com/article/us-turkey-eu-idUSKCN1QA0MJ|title=Turkey condemns European parliament committee call to suspend...|date=21 February 2019|work=Reuters|access-date=21 February 2019}}</ref> A similar threat was raised as the [[European Parliament]] voted to suspend EU membership talks with Turkey in November 2016: "if you go any further," [[Recep Tayyip Erdoğan|Erdoğan]] declared, "these border gates will be opened. Neither me nor my people will be affected by these dry threats."<ref>{{Cite journal|last1=Adamson|first1=Fiona B|last2=Tsourapas|first2=Gerasimos|date=2019-05-01|title=Migration Diplomacy in World Politics|journal=International Studies Perspectives|language=en|volume=20|issue=2|pages=113–128|doi=10.1093/isp/eky015|issn=1528-3577|url=http://pure-oai.bham.ac.uk/ws/files/57727314/Adamson_Tsourapas_2018_Migration_diplomacy_in_world_politics_International_Studies_Perspectives.pdf}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/president-erdogan-turkey-eu-membership-migrants-refugees-europe-warning-a7438316.html|title=Turkey warns Europe it will open the floodgates to more migrants|date=2016-11-25|website=The Independent|language=en|access-date=2019-06-09}}</ref>

Migrants from Greece to Turkey were to be given medical checks, registered, fingerprinted,  and bused to "reception and removal" centres.<ref name="BBC April 8">[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35993767 Migrant crisis: Deportations resume from Greece to Turkey] [[BBC News]]. Published on 8 April 2016,</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.publictenders.net/tender/374386|title=TR-Ankara: IPA – construction of reception and removal centres|work=publictenders.net|access-date=29 April 2016}}</ref> before being deported to their home countries.<ref name="BBC April 8" /> UNHCR director [[Vincent Cochetel]] claimed in August 2016 that parts of the deal were already suspended because of the post-coup absence of Turkish police at the Greek detention centres to oversee deportations.<ref>{{cite web |title=Greece on edge, as Turkish coup prompts surge in new arrivals |url=https://euobserver.com/beyond-brussels/134868|publisher=euobserver|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Turkish police withdrawal from Greece stalls EU migration pact|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/aug/31/turkish-police-withdrawal-greece-stalls-eu-migration-pact-unhcr|publisher=theguardian|language=en|newspaper=The Guardian|date=31 August 2016}}</ref>

The UNHCR said it was not a party to the EU-Turkey deal and would not be involved in returns or detention.<ref>{{cite news|title=UNHCR redefines role in Greece as EU-Turkey deal comes into effect|url=http://www.unhcr.org/56f10d049.html|work=UNHCR|date=22 March 2016}}</ref> Like the UNHCR, four aid agencies ([[Médecins Sans Frontières]], the [[International Rescue Committee]], the [[Norwegian Refugee Council]] and [[Save the Children]]) said they would not help to implement the EU-Turkey deal because blanket expulsion of refugees contravened international law.<ref>{{cite news|title=Refugee crisis: key aid agencies refuse any role in 'mass expulsion'|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/mar/23/refugee-crisis-aid-agencies-unhcr-refuse-role-mass-expulsion-greece-turkey|work=The Guardian|date=23 March 2016}}</ref>

[[Amnesty International]] said that the agreement between EU and Turkey was "madness", and that 18 March 2016 was "a dark day for Refugee Convention, Europe and humanity". Turkish prime minister [[Ahmet Davutoglu]] said that Turkey and EU had the same challenges, the same future, and the same destiny. Donald Tusk said that the migrants in Greece would not be sent back to dangerous areas.<ref>[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/turkey/12197969/Refugee-crisis-Turkey-and-EU-agree-deal-to-send-migrants-back-to-Turkey-from-Greece.html Migrants given 24-hour deadline to reach Europe after Turkey and EU agree 'historic' deal] M. Holehouse, R. Akkoc and N. Squires, The Daily Telegraph, 18 March 2016</ref>

On 17 March 2017, Turkish [[Ministry of the Interior (Turkey)|interior minister]] [[Süleyman Soylu]] threatened to send 15,000 refugees to the [[European Union]] every month, while Turkish foreign minister [[Mevlut Cavusoglu]] also threatened to [[EU-Turkey deal|cancel the deal]].<ref>{{cite news |url= http://www.nu.nl/buitenland/4549128/turkije-dreigt-met-sturen-migranten-europese-unie.html |title= Turkije dreigt met sturen migranten naar Europese Unie |language= nl |work= [[NU.nl]] |year= 2017 |access-date= 17 March 2017}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/turkey-threatens-to-send-europe-15000-refugees-a-month/28375772.html|title=Turkey Threatens To Send Europe 15,000 Refugees A Month|website=RadioFreeEurope/RadioLiberty}}</ref>

[[File:Refugees waiting at Greek-Turkish Border.jpg|thumb|Refugees protesting at the Pazarkule border gate, the Greek-Turkish border]]

On 9 October 2019, the [[2019 Turkish offensive into north-eastern Syria|Turkish offensive into north-eastern Syria]] began. Within the first week and a half 130,000 people were displaced. On 10 October it was reported that President Erdoğan had threatened to send "millions" of Syrian refugees to Europe in response to criticism of his military offensive into Kurdish-controlled northern Syria.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Turkey's Erdogan threatens to send 'millions' of refugees to Europe if EU calls Syria offensive 'invasion' |date=2019-10-10|website=The Telegraph|language=en|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2019/10/10/turkeys-erdogan-threatens-send-millions-refugees-europe-eu-calls/}}</ref> On 27 February 2020, a senior Turkish official said Turkish police, coast guard and border security officials had received orders to no longer stop refugees' land and sea crossings to Europe.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-syria-security/turkey-with-more-dead-troops-wont-stop-syrian-refugees-reaching-europe-official-idUSKCN20L0GQ|title=Turkey, with more dead troops, won't stop Syrian refugees reaching Europe: official|work=Reuters|date=27 February 2020|access-date=28 February 2020}}</ref>

====Changes in Schengen & Dublin====
{{Main|Dublin Regulation|Schengen Area}}
[[File:Map of the Schengen Area.svg|thumb|{{legend|#003399|The [[Schengen Area]]}}{{legend|#ffa500|European Union members legally obliged to join Schengen at a future date}}{{legend|#27a4bb|Countries with open borders}}]]
In the [[Schengen Agreement]] of 14 June 1985, 26 European countries (22 of the 28 [[European Union]] member states, plus four [[European Free Trade Association]] states) joined together to form an area where border checks were restricted to and enforced on the [[Schengen Area#Regulation of external borders|external Schengen borders]] and countries with external borders. Countries may reinstate internal border controls for a maximum of two months for "public policy or national security" reasons.<ref>{{cite news|title=Schengen: Controversial EU free movement deal explained|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-13194723|work=BBC News|date=14 September 2015}}</ref>

The Dublin Regulation determines the EU member state responsible to examine an [[right of asylum|asylum]] application and prevent asylum applicants in the EU from "[[asylum shopping]]"{{Em dash}}where applicants send their applications for asylum to numerous EU member states to get the best "deal" instead of just having "safety countries"{{Em dash}}<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.foxnews.com/world/2016/07/13/eu-floats-new-asylum-system-seeks-to-stop-asylum-shopping.html|title=EU floats new asylum system, seeks to stop 'asylum shopping'|date=13 July 2016}}</ref> or "asylum orbiting"{{Em dash}}where no member state takes responsibility for an asylum seeker. By default (when no family reasons or humanitarian grounds are present), the first member state that an asylum seeker entered and in which they have been fingerprinted is responsible. If the asylum seeker moves to another member state afterwards, they can be transferred back to the member state they first entered. This rule led many to criticise the Dublin Regulation for placing too much responsibility for asylum seekers on member states on the EU's external borders (like Italy, Greece, Croatia and Hungary), instead of devising a burden-sharing system among EU states.<ref>{{cite web|title=EU legal framework on asylum and irregular immigration 'on arrival'|url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/etudes/BRIE/2015/551333/EPRS_BRI%282015%29551333_EN.pdf|publisher=European Parliamentary Research Service}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Asylum in the EU: Facts and Figures|url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/etudes/BRIE/2015/551332/EPRS_BRI%282015%29551332_EN.pdf|publisher=European Parliamentary Research Service}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Dublin regulation leaves asylum seekers with their fingers burnt|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2011/oct/07/dublin-regulation-european-asylum-seekers|work=The Guardian|date=7 October 2011}}</ref>

In June 2016, the Commission to the European Parliament and Council addressed "inherent weaknesses" in the Common European Asylum System and proposed reforms for the Dublin Regulation.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://ec.europa.eu/home-affairs/sites/homeaffairs/files/what-we-do/policies/european-agenda-migration/proposal-implementation-package/docs/20160406/towards_a_reform_of_the_common_european_asylum_system_and_enhancing_legal_avenues_to_europe_-_20160406_en.pdf|title=Communication from the Commission to the European Parliament and the Council|date=4 June 2016}}</ref> Under the initial Dublin Regulation, responsibility was concentrated on border states that received a large influx of asylum seekers. A briefing by the European Parliament explained that the Dublin Agreement was only designed to assign responsibility and not to effectively share responsibility.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/RegData/etudes/BRIE/2016/586639/EPRS_BRI(2016)586639_EN.pdf|title=EU Legislation in Process: Reform of the Dublin System}}</ref> The reforms would attempt to create a burden-sharing system through several mechanisms. The proposal would introduce a "centralised automated system" to record the number of asylum applications across the EU, with "national interfaces" within each of the Member States.<ref name=":02">{{cite web|url=http://www.statewatch.org/news/2017/feb/eprs-mgration-compendium.pdf|title=Addressing Migration in the European Union: Selected publications by the European Parliamentary Research Service}}</ref> It would also present a "reference key" based on a Member State's GDP and population size to determine its absorption capacity.<ref name=":02" /> When the absorption capacity in a Member State exceeded 150 percent of its reference share, a "fairness mechanism" would distribute the excess number of asylum seekers across less congested Member States.<ref name=":02" /> If a Member State chooses not to accept the asylum seekers, it would contribute €250,000 per application instead as a "solidarity contribution".<ref name=":02" /> The reforms have been discussed in European Parliament since its proposal in 2016, and was included in a meeting on "The Third Reform of the Common European Asylum System – Up for the Challenge" in 2017.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.europarl.europa.eu/legislative-train/theme-towards-a-new-policy-on-migration/file-revision-of-the-dublin-regulation|title=Legislative train schedule {{!}} European Parliament|website=European Parliament|access-date=2017-11-30}}</ref>

As most asylum seekers try to reach Germany or Sweden through other EU member states, many of which form the borderless [[Schengen area]] where internal border controls are abolished, enforcing the Dublin Regulation became increasingly difficult in the late summer of 2015, with some countries allowing asylum seekers to transit through their territories, renouncing the right to return them, or reinstating border controls within the Schengen Area to prevent them from entering. In July 2017, the [[European Court of Justice]] upheld the Dublin Regulation, despite the high influx of 2015, and gave EU member states the right to deport migrants to the first country of entry to the EU.<ref name="telegraph26July2017">{{cite news|title=EU court rejects 'open-door' policy and upholds right of member states to deport refugees|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2017/07/26/eu-court-rejects-open-door-policy-upholds-right-member-states/|newspaper=The Daily Telegraph|date=26 July 2017}}</ref>

Countries responded in different ways:
*Hungary became overburdened by asylum applications and on 23 June 2015 it stopped receiving returned applicants who had crossed the borders to other EU countries and been detained there.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/06/23/uk-europe-migrants-austria-hungary-idUKKBN0P31ZB20150623 |title=Defying EU, Hungary suspends rules on asylum seekers |work=Reuters |access-date=9 March 2015}}</ref> Later in the year, migrants in southern Hungary started a hunger strike in protest against the closure of the green border with Serbia.<ref>[https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2015/sep/15/refugee-crisis-hungary-launches-border-crackdown-live-updates Refugee crisis: Hungary declares state of emergency at Serbian border – live updates], ''The Guardian''</ref> Hungarian police used tear gas and a water cannon on the protesters after they threw stones and concrete at the riot police.<ref>{{cite news|first=Krisztina|last=Than |title=Hungarian police fire water cannon and tear gas at migrants|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/09/16/us-europe-migrants-hungary-protests-idUSKCN0RG1TA20150916 |work=Reuters |date=16 September 2015|access-date=16 September 2015}}</ref>
* On 24 August 2015, in accordance with article 17 of the Dublin III Regulations, Germany suspended the general procedure in regards to Syrian refugees and to process their asylum applications directly itself.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/germany-opens-its-gates-berlin-says-all-syrian-asylumseekers-are-welcome-to-remain-as-britain-is-urged-to-make-a-similar-statement-10470062.html |title=Germany opens its gates: Berlin says all Syrian asylum-seekers are welcome to remain, as Britain is urged to make a 'similar statement' |work=The Independent |access-date=9 March 2015}}</ref> The change in Germany asylum policy incited large numbers of migrants to move towards Germany, especially after Merkel stated that "there is no legal limit to refugee numbers".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/11861966/Germany-to-reinstate-border-controls-as-country-struggles-with-influx-of-refugees-live.html |title=Germany 'to reinstate border controls' as country struggles with influx of refugees – live |work=The Independent |access-date=12 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.kvoa.com/story/29997280/the-latest-merkel-says-no-legal-limit-to-refugee-numbers |title=The Latest: Merkel says no legal limit to refugee numberse |publisher=KVOA |access-date=12 September 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150923182953/http://www.kvoa.com/story/29997280/the-latest-merkel-says-no-legal-limit-to-refugee-numbers |archive-date=23 September 2015 }}</ref> Meanwhile, Austria allowed unimpeded travel of migrants from Hungary to Germany through its own territory. Germany then established temporary border controls along its border with Austria to "limit the current inflows" and "return to orderly procedures when people enter the country" according to de Maizière.<ref>[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34239674 Migrant crisis: Germany to start temporary border controls]. BBC News</ref> The Czech Republic reacted by increasing its police presence along its border with Austria in anticipation of the mass of migrants in Austria trying to reach Germany through the Czech Republic. Czech police conducted random searches of vehicles and trains within Czech territory and patrolled the green border in cars and helicopters. Some Czech police officers were stationed within Austria in order to give advance warning if large numbers of migrants moved towards the Austrian–Czech borders.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.novinky.cz/domaci/380564-policiste-chystaji-zalohy-pro-dohled-na-hranici.html |title=Policisté chystají zálohy pro dohled na hranici |publisher=novinky.cz |access-date=14 September 2015}}</ref> On 9 and 10 September, Denmark closed rail lines with Germany after hundreds of migrants refused to be registered in the country as asylum seekers and insisted on continuing their travel to Sweden.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.businessinsider.com/afp-denmark-shuts-rail-link-as-europe-wrangles-over-refugees-2015-9 |title=Denmark has shut down its rail link as refugees surge into Scandinavia |work=Business Insider |access-date=14 September 2015}}</ref>
* On 2 September 2015, the Czech Republic defied the Dublin Regulation and offered Syrian refugees the option to have their application processed in the Czech Republic or to continue their journey elsewhere. Immigrants of other nationalities would normally face detention and return under the Dublin Regulation if they tried to reach Germany through the Czech Republic.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.praguepost.com/eu-news/49584-change-in-czech-refugee-policy |title=Change in Czech refugee policy |work=The Prague Post |access-date=9 March 2015}}</ref> On 7 September, Austria began phasing out special measures that had allowed tens of thousands of migrants to cross its territory and reinstated the Dublin Regulation.<ref>[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34169726 Migrant crisis: Austria 'to end emergency migrant measures']. [[BBC News]]. 7 September 2015.</ref>
* On 14 September, Austria established border controls along its border with Hungary and deployed police officers and the army there.<ref>[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34242123 Migrant crisis: Austria to deploy troops]. [[BBC News]].</ref> Hungary also deployed army personnel along its border with Serbia<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34205849|title=Migrant crisis: Hungarian army stages border protection exercise|work=BBC News|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> and announced that in those who illegally enter Hungary would be arrested and face imprisonment<ref>[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34229335 Europe migrant crisis: Hungary PM calls for €3bn Syria aid package]. [[BBC News]]. 12 September 2015.</ref> before closing it.<ref name="Holehouse 2015">{{cite web | last=Holehouse | first=Matthew | title=Refugee crisis: Croatia seals border crossings with Serbia | website=The Daily Telegraph | date=18 September 2015 | url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/hungary/11873012/Refugee-crisis-Hungary-declares-victory-in-border-strategy-as-migrants-head-to-Croatia-instead.html | access-date=22 December 2015}}</ref> After Austrian chancellor Werner Faymann's made remarks likening Hungary's treatment of refugees to Nazi policies,<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2015-09-13/austria-likens-hungary-asylum-seeker-policy-to-nazi-era/6771418 |title=European migrant crisis: Hungary hits back at Austria's criticism of 'Nazi-like' asylum seeker policies |publisher=ABC.au |access-date=14 September 2015}}</ref> Hungary started transporting refugees by bus directly to the border with Austria, where they were offloaded and tried to cross to Austria on foot.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://bbj.hu/politics/report-refugees-bused-from-roszke-to-austrian-border_103990 |title=Report: Refugees bused from Röszke to Austrian border |work=Budapest Business Journal |access-date=14 September 2015}}</ref>

The table above summarizes the 1.7 million asylum applicants in 2015 costed €18 billion in maintenance costs in 2016, with the total 2015 and 2016 asylum caseload costing €27.3 billion (27.296 in € Mil.) in 2016. Sweden is observed to bear the heaviest cost.<ref name="cost2016" />

====Quota system (relocation)====
The escalation in April 2015 of [[List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea|shipwrecks of migrant boats in the Mediterranean]] led EU leaders to reconsider their policies on border control and migrant processing.<ref name="EmergencyTalks">{{cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/04/19/us-europe-migrants-idUSKBN0NA07020150419|title=EU leaders call for emergency talks after 700 migrants drown off Libya|work=Reuters|date=19 April 2015}}</ref> On 20 April the European Commission proposed a 10-point plan that included the [[European Asylum Support Office]] deploying teams in Italy and Greece to asylum applications together.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_IP-15-4813_en.htm|title=European Commission – PRESS RELEASES – Press release – Joint Foreign and Home Affairs Council: Ten point action plan on migration|publisher=Europa (web portal)|access-date=21 April 2015}}</ref> [[Angela Merkel|Merkel]] proposed a new system of quotas to distribute non-EU asylum seekers across the EU member states.<ref>Justin Huggler, Andrew Marszal, [https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/11561430/Angela-Merkel-calls-for-new-rules-for-distributing-asylum-seekers-in-Europe.html Angela Merkel calls for new rules for distributing asylum seekers in Europe], ''[[The Daily Telegraph]]'' dated 24 April 2015</ref>

In September 2015, as thousands of migrants started to move from [[Budapest]] to [[Vienna]], Germany, Italy, and France demanded asylum-seekers be shared more evenly between EU states. Commission President [[Jean-Claude Juncker]] proposed to distribute 160,000 asylum seekers among EU states under a new migrant quota system. Luxembourg Foreign Minister [[Jean Asselborn]] called for the establishment of a European Refugee Agency, which would have the power to investigate whether every EU member state is applying the same standards for granting asylum to migrants. Orbán criticised the European Commission, warning that "tens of millions" of migrants could come to Europe, whom Asselborn declared to be "ashamed" of.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/nicola-sturgeon/11841808/David-Cameron-insists-he-cares-about-refugees-amid-criticism-from-Tories.html |title=David Cameron insists he 'cares' about refugees amid criticism from Tories |date=4 September 2015 |work=The Daily Telegraph}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.wort.lu/en/politics/zdf-german-tv-interview-jean-asselborn-ashamed-of-hungary-pm-orban-55e968910c88b46a8ce5f66a |work=Luxemburger Wort |title=Jean Asselborn 'ashamed' of Hungary PM Orban}}</ref> German Foreign Minister [[Frank-Walter Steinmeier]] said that EU members reluctant to accept compulsory migrant quotas may have to be outvoted: "if there is no other way, then we should seriously consider to use the instrument of a qualified majority".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/11873936/Eastern-European-countries-may-be-forced-accept-quotas-for-migrants.html |title=Eastern European countries may be forced accept quotas for migrants |date=18 September 2015 |work=[[The Daily Telegraph]]}}</ref>

[[File:2015-09-22 EU JHA Council majority vote to relocate 120,000 refugees.svg|thumb|right|National governments' position in the European Union Justice and Home Affairs Council majority vote to relocate 120,000 refugees:
{{legend|#8cd19d|Yes}}
{{legend|#ff9000|[[Opt-outs in the European Union|Opt-out]]}}
{{legend|#5cacc4|Abstention}}
{{legend|#fa3d3f|No}}
{{legend|#D6D6D6|Non-EU state}}]]
Leaders of the [[Visegrád Group]] (Czech Republic, Hungary, Poland, Slovakia) declared in a September meeting in Prague that they will not accept any compulsory long-term quota on redistribution of immigrants.<ref>Ian Traynor. [https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/05/migration-crisis-europe-leaders-blame-brussels-hungary-germany Refugee crisis: east and west split as leaders resent Germany for waiving rules]. ''[[The Guardian]]''. 5 September 2015.</ref> Czech Government's Secretary for European Affairs [[Tomáš Prouza]] commented that "if two or three thousand people who do not want to be here are forced into the Czech Republic, it is fair to assume that they will leave anyway. The quotas are unfair to the refugees, we can't just move them here and there like a cattle." According to the Czech interior minister [[Milan Chovanec]], from 2 September 2015, Czech Republic was offering asylum to every Syrian caught by the police notwithstanding the Dublin Regulation: out of about 1,300 apprehended until 9 September, only 60 decided to apply for asylum in the Czech Republic, with the rest of them continuing to Germany or elsewhere.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.novinky.cz/domaci/380081-nemuzeme-s-uprchliky-soupat-jako-s-dobytkem-odmitla-vlada-znovu-kvoty.html |title=Nemůžeme s uprchlíky šoupat jako s dobytkem, odmítla vláda znovu kvóty |date=9 September 2015 |publisher=Novinky.cz}}</ref>

Czech President [[Miloš Zeman]] said that [[Ukraine|Ukrainian]] refugees fleeing the [[War in Donbass]] should be also included in migrant quotas.<ref>{{cite news |title=Ukrainian refugees should be among voluntarily accepted – Zeman |url=http://www.ceskenoviny.cz/zpravy/ukrainian-refugees-should-be-among-voluntarily-accepted-zeman/1259473 |publisher=[[Czech News Agency|ČTK]] |date=17 September 2015}}</ref> In November 2015, the Czech Republic started a program of medical evacuations of 400 selected Syrian refugees from Jordan. Under the program, severely sick children were selected for treatment in the best Czech medical facilities, with their families getting asylum, airlift, and a paid flat in the Czech Republic after stating their clear intent to stay in the country. However, from the first three families that had been transported to Prague, one immediately fled to Germany. Czech Prime Minister [[Bohuslav Sobotka]] said that this signals that quota system will not work either.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://zpravy.idnes.cz/syrsti-azylanti-odesli-z-ceska-do-nemecka-f16-/domaci.aspx?c=A151106_160518_domaci_jj |title= Malí Syřané se měli léčit v Motole, rodina obratem odjela do Německa [Little Syrians were supposed to get treatment in Motol Hospital, a family immediately left to Germany] |date=9 November 2015 |work=Mladá fronta DNES}}</ref>

On 7 September 2015, France announced that it would accept 24,000 asylum-seekers over two years; Britain announced that it would take in up to 20,000 refugees, primarily vulnerable children and orphans from camps in Jordan, Lebanon and Turkey; and Germany pledged US$6.7 billion to deal with the migrant crisis.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/08/world/europe/europe-migrant-crisis.html|title=A Steady Flow Staggers into Europe, Outpacing Pledges of Shelter |author1=Rick Lyman |author2=Steven Erlange |author3=Aurelien Breeden |newspaper=The New York Times |date=7 September 2015 |access-date=7 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=UK to accept 20,000 refugees from Syria by 2020 |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-34171148 |access-date=8 September 2015 |publisher=BBC |date=7 September 2007}}</ref> However, both Austria and Germany also warned that they would not be able to keep up with the current pace of the influx and that it would need to slow down first.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://www.cnn.com/2015/09/07/europe/europe-migrant-crisis/index.html |title=Migrant crisis: More troubles in Hungary as Austria, Germany near tipping point |author1=Holly Yan |author2=Arwa Damon |publisher=CNN |date=7 September 2015 |access-date=7 September 2015}}</ref>

On 22 September 2015, European Union interior ministers meeting in the [[Justice and Home Affairs Council]] approved a plan to relocate 120,000 asylum seekers over two years from the frontline states [[Italy]], [[Greece]] and [[Hungary]] to all other EU countries (except Denmark, Ireland and the United Kingdom which have [[Opt-outs in the European Union|opted out]]). The relocation plan applies to asylum seekers "in clear need of international protection" (those with a recognition rate higher than 75 percent, i.e., [[Syria]]ns, [[Eritrea]]ns and [[Iraq]]is) – 15,600 from Italy, 50,400 from Greece and 54,000 from Hungary – who will be distributed among EU states on the basis of quotas taking into account the size of the economy and population of each state, as well as the average number of asylum applications. The decision was made by majority vote, with the [[Czech Republic]], [[Hungary]], [[Romania]] and [[Slovakia]] voting against and [[Finland]] abstaining. Since Hungary voted against the relocation plan, its 54,000 asylum seekers would not be relocated.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Why EU deal on refugees is difficult|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34324096|work=BBC News|date=25 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: EU ministers approve disputed quota plan|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34329825|work=BBC News|date=22 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Justice and Home Affairs Council, 22/09/2015|url=http://www.consilium.europa.eu/en/meetings/jha/2015/09/22/|publisher=Council of the European Union}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/23/world/europe/european-union-ministers-migrants-refugees.html|title=European Union Ministers Approve Plan to Distribute Refugees|author=James Kanter|newspaper=The New York Times|date=22 September 2015|access-date=22 September 2015}}</ref> Czech Interior Minister tweeted after the vote: "Common sense lost today."<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/11883024/Europe-ministers-agree-relocation-of-120000-refugees-by-large-majority.html EU quota plan forced through against eastern European states' wishes]". ''The Daily Telegraph''. 23 September 2015.</ref> Slovak Prime Minister [[Robert Fico]] threatened legal action over EU's mandatory migrant quotas at [[European Court of Justice]] in Luxembourg.<ref>"[https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/23/eu-summit-brussels-divisive-deal-refugee-quotas EU braces for turbulent summit after divisive deal on refugee quotas]". ''The Guardian''. 23 September 2015.</ref> On 9 October, the first 20 Eritrean asylum seekers were relocated by plane from Italy to Sweden,<ref>{{cite news|title=Eritrean refugees flown from Italy to Sweden in first EU quota relocation|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/oct/09/eritrean-refugees-italy-sweden-eu-quota-relocation|work=The Guardian|date=9 October 2015}}</ref> and were [[fingerprinting|fingerprinted]] in Italy.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/10/10/world/europe/italy-sends-eritreans-to-sweden-as-eu-migrant-relocations-begin.html?ribbon-ad-idx=8&rref=world&module=Ribbon&version=origin&region=Header&action=click&contentCollection=World&pgtype=article|title=Italy Sends Eritreans to Sweden as E.U. Migrant Relocations Begin|author=Elisabetta Povoledo|newspaper=The New York Times|date=9 October 2015|access-date=10 October 2015}}</ref>

On 25 October 2015, the leaders of Greece and other states along Western Balkan routes to wealthier nations of Europe, including Germany, agreed to set up holding camps for 100,000 asylum seekers, a move which Merkel supported.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/10/26/world/europe/merkel-and-east-european-leaders-discuss-migrant-crisis-in-brussels.html?ref=world|title=European Leaders Look Again for a Unified Response to Migrant Crisis|author=Andrew Higgins|newspaper=The New York Times|date=25 October 2015|access-date=26 October 2015}}</ref>

On 12 November it was reported that Frontex had been maintaining combined asylum seeker and deportation hotspots in Lesbos, Greece, since October.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://deutsche-wirtschafts-nachrichten.de/2015/12/12/hotspots-fuer-fluechtlinge-das-haessliche-gesicht-deutschlands-und-der-eu/|title=Hotspots für Flüchtlinge: Das hässliche Gesicht Deutschlands und der EU|date=12 December 2015|work=– DEUTSCHE WIRTSCHAFTS NACHRICHTEN}}</ref>

On 15 December 2015 the EU proposed taking over the border and coastal security operations at major migrant entry pressure points via its Frontex operation.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/12/16/world/europe/eu-borders-migrant-crisis.html|title=E.U. Pushes to Take Over Border Security at Migrant Pressure Points|author=James Kanter|newspaper=The New York Times|date=15 December 2015|access-date=15 December 2015}}</ref>

By September 2016 the quota system proposed by EU was abandoned after staunch resistance by [[Visegrád Group]] countries.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://euobserver.com/migration/135576|title=EU buries migration dispute for now|website=EUobserver}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.euractiv.com/section/justice-home-affairs/news/schulz-admits-mandatory-relocation-of-refugees-has-failed/|title=Schulz admits mandatory relocation of refugees has failed|first=Georgi|last=Gotev|date=16 September 2016}}</ref>

By 9 June 2017, 22,504 people were resettled through the quota system, with over 2000 of them being resettled in May alone.<ref>{{cite web |title=RELOCATION AND RESETTLEMENT 13 JUNE 2017|date=13 June 2017|url=https://ec.europa.eu/home-affairs/sites/homeaffairs/files/what-we-do/policies/european-agenda-migration/20170613_factsheet_relocation_and_resettlement_en.pdf |access-date=26 August 2017|publisher=Euriopean Commission}}</ref> All relevant countries participated in the relocation scheme except Austria, Denmark, Czech Republic, Poland, and Hungary.<ref>{{cite web|title=Relocation and Resettlement – State of Play |publisher=European Commission|date=8 February 2017|url=https://ec.europa.eu/home-affairs/sites/homeaffairs/files/what-we-do/policies/european-agenda-migration/20170208_factsheet_on_relocation_and_resettlement_en.pdf|access-date=26 August 2017}}</ref> The European commission had consequentially launched sanctions against the Czech Republic, Poland, and Hungary.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.euractiv.com/section/justice-home-affairs/news/eu-opens-sanctions-procedure-against-hungary-poland-and-czech-republic-over-refugees/|title=EU opens sanctions procedure against Hungary, Poland and Czech Republic over refugees|website=EURACTIV.com|date=13 June 2017}}</ref>

====Crime by immigrants====
{{see also|Immigration and crime}}
{{Undue weight|date=July 2020|to=The section does not adequately outline the number of terrorist attacks and terrorist plots where asylum seekers were involved during the crisis. Instead of outlining recorded incidents, it misinforms the reader by calling the security threat a "narrative" in the lead paragraph.}}
Although it was stated that terrorists were exploiting refugee sea and land routes to enter Europe, acts of terrorism in Europe between 2014 and 2020, led many governments to mistakenly take a tough stance on refugees.  For example, in the wake of [[November 2015 Paris attacks]],{{Clarify|reason=Why are the Paris attacks relevant to this article? They are, but explain why.|date=July 2020}} Poland's European affairs minister-designate [[Konrad Szymański]] stated that he did not see it possible to enact the EU refugee relocation scheme,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/poland-plans-to-backtrack-on-migrant-commitment-following-attacks-in-paris-a6734521.html |title=Poland says it cannot accept migrants under EU quotas, following attacks in Paris |newspaper=[[The Independent]]|date=14 November 2015|access-date=14 November 2015}}</ref> unless there were security guarantees for accepting refugees, implying that refugees were responsible for the Paris attacks, when they were not.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/11/14/uk-france-shooting-poland-reaction-idUKKCN0T30P920151114|title=Poland says cannot take migrants under EU quotas without guarantees after Paris attacks|work=Reuters|date=14 November 2015|access-date=14 November 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |last1=Henley |first1=John |title=Paris attacks: EU in emergency talks on border crackdown |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/nov/20/paris-attacks-france-launches-un-push-for-unified-declaration-of-war-on-isis |access-date=27 October 2020 |agency=The Guardian |date=20 November 2015}}</ref>

During 2015, [[Foreign fighters in the Syrian and Iraqi Civil Wars|foreign fighters]] who had joined the [[Islamic state]] travelled with the migration flow back to Europe. In the January 2016-April 2017 period, four asylum seekers were involved in terrorist incidents, but none who had been granted refugee status. Most of the terrorist attacks in Europe in the period were carried out by citizens of European countries.<ref>{{Cite web|title=European citizens, not refugees, behind most terrorist attacks in Europe {{!}} DIIS|url=https://www.diis.dk/en/research/european-citizens-not-refugees-behind-most-terrorist-attacks-in-europe|access-date=2020-07-27|website=www.diis.dk|language=en}}</ref>

The [[November 2015 Paris attacks]] prompted European officials—particularly German officials—to re-evaluate their stance on EU policy toward migrants.<ref name="ParisAttacksMigrants1">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/16/world/europe/paris-attacks-shift-europes-migrant-focus-to-security.html?rref=collection%2Fnewseventcollection%2Fattacks-in-paris&action=click&contentCollection=europe&region=rank&module=package&version=highlights&contentPlacement=1&pgtype=collection|title=Paris Attacks Shift Europe's Migrant Focus to Security|author1=Rick Lyman |author2=Alison Smale |newspaper=The New York Times|date=15 November 2015|access-date=16 November 2015}}</ref><ref name="ParisAttacksMigrants2">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/11/14/world/europe/ap-eu-germany-migrants-rising-tensions.html|title=Paris Attacks Provoke Fresh Migrant Fears in Europe|author=Eldar Emric, Demetri Nellas, and the Associated Press|newspaper=The New York Times|date=14 November 2015|access-date=16 November 2015}}</ref>{{Clarify|reason=|date=July 2020}} Many German officials believed a higher level of scrutiny was needed, and criticised Merkel's stance, but the German Vice-Chancellor [[Sigmar Gabriel]] defended her position and pointed out that a lot of migrants were fleeing terrorism.<ref name="ParisAttacksMigrants2" />

In January 2016, 18 of 31 men suspected of [[New Year's Eve sexual assaults in Germany|violent assaults on women]] in [[Cologne]] on [[New Year's Eve]] were identified as asylum seekers, prompting calls by German officials to deport convicted criminals who may be seeking asylum;<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/01/09/world/europe/cologne-new-years-eve-attacks.html|title=18 Asylum Seekers Are Tied to Attacks on Women in Germany|author=Alison Smale|newspaper=The New York Times|date=8 January 2016|access-date=8 January 2016}}</ref> these sexual attacks brought about a new wave of anti-immigrant protests across Europe.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/01/14/world/europe/a-climate-of-fear-widens-divisions-in-europes-migrant-crisis.html|title=Sexual Attacks Widen Divisions in European Migrant Crisis|author=Jim Yardley|newspaper=The New York Times|date=13 January 2016|access-date=14 January 2016}}</ref> Merkel said "[[wir schaffen das]]" during the violence and crime by German immigrants, including the [[2016 Munich shooting]], the [[2016 Ansbach bombing]], and the [[Würzburg train attack]].<ref>{{cite news|title=After rampages, Merkel says again: Wir schaffen das|url=https://www.thelocal.de/20160728/merkel-says-again-wir-schaffen-das|agency=AFP|publisher=The Local|date=26 July 2016}}</ref>

In 2016, the Italian daily newspaper ''[[La Stampa]]'' reported that officials from [[Europol]] conducted an investigation into the trafficking of fake documents for [[ISIL]]. They identified fake [[Syrian]] passports in the [[refugee camp]]s in [[Greece]] that were for supposed members of ISIL to avoid Greek security and make their way to other parts of Europe. The chief of Europol also said that a new task force of 200 counter-terrorism officers would be deployed to the Greek islands alongside Greek border guards in order to help Greece stop a "strategic" level campaign by ISIL to infiltrate terrorists into Europe.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.lastampa.it/2016/08/21/italia/in-europa-la-fabbrica-della-cittadinanza-cos-funziona-il-business-dei-passaporti-comprati-e0dWQ28J4sGXYEcJ0jWLOI/pagina.html|title=In Europa la fabbrica della cittadinanza: così funziona il business dei passaporti comprati|last=Scarcella|first=Roberto|date=2016-08-21|website=LaStampa.it|language=IT|access-date=2019-06-29}}</ref>

In October 2016 Danish immigration minister [[Inger Støjberg]] reported 50 cases of suspected radicalised asylum seekers at asylum centres. The reports ranged from adult [[Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant|Islamic State]] sympathisers celebrating terror attacks to violent children who dress up as IS fighters decapitating teddy bears. Støjberg expressed her frustration at asylum seekers ostensibly fleeing war yet simultaneously supporting violence. Asylum centres that detected radicalisation routinely reported their findings to police. The 50 incidents were reported between 17 November 2015 and 14 September 2016.<ref name="tv2_dk_22okt2016a">{{cite news|title=IS-videoer, terrorjubel og halshugget bamse: 50 mistanker om radikalisering på asylcentre sendt til Udlændingestyrelsen|url=http://nyheder.tv2.dk/politik/2016-10-22-stoejberg-om-radikalisering-paa-asylcentre-der-er-alvorlige-sager-iblandt|access-date=23 October 2016|publisher=[[TV 2 (Denmark)]]|date=22 October 2016}}</ref><ref name="tv2_dk_22okt2016b">{{cite news|title=Støjberg om radikalisering på asylcentre: Der er alvorlige sager iblandt|url=http://nyheder.tv2.dk/politik/2016-10-22-stoejberg-om-radikalisering-paa-asylcentre-der-er-alvorlige-sager-iblandt|access-date=23 October 2016|publisher=[[TV2 (Denmark)]]|date=22 October 2016}}</ref>

In February 2017, British newspaper ''[[The Guardian]]'' reported that ISIL was paying the smugglers fees of up to $2,000 [[USD]] to recruit people from refugee camps in Jordan and in a desperate attempt to radicalize children for the group. The reports by counter-extremism [[think tank]] [[Quilliam (think tank)|Quilliam]] indicated that an estimated 88,300 unaccompanied children—who are reported as missing—were at risk of radicalization by ISIL.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/feb/05/isis-recruitment-drive-child-refugees|title=Isis paying smugglers' fees in recruitment drive among child refugees|last=Townsend|first=Mark|date=2017-02-05|work=The Guardian|access-date=2019-03-07|language=en-GB|issn=0029-7712}}</ref>

====Crime against immigrants====
{{see also|Opposition to immigration|Immigration and crime}}
There can be instances of exploitation at the hands of enforcement officials, citizens of the host country, instances of human rights violations, child labor, mental and physical trauma/torture, violence-related trauma, and [[Sexual exploitation and abuse in humanitarian response|sexual exploitation]], especially of children, have been documented.<ref>{{cite encyclopedia |last=Aggrawal |first=A. |title=Refugee Medicine |year=2005 |veditors=Payne-James JJ, Byard RW, Corey TS, Henderson C |encyclopedia=Encyclopedia of Forensic and Legal Medicine |publisher=Elsevier Academic Press |location=London |volume=3|pages=514–525}}</ref>

In October, a [[2015 German refugee attack plot|plot by neo-Nazis]] to attack a refugee center with explosives, knives, a baseball bat, and a gun was foiled by German police. Nazi magazines and memorabilia from the Third Reich, flags emblazoned with banned swastikas were found. According to the prosecutor the goal was "to establish fear and terror among asylum-seekers". The accused claimed to be either the members of Die Rechte, or anti-Islam group Pegida (Nügida).<ref>{{cite web|url=https://uk.news.yahoo.com/germany-police-foil-neo-nazi-073146377.html#ioeGHQv|title=Germany: Police foil Neo-Nazi terror attack on refugee shelter}}</ref>

In November 2016, the [[Euro-Med HRM|Euro-Mediterranean Human Rights Monitor]] issued a report in regards to the humanitarian situation of migrants into [[Greece]]. It hosted 16,209 migrants on its island and 33,650 migrants on the mainland, most of whom were women and children. Because of the lack of water, medical care and security protection witnessed by the Euro- Med monitor team- especially with the arrival of winter, they were at risk of serious health deterioration. 1,500 refugees were moved into other places since their camps were deluged with snow, but relocation of the refugees always came too late after they lived without electricity and heating devices for too long. It showed that there was a lack of access to legal services and protection for the refugees and migrants in the camps; there was no trust between the residents and the protection offices. In addition, migrants were subject to regular xenophobic attacks, fascist violence, forced strip searches at the hands of residents and police, and detention. Women living in the Athens settlements and the [[Vasilika refugee camp|Vasilika]], [[Softex]] and [[Diavata]] camps felt worried about their children as they may be subjected to sexual abuse, trafficking and drug use. As a result, some of the refugees and migrants committed suicide, burned property and protested. The report clarified the difficulties the refugees face when entering into Greece; more than 16,000 people were trapped while awaiting deportation on the Greek islands of [[Lesbos]], [[Chios]], [[Samos]], [[Leros]] and [[Kos]], which is twice the capacity of the five islands.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://euromedmonitor.org/en/article/1703/Asylum-seekers-attempt-suicide-daily-as-they-face-desperate-circumstances-in-Greece|title=Asylum seekers attempt suicide daily as they face desperate circumstances in Greece|last=Monitor|first=Euro-Med|newspaper=Euro-Mediterranean|language=en|access-date=29 January 2017}}</ref>

In August 2017 dozens of Afghan asylum seekers demonstrated in a square in Stockholm against their pending deportations. They were attacked by a group of 15–16 men who threw fireworks at them. Three protesters were injured and one was taken to hospital. No one was arrested.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.gp.se/nyheter/sverige/strejkande-ensamkommande-attackerade-1.4515731|title=Strejkande ensamkommande attackerade|work=Göteborgs-Posten|access-date=10 August 2017|language=sv}}</ref>

====Support systems by local communities and NGOs====
There are a number of support systems that aid the integration of refugees and asylum seekers in their host country. [[United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees]], working with partners, is providing a broad range of support and assistance in Europe for refugees and asylum-seekers. These efforts include humanitarian and cash assistance, provision of accommodation and support to improve reception conditions, prevention and response to sexual and gender-based violence, protection monitoring and interventions, engaging with refugee communities to enhance their participation and including their voice in their voice in the response, identification and support to persons with specific needs, including separated and unaccompanied children, and referral to appropriate services.<ref name="UNHCR2">{{cite web |title=Redirect page |website=UNHCR |url=https://www.unhcr.org/uk/europe-emergency.html |language=fr |access-date=2020-10-05}}</ref> The Voice of Young Refugees in Europe<ref name="Voices of Young Refugees in Europe 2019">{{cite web |title=Voices of Young Refugees in Europe |website=Voices of Young Refugees in Europe |date=2019-11-13 |url=https://www.wearevyre.net |access-date=2020-10-05}}</ref> provide a support and educational network for young refugees.  Many refugees arrive in Europe with a great diversity of skills, experience and specialisations that could make tangible contributions to the EU workforce. In the UK, the [[Refugee Council]] organisation provides support and advice to refugees and asylum seekers. The Building Bridges Partnership in the UK was set up to support refugee health professionals re-qualify in the UK. Other organisations include Transitions, a social enterprise that provides advice and helps refugees find placements depending on their qualifications and skills.

==Profile of migrants==
{{image frame|content={{Photomontage
| photo1a = Map of the European Migrant Crisis 2015 - Asylum applicants' countries of origin.png{{!}}Countries of origin of asylum applicants in the EU and EFTA states between 1 January and 30 June 2015
