{{See also|Refugee crisis|List of countries by refugee population|Arab Winter|Refugees of the Syrian Civil War|Emigration from Africa}}

According to the [[UNHCR]], the number of [[Displaced person|forcibly displaced people]] worldwide reached 59,500,000 by the end of 2014,<ref>{{cite news |title=The Global Refugee Crisis, Region by Region |url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/06/09/world/migrants-global-refugee-crisis-mediterranean-ukraine-syria-rohingya-malaysia-iraq.html |work=The New York Times |date=26 August 2015}}</ref> with a 40 percent increase since 2011. Of these 59.5&nbsp;million, 19.5&nbsp;million were [[refugees]] (14.4&nbsp;million under UNHCR's mandate, plus 5.1&nbsp;million [[Palestinian refugees]] under [[UNRWA]]'s mandate) and 1.8&nbsp;million were [[asylum-seekers]]. The rest were persons displaced within their own countries ([[internally displaced persons]]). The refugees under UNHCR's mandate increased by approximately 2.7&nbsp;million (23%) compared to the end of 2013, the highest level since 1995. Among them, [[Syrian refugees]] became the largest refugee group in 2014 (3.9&nbsp;million, 1.55&nbsp;million more than the previous year), overtaking [[Afghan refugees]] (2.6&nbsp;million), who had been the largest refugee group for three decades. Six of the ten largest countries refugees originated from were African: [[Somalia]], [[Sudanese refugees|Sudan]], [[South Sudan]], the [[Democratic Republic of Congo]], the [[Central African Republic]], and [[Eritrea]].<ref name="UNHCRtrends">{{cite web |url=http://unhcr.org/556725e69.html |title=UNHCR Global Trends –Forced Displacement in 2014 |publisher=UNHCR |date=18 June 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=The dispossessed|url=https://www.economist.com/blogs/graphicdetail/2015/06/daily-chart-15|work=The Economist|date=18 June 2015}}</ref>

In 2016, the UNHCR reported the number of forcibly displaced people worldwide reached 65,600,000 at the end of 2016, the highest level since World War II. Of these 65,600,000, 22.5 million were refugees (17.2 million under UNHCR's mandate, plus 5.3 million Palestinian refugees under UNRWA's mandate), 2.8 million of which were asylum seekers. The rest were internally displaced persons. The 17.2 million refugees under UNHCR's mandate increased by 2.9 million compared to the end of 2014, and is the highest number of refugees since 1992.

As of 2017, 55 percent of refugees worldwide came from three nations: South Sudan, Afghanistan, and Syria. Of all displaced peoples, 17 percent of them are hosted in Europe. As of April 2018, 15,481 refugees successfully arrived in Europe via sea within the first few months of the year alone. There was an estimated 500 that have died. In 2015, there was a total of 1.02 million arrivals by sea. Since then, there is still an influx, albeit steadily decreasing.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://data2.unhcr.org/en/situations/mediterranean#_ga=2.97327127.949908654.1523126683-1807715582.1519328261|title=Situation Mediterranean Situation|website=data2.unhcr.org|language=en|access-date=2018-04-07}}</ref>

UNHCR data reported 58 percent of the refugees and migrants arriving in Europe by sea in 2015 were men, 17 percent were women and 25 percent were children.<ref name="bsUNHCR2015" /><ref name="abcUNHCR2015" /> Of the asylum applications received in Sweden in 2015, 70 percent were by men (including minors),<ref name="sma2015" /> as men search for a safe place to live and work before attempting to reunite later with their families.<ref name="UNHCRMed" /> In war-torn countries, men are also at greater risk of being forced to fight or killed.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.politico.eu/article/europes-man-problem/|title=Europe's man problem|publisher=Politico Europe|date=6 January 2016}}</ref> Among people arriving in Europe there were also large numbers of women and unaccompanied children.<ref name="UNHCRMed">{{cite web|url=http://www.unhcr.org/5592bd059.html#7 |title=The sea route to Europe: The Mediterranean passage in the age of refugees |page=7 |publisher=[[UNHCR]]}}</ref> Europe received a record number of asylum applications from unaccompanied child refugees in 2015 as they became separated from their families in war, or their family could not afford to send more than one member abroad. Younger refugees also have better chances of receiving asylum.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.northjersey.com/news/young-and-alone-europe-sees-record-surge-of-child-refugees-1.1430278|title=Young and alone: Europe sees record surge of child refugees|author=Sylvia Hui, Associated Press|date=11 October 2015|access-date=11 October 2015|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151020000722/http://www.northjersey.com/news/young-and-alone-europe-sees-record-surge-of-child-refugees-1.1430278|archive-date=20 October 2015|df=dmy-all}}</ref>

UNHCR noted the top ten nationalities of Mediterranean Sea arrivals in 2015 were [[Syria]] (49 percent), [[Afghanistan]] (21 percent), [[Iraq]] (8 percent), [[Eritrea]] (4 percent), [[Pakistan]] (2 percent), [[Nigeria]] (2 percent), [[Somalia]] (2 percent), [[Sudan]] (1 percent), [[the Gambia]] (1 percent) and [[Mali]] (1 percent).<ref name="bsUNHCR2015">{{cite news|url=http://www.business-standard.com/article/pti-stories/over-1-million-arrivals-in-europe-by-sea-unhcr-115123000668_1.html|title=Over 1 million arrivals in Europe by sea: UNHCR|date=30 December 2015|work=[[Business Standard]]}}</ref><ref name="abcUNHCR2015">{{cite news|url=http://www.abc.net.au/news/2015-12-30/more-than-1-million-asylum-seekers-reached-europe-by-sea-in-2015/7060012|title=More than 1 million asylum seekers reached Europe by sea this year: UNHCR|date=30 December 2015|work=[[Australian Broadcasting Corporation]]}}</ref> Asylum seekers of seven nationalities had an asylum recognition rate of over 50 percent in EU states in the first quarter of 2015, which meant that they obtained protection over half the time they applied: Syrians (94 percent recognition rate), Eritreans (90 percent), [[Iraq]]is (88 percent), Afghans (66 percent), [[Iran]]ians (65 percent), [[Somalia|Somalis]] (60 percent) and [[Sudan]]ese (53 percent). Migrants of these nationalities accounted for 90 percent of the arrivals in Greece and 47 percent of the arrivals in Italy between January and August 2015.<ref name="Asylum quarterly report" /><ref>{{cite news |title=How many migrants to Europe are refugees? |url=https://www.economist.com/blogs/economist-explains/2015/09/economist-explains-4 |work=The Economist |date=7 September 2015}}</ref>

[[Developing countries]] hosted the largest share of refugees (86 percent by the end of 2014, the highest figure in more than two decades); the [[least developed countries]] alone provided asylum to 25 percent of refugees worldwide.<ref name="UNHCRtrends" /> Even though most Syrian refugees were hosted by neighbouring countries such as [[Turkey]], [[Lebanon]] and [[Jordan]], the number of asylum applications lodged by Syrian refugees in Europe steadily increased between 2011 and 2015, totaling 813,599 in 37 European countries (including both EU members and non-members) as of November 2015; 57 percent of them applied for [[asylum in Germany]] or [[Serbia]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Syria Regional Refugee Response|url=http://data.unhcr.org/syrianrefugees/asylum.php|publisher=UNHCR}}</ref>

===Origins and routes===
[[File:Aegean Sea with island groups labeled.gif|thumb|Island groups of the [[Aegean Sea]] ]]
[[File:Greece–Turkey land border.svg|thumb|Greek, Turkish and Bulgarian borders and the course of the [[Maritsa|Evros River]] (also known as Maritsa River)]]

As of May 2017, [[Frontex]] (the European border and coast guard agency) identified the following eight main routes on sea and on land used by irregular migrants to enter the EU:<ref>{{cite web |title=Migratory routes map |url=http://frontex.europa.eu/trends-and-routes/migratory-routes-map/ |access-date=29 August 2015 |publisher=[[Frontex]]}}</ref>

*''Western African route'' (Sea passage from [[West Africa]]n countries into the [[Canary Islands]] (i.e., territory of [[Spain]]))
*''Western Mediterranean route'' (Sea passage from [[North Africa]] to southern coast of Spain which also includes the land route through the borders of [[Ceuta]] and [[Melilla]])
*''Central Mediterranean route'' (Sea passage from North Africa (particularly [[Egypt]]<ref>{{cite web|url=http://regionalmms.org/index.php/research-publications/feature-articles/item/51|title=Migration through Egypt: The Safe Alternative to Libya?|access-date=28 December 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20161229032112/http://regionalmms.org/index.php/research-publications/feature-articles/item/51|archive-date=29 December 2016|url-status=dead}}</ref> and [[Libya]]) towards [[Italy]] and [[Malta]] across the [[Mediterranean Sea]]). Most migrants taking this route board vessels operated by [[People smuggling|people smugglers]]. NGOs such as [[Save the Children]], [[Médecins Sans Frontières|MSF]], and the German organisation Sea Eye operate search-and-rescue ships in this area to bring migrants to Europe.<ref name=":4" />
*''[[Apulia]] and [[Calabria]] route'' (Sea passage from Turkey and Egypt who enter Greece before crossing the [[Ionian Sea]] towards southern Italy; since October 2014 this has been classified by Frontex as a subset of the Central Mediterranean route)
*''Albania–Greece circular route'' (Large number of illegal land border crossings where economic migrants from [[Albania]] cross into [[Greece]] for seasonal jobs before returning home.)
*''Western Balkan route'' (Land and sea route from the Greek-Turkish border to [[Hungary]] via [[North Macedonia]] and [[Serbia]], [[Romania]] or [[Croatia]].<ref name="aljazeera.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2015/09/refugees-seeking-routes-border-closures-150916045558970.html|title=Refugees cross Croatia border in search of new route|publisher=Al Jazeera|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> Mostly used by Greater Middle Eastern immigrants (from [[Syria]], [[Afghanistan]] and [[Iraq]]) but also by large numbers of migrants from [[Western Balkans|Western Balkan]] countries, primarily [[Kosovo]]).
*''Eastern Mediterranean route'' (Passage used primarily by Greater Middle Eastern migrants crossing from Turkey into the EU via [[Greece]], [[Bulgaria]] or [[Cyprus]]. Large portions of these migrants continue along the Western Balkan route towards Hungary or Romania.)
*''Eastern Borders route'' (The 6,000&nbsp;km long land border between EU's eastern member countries and [[Russia]], [[Belarus]], [[Ukraine]] and [[Moldova]].)

Another route was added:
* The ''Arctic route'' (from Russia via to [[Sør-Varanger]] in [[Norway]]) emerged by September 2015<ref name="ArcticRoute" /> and became one of the fastest-growing routes to enter [[Western Europe]] by November 2015.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2015/11/11/world/asia/11reuters-europe-migrants-arctic.html?ref=world&_r=0|title=Growing Number of Asylum Seekers Opt for Arctic Route to Enter Europe|author=Catherine Evans|newspaper=The New York Times|date=11 November 2015|access-date=11 November 2015}}</ref> This route was temporarily closed in 2016 after Russia and Norway decided to limit movement through Salla and Lotta for migrants, and allowed only Russian, Norwegian and Belarusian citizens to access it.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.express.co.uk/news/world/657646/Russia-SHUTS-DOWN-border-Europe-fears-new-migrant-route-ARCTIC|title=Russia SHUTS DOWN border with Europe amid fears over new migrant route through the ARCTIC|first=Oli|last=Smith|date=2 April 2016}}</ref>

====Economic migrants====
Migrants from the [[Western Balkans]] ([[Kosovo]], [[Albania]], [[Serbia]]) and parts of [[West Africa]] ([[The Gambia]], [[Nigeria]]) were more likely to be [[economic migrant]]s, who were fleeing poverty and job scarcity, many of whom hoped for a better lifestyle and job offers without valid claims to [[Convention relating to the Status of Refugees|refugee status]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Mass Migration: What Is Driving the Balkan Exodus? |url=http://www.spiegel.de/international/europe/western-balkan-exodus-puts-pressure-on-germany-and-eu-a-1049274.html |work=Der Spiegel |date=26 August 2015}}</ref><ref name="NossiterNiger">{{cite news |last1=Nossiter |first1=Adam |title=Migrant Smuggling Business Is Booming in Niger, Despite Crackdown |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/08/21/world/africa/migrant-smuggling-business-is-booming-in-niger-despite-crackdown.html?ref=world&_r=0 |access-date=20 August 2015 |work=The New York Times |date=20 August 2015}}</ref> The majority of asylum applicants from [[Serbia]], [[North Macedonia]] and [[Montenegro]] are [[Romani people|Roma]] people who felt discriminated against in their countries of origin.<ref name="BalkanExodus">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34173252|title=Migrant crisis: Explaining the exodus from the Balkans|work=BBC News|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref>

Some argue that migrants have been seeking to settle preferentially in national destinations that offer more generous [[social welfare]] benefits and host more established Middle Eastern and African immigrant communities. Others argue that migrants are attracted to more tolerant societies with stronger economies, and that the chief motivation for leaving Turkey is that they are not permitted to leave camps or work.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/13/world/europe/eastern-europe-migrant-refugee-crisis.html|title=Eastern Bloc's Resistance to Refugees Highlights Europe's Cultural and Political Divisions|author=Rick Lyman|newspaper=The New York Times|date=12 September 2015|access-date=13 September 2015}}</ref> A large number of refugees in Turkey have been faced with difficult living circumstances;<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Villasana |first1=Danielle |title=Picturing health: challenges for Syrian refugees in Turkey |journal=The Lancet |date=October 2016 |volume=388 |issue=10056 |pages=2096–103 |doi=10.1016/S0140-6736(16)31647-6 |pmid=27642017 |s2cid=6487863 }}</ref> thus, many refugees arriving in southern Europe continue their journey in attempts to reach northern European countries such as Germany, which are observed as having more prominent outcomes of security.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.unhcr.org/en-us/protection/operations/5592bd059/sea-route-europe-mediterranean-passage-age-refugees.html|title=The sea route to Europe: The Mediterranean passage in the age of refugees|last=Refugees|first=United Nations High Commissioner for|newspaper=UNHCR|access-date=16 November 2016}}</ref> In contrast to Germany, France's popularity eroded in 2015 among migrants seeking asylum after being historically considered a popular final destination for the EU migrants.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/18/world/europe/a-belated-welcome-in-france-is-drawing-few-migrants.html|title=A Belated Welcome in France Is Drawing Few Migrants|author=Adam Nossiter|newspaper=The New York Times|date=17 September 2015|access-date=17 September 2015|quote=Migrants crowding onto the trains in Hungary shout, "Germany, Germany!" But they do not shout, "France, France."}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/09/10/world/europe/scale-of-migrant-crisis-in-europe.html|title=The Scale of the Migrant Crisis, From 160 to Millions|author1=Gregor Aisch |author2=Sarah Almukhtar |author3=Josh Keller |author4=Wilson Andrews |newspaper=The New York Times|date=10 September 2015|access-date=17 September 2015}}</ref>

The influx from states like [[Nigeria]] and [[Pakistan]] is a mix of economic migrants and refugees fleeing from violence and war such as the [[Boko Haram insurgency]] in northeastern Nigeria and the [[War in North-West Pakistan]].<ref name="origins" /><ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Who does the EU send back?|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34190359|work=BBC News|date=9 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Europe's forgotten migrants – the ones who aren't from Syria|url=https://www.latimes.com/world/europe/la-fg-europe-forgotten-migrants-20150916-story.html|work=Los Angeles Times|date=16 September 2015}}</ref>
==Public opinion==

=== Perspectives of refugees and asylum seekers ===
British Somali poet [[Warsan Shire]]'s poem 'Home' has become a popular depiction of the refugee experience amongst refugees and asylum seekers, particularly the line “You have to understand...no one puts their children in a boat, unless the water is safer than the land.”<ref>{{Cite web|last=Kuo|first=Lily|title=This poem is now the rallying call for refugees: "No one leaves home unless home is the mouth of a shark"|url=https://qz.com/africa/897871/warsan-shires-poem-captures-the-reality-of-life-for-refugees-no-one-leaves-home-unless-home-is-the-mouth-of-a-shark/|access-date=2020-10-05|website=Quartz Africa|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=May 20 2020|date=2020-05-20|title=How Europe is using coronavirus to reinforce its hostile environment in the Mediterranean|url=https://lacuna.org.uk/migration/how-europe-is-using-coronavirus-to-reinforce-its-hostile-environment-in-the-mediterranean/|access-date=2020-10-05|website=Lacuna Magazine|language=en-US}}</ref>

=== Death of Alan Kurdi ===
{{Main|Death of Alan Kurdi}}
Images of the body of a 3-year-old Syrian boy named Alan Kurdi (after he drowned on 2 September 2015) are widely believed to have shifted public opinion on the 'European migrant crisis' as well as the opinions of world leaders.<ref>{{cite web|last=Agencies|first=Daily Sabah with|date=2015-09-03|title=French President calls Erdoğan over images of drowned Syrian boy, calls for common EU refugee policy|url=https://www.dailysabah.com/diplomacy/2015/09/03/french-president-calls-erdogan-over-images-of-drowned-syrian-boy-calls-for-common-eu-refugee-policy|access-date=2020-10-05|website=Daily Sabah|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=CNN|first=Ashley Fantz and Catherine E. Shoichet|title=Drowned Syrian boy's dad: Everything is gone|url=https://www.cnn.com/2015/09/03/europe/migration-crisis-aylan-kurdi-turkey-canada/index.html|access-date=2020-10-05|website=CNN}}</ref> Kurdi and his family were Syrian refugees, and 3-year-old Alan passed away alongside his brother and mother - only his father survived the journey, telling CNN "[e]verything I was dreaming of is gone. I want to bury my children and sit beside them until I die."<ref>{{cite web|last=CNN|first=Ashley Fantz and Catherine E. Shoichet|title=Drowned Syrian boy's dad: Everything is gone|url=https://www.cnn.com/2015/09/03/europe/migration-crisis-aylan-kurdi-turkey-canada/index.html|access-date=2020-10-05|website=CNN}}</ref> Kurdi's body was photographed by Turkish journalist [[Nilüfer Demir]].

=== Demonstrations ===
{{image frame|content={{Photomontage
| photo1a   = Wien - Demo Mensch sein in Österreich - 8.jpg {{!}} "Syrian Refugees Welcome" rally in [[Vienna]], 31 August 2015

| photo2b   = Natsit ja ISIS on samaa paskaa.jpg{{!}}A pro-migration demonstration in [[Helsinki]], Finland, showing a sign saying ''Natsit & ISIS = samaa paskaa'', [[Finnish language|Finnish]] for "Nazis & ISIS = the same shit".

[[Pegida]], a far right political movement, was founded in Dresden in October 2014.  Pegida's stated goal was to curb immigration and organization accused authorities of failure to enforce immigration laws. On 9 January 2016 about 1,700 people joined a 'PEGIDA' demonstration.<ref>{{cite news |title=Riot police break up anti-refugee protest in wake of Cologne attacks |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2016/01/10/riot-police-break-up-anti-refugee-protest-in-wake-of-cologne-attacks.html |work=CNBC |date=10 January 2016 |language=en}}</ref> Following the demonstrations representatives of Pegida, including Pegida Austria, Pegida Bulgaria, and Pegida Netherlands published their [[Pegida#Fortress Europe|Fortress Europe]] on 23 January 2016. The English-language document stated that it is duty to stand up against "political Islam, extreme Islamic regimes and their European collaborators."<ref>{{cite news |last1=Welle (www.dw.com) |first1=Deutsche |title=Pegida meets with European allies in the Czech Republic {{!}} DW {{!}} 23.01.2016 |url=https://www.dw.com/en/pegida-meets-with-european-allies-in-the-czech-republic/a-19000895 |work=DW.COM}}</ref> During this period a far-right position [[Eurabia]] went mainstream, which was a [[far-right]] [[Islamophobia|Islamophobic]] [[conspiracy theory]], involving [[globalism|globalist]] entities allegedly led by French and Arab powers, to Islamise and Arabise Europe, thereby weakening its existing culture and undermining a previous alignment with the U.S. and Israel.<ref name=Guardian190816>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2019/aug/16/the-myth-of-eurabia-how-a-far-right-conspiracy-theory-went-mainstream | title = The myth of Eurabia: how a far-right conspiracy theory went mainstream | author= Andrew Brown | newspaper = The Guardian | date= 16 August 2019 | access-date= 24 August 2019}}</ref>

In 2015, members of the far-right, anti-immigration group [[Britain First]] organised protest marches.<ref name=BF-LibertGB>{{cite news |title=Britain First: anti-Islam group that bills itself as a patriotic movement |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/nov/29/britain-first-anti-islam-group-that-bills-itself-as-a-patriotic-movement |work=the Guardian |date=29 November 2017 |language=en}}</ref> According to 2015 analysis, Islamophobic groups in Britain were capitalizing on public concerns following the Paris attacks, ongoing refugee crisis and 24 different far-right groups were also attempted to provoke a cultural civil war.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Townsend |first1=Mark |title=Anti-Muslim prejudice "is moving to the mainstream" |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/dec/05/far-right-muslim-cultural-civil-war |work=The Observer |date=5 December 2015}}</ref> Other groups included [[Pegida UK]] and [[Liberty GB]]. Liberty GB was an anti-immigration political party. Liberty GB's chairman was Paul Weston who writes about impending civil war against Muslims and "[[White genocide conspiracy theory|white genocide]]" in Britain.<ref name=BF-LibertGB /> These groups used the [[Great Replacement]] in their messaging which [[Bernard-Henri Lévy]] dismissed the notion as a "junk idea".<ref name=Replacement/> Great Replacement [you-will-not-replace-us!] had gained a lot of traction in Europe.<ref name=Replacement>{{cite news |last1=Williams |first1=Thomas Chatterton |title=The French Origins of "You Will Not Replace Us" |url=https://www.newyorker.com/magazine/2017/12/04/the-french-origins-of-you-will-not-replace-us |work=The New Yorker |language=en-us}}</ref>

On 25 December 2015, a Muslim prayer hall was raided by protesters [mob] in [[Ajaccio]], which French Prime Minister Manuel Valls said it was "an unacceptable desecration". The protesters [mob] assumed a recent crime in the town was performed by [part of] a large North African, often Muslim, immigrant population of the town.<ref>{{cite news |last1=McHugh |first1=Jess |title=After Anti-Muslim Protest In Corsica, Nationalism, High Unemployment, Slow Economic Growth Blamed |url=https://www.ibtimes.com/after-anti-muslim-protest-corsica-nationalism-high-unemployment-slow-economic-growth-2240947 |work=International Business Times |date=28 December 2015}}</ref> The [[2015 Corsican protests]] continued couple more days, as hundreds defied protest ban.<ref>{{cite news |title=Hundreds defy Corsica protest ban |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35187901 |work=BBC News |date=28 December 2015}}</ref> Another riot in the same year, the [[2015 Geldermalsen riot]], was ignited after the town council's decision to establish an asylum centre for 1,500 asylum seekers in the [[Netherlands|Dutch]] town of [[Geldermalsen]].<ref>{{Cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Dutch town riots over asylum centre plan|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35118496|work=BBC News|date=17 December 2015}}</ref> After a festival celebrating the city's founding, the [[2018 Chemnitz protests]] took place in the early morning of 26 August following a fight broke out. The incident reignited the tensions ["Foreigners get out!"] surrounding immigration to Germany. Mass protests against immigration were followed by counter-demonstrations.<ref name=Chemnitzprotests /> German government condemned right-wing rioters after protests surprised police.<ref name=Chemnitzprotests>{{cite news |title=German government condemns right-wing rioters |url=https://edition.cnn.com/2018/08/27/europe/germany-chemnitz-violence-intl/ |work=CNN}}</ref> The [[Alternative for Germany]] (blamed for being behind the protests, but officially denied responsibility) campaigned on an anti-immigration, anti-Islam platform, won more than 25% of the vote in the state of Saxony—where Chemnitz is located. Alternative for Germany declared "Families can't even feel safe in going to the state festival any more... We call upon our voters to do something about this."<ref name=Chemnitzprotests />

Response to right-wing positions were [[Birlikte]], which was the name and motto of a series of semi-annual rallies and corresponding [[cultural festival]]s against right-wing extremist violence in Germany. First one took place on 9 June 2014 in [[Cologne]], second on 14 June 2015, and the third one 5 June 2016. Birlikte events comprised a mixture of speeches and multi-cultural music performances.<ref>{{cite web |title=Birlikte: Die Highlights im Birlikte-Programm |language=de |date=2014-11-29 |website=koeln.de |publisher=[[NetCologne Gesellschaft für Telekommunikation mbH]], Abteilung Content |url=http://www.koeln.de/koeln/birlikte_836979.html?page=0,1 |access-date=2014-11-29 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141129023858/http://www.koeln.de/koeln/birlikte_836979.html?page=0,1 |archive-date=2014-11-29}} [https://web.archive.org/web/20170909030323/http://birlikte.info/Programm_Birlikte_2016.pdf]</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Veranstalter sagen Festival Birlikte komplett ab |language=de |author-first1=Jan H. |author-last1=Stellmacher |author-first2=Martin |author-last2=Böhmer |date=2016-06-05 |newspaper=[[Express (Cologne newspaper)|Express]] |url=http://www.express.de/koeln/wegen-unwetterwarnung-veranstalter-sagen-festival-birlikte-komplett-ab-24173842 |access-date=2019-05-13 |url-status=live |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160627215538/https://www.express.de/koeln/wegen-unwetterwarnung-veranstalter-sagen-festival-birlikte-komplett-ab-24173842 |archive-date=2016-06-27}}</ref>

On 12 September 2015, tens of thousands of people have taken part in a "day of action" in several European cities in support of refugees and migrants.<ref name=BBCdemons>{{cite news |title=Rallies in Europe as migrants arrive |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34235673 |work=BBC News |date=12 September 2015}}</ref> At the same day, rallies against migrants took place in some eastern European countries.<ref name=BBCdemons />

On 18 February 2017, tens of thousands of demonstrators [carried signs reading "Enough excuses, welcome them now"] marched after Ada Cola's [mayor] call for more immigrants at the [[protest "Volem acollir"]].<ref>{{cite news |last1=France-Presse |first1=Agence |title=Protesters in Barcelona urge Spain to take in more refugees |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2017/feb/18/protesters-in-barcelona-urge-spain-to-take-in-more-refugees |work=The Guardian |date=18 February 2017}}</ref>

=== Surveys on immigration ===
The Pew study links the anti-immigrant rhetoric of the right-wing parties across the continent and the heated debate over the [[Brexit|UK’s decision to exit the European Union]] to the surge of refugees into Europe. There were sharp and deep ideological divides among the public over their views of minorities and diversity represented by these immigrants. Negative attitudes toward immigrants were tied to a belief that these groups do not wish to participate in their society.<ref name=2016Opinion />

==== Security ====
A study published by [[Pew Research Center]] on 11 July 2016 concluded that "Europeans fear [that a] wave of refugees means more terrorism, fewer jobs".  Half of the population in Italy and Sweden blame crime on immigrants.<ref name=2016Opinion>{{cite report  |last1=Wike |first1=Richard |title=Europeans Fear Wave of Refugees Will Mean More Terrorism, Fewer Jobs |url=https://www.pewresearch.org/global/wp-content/uploads/sites/2/2016/07/Pew-Research-Center-EU-Refugees-and-National-Identity-Report-FINAL-July-11-2016.pdf |website=Pew Research Center:Global Attitudes & Trends |publisher=Pew Research Center}}</ref>

==== Economy ====
A study published by [[Pew Research Center]] in 2016 concluded that Half of the respondents felt that immigrants would take away jobs and social benefits; Hungarians, Poles, Greeks, Italians and French identify losing jobs and social benefits as their first concern.<ref name=2016Opinion />

In a 2016 poll, refugees, unemployment, and refugees taking away jobs was the list of issues that ordinary Finns were most concerned about.<ref>{{cite news |title=Do refugees take away jobs? |url=https://www.debatingeurope.eu/2018/04/04/refugees-take-away-jobs/#.XtZi8TdKijA |work=Debating Europe |date=4 April 2018}}</ref> The original study in Finland found that immigration was a marginal concern in the early 2010s, however the economy was a concern since the neighboring Soviet Union, significant export market, collapsed in the 1990s. The original study found that around 30% believe that uncontrolled immigration was a problem. This ratio was 40% under the age of 25, people who often were looking for jobs themselves. Women consider it a problem larger percentage than men.<ref>{{cite news |last1=staff |title=Top Finnish concerns: Unemployment, the refugee situation and gov't indecision |url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/top_finnish_concerns_unemployment_the_refugee_situation_and_govt_indecision/8770166 |work=Yle Uutiset |language=en}}</ref>

==== Muslim immigration ====
The debate on the Muslim immigrants moved into the center of European discourse. Muslim immigration presented as a cultural threat to the future of Europe, using the argument "Muslim immigration is an incompatible ontological category predicated on culture [they don't share our values!]."<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Yılmaz |first1=Ferruh |title=Right-wing hegemony and immigration: How the populist far-right achieved hegemony through the immigration debate in Europe |journal=Current Sociology |date=1 May 2012 |volume=60 |issue=3 |pages=368–381 |doi=10.1177/0011392111426192 |s2cid=145740365 |language=en |issn=0011-3921}}</ref> Public discourse [across Western Europe] concentrated on Muslims and Islam with a wide spectrum claim that Islam is incompatible with the values of Europe.<ref>{{cite book |last1=Bowen |first1=John |title=European states and their Muslim citizens : the impact of institutions on perceptions and boundaries |publisher=Cambridge University Press |isbn=978-1-107-03864-6}}</ref> EU states such as Slovakia have openly rejected to accept the refugees either because they do not want the Brussels to impose immigration policies and/or because they simply do not want Muslims or non-Europeans in their communities.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Brljavac |first1=Bedrudin |title=REFUGEE CRISIS IN EUROPE: THE CASE STUDIES OF SWEDEN AND SLOVAKIA |journal=Journal of Liberty and International Affairs |date=2017 |volume=III |issue=Suppl |pages=91–107 |url=https://www.ceeol.com/search/article-detail?id=553205 |language=en |issn=1857-9760}}</ref> A study released by the [[European Union Agency for Fundamental Rights]] found out that almost 40% of Muslims (focused on first- and second-generation immigrants) surveyed reported discrimination in their daily life.<ref>{{cite news |last1=Welle (www.dw.com) |first1=Deutsche |title=Muslims in the EU: Feeling at home despite discrimination {{!}} DW {{!}} 21.09.2017 |url=https://www.dw.com/en/muslims-in-the-eu-feeling-at-home-despite-discrimination/a-40630952 |work=DW.COM}}</ref>

A study published in 2016 by [[Royal Institute of International Affairs]] surveyed 10,000 people in ten European states found that 55% agreed with the statement that ‘all further migration from mainly Muslim countries should be stopped’, with particularly strong support for this sentiment in Austria, Poland, Hungary, France and Belgium<ref>Goodwin, M., Raines, T., and Cutts, D. (2017) What Do Europeans Think About Muslim Immigration? London: Chatham House.</ref> A study published by [[Pew Research Center]] in 2016 concluded that attitudes towards migrants were deeply connected to individual values and people who have a more negative view of Muslims are also much more concerned about the threat [refugees leaving Iraq and Syria are a major threat to their country].<ref>{{cite web |last1=staff |title=European opinions of the refugee crisis in 5 charts |url=https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2016/09/16/european-opinions-of-the-refugee-crisis-in-5-charts/ |website=Pew Research Center}}</ref>

TNS Gallup for Berlingske found out that two out of three (64%) Danes want to restrict immigration from Muslim countries.<ref>{{cite news |last1=staff |title=Two out of three will restrict Muslim immigration |url=https://www.berlingske.dk/samfund/to-ud-af-tre-vil-begraense-muslimsk-indvandring |agency=/ritzau/ |date=14 March 2017}}</ref>

The public perception of the migrant crisis from the Hungarian point of view characterized as anti-immigration since 2015. Muslim immigrants are perceived as a symbolic threat to the dominant—mostly Christian—Western culture and [specifically in the Hungarian context] asylum seekers with a Christian background are more welcomed than those with a Muslim background.<ref>{{cite journal |last1=Simonovits |first1=Bori |title=The Public Perception of the Migration Crisis from the Hungarian Point of View: Evidence from the Field |journal=Geographies of Asylum in Europe and the Role of European Localities |series=IMISCOE Research Series |date=2020 |pages=155–176 |doi=10.1007/978-3-030-25666-1_8 |publisher=Springer International Publishing |isbn=978-3-030-25665-4 |language=en|doi-access=free }}</ref>

=== Brexit ===
{{further|Causes of the vote in favour of Brexit}}
The [[2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum]] took place on 23 June 2016. Result was the UK voted to "Leave" the European Union by 51.89% to 48.11% for Remain. [[Opinion polling for the United Kingdom European Union membership referendum|At the opinion polls]], public responded leaving the EU was "more likely to bring about a better immigration system, improved border controls, a fairer welfare system, better quality of life, and the ability to control our own laws."<ref name=lordashcroftpolls/> Also at the opinion polls, public responded leaving the EU "offered the best chance for the UK to regain control over immigration and its own borders".<ref name=lordashcroftpolls>{{cite web |last1=Ashcroft |first1=Lord |title=How the United Kingdom voted on Thursday... and why - Lord Ashcroft Polls |url=https://lordashcroftpolls.com/2016/06/how-the-united-kingdom-voted-and-why/ |publisher=lordashcroftpolls}} http://lordashcroftpolls.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/06/How-the-UK-voted-Full-tables-1.pdf</ref>

Migration crisis was a defining issue in the "[[Causes of the vote in favour of Brexit|Leave campaign]]", ([[Vote Leave]] predominant economic, [[Leave.EU]] predominant anti-immigration) giving a sharper focus to the slogan of “taking back control” and opposition to EU law and European human rights law, both giving rights to “foreigners” which were deemed unacceptable by many conservatives as well as those further to the right. Crisis created the image of a Union unable to handle the situation, and "Leave" campaigners raised the spectre of Turkish people [generally did not distinguish between different categories of migrants] gaining freedom of movement.<ref name=Oxford />

Theresa May, who sided on "Remain," declared that Britain should withdraw from the European convention on human rights (ECHR) irrespective of the EU referendum result. The Home Secretary, Theresa May, has argued in a speech staking out her position between Brexit (She was against) - migration crisises (She was for control of refugee policies)"<ref name=Oxford>{{cite web |last1=Outhwaite |first1=William |editor3-first=Immanuel |editor3-last=Ness |editor2-first=Marie |editor2-last=Ruiz |editor1-first=Cecilia |editor1-last=Menjívar |title=Migration Crisis and "Brexit" |url=https://www.oxfordhandbooks.com/view/10.1093/oxfordhb/9780190856908.001.0001/oxfordhb-9780190856908-e-7 |website=The Oxford Handbook of Migration Crises |publisher=Oxford Handbooks |language=en |doi=10.1093/oxfordhb/9780190856908.001.0001 |date=28 February 2019|isbn=9780190856908 }}</ref> {{Quote|[on the freedom to act regarding migrants/foreigners] The ECHR can bind the hands of parliament, adds nothing to our prosperity, makes us less secure by preventing the deportation of dangerous foreign nationals—and does nothing to change the attitudes of governments like Russia’s when it comes to human rights . . . it isn’t the EU we should leave but the ECHR and the jurisdiction of its court.|Home Secretary, Theresa May<ref>{{cite web |last1=May |first1=Theresa |title=Theresa May addresses audience at the Institute of Mechanical Engineers in central London. |url=https://www.gov.uk/government/speeches/home-secretarys-speech-on-the-uk-eu-and-our-place-in-the-world |website=UK Gov |publisher=UK gov}} Content is available under the Open Government Licence v3.0</ref>}}

=== Hungarian migrant referendum ===
The [[2016 Hungarian migrant quota referendum]] announced by the [[Third Orbán Government]] was about the EU migrant relocation plan. It was commonly referred to as the "quota referendum" in the Hungarian media. In September 2015, the Justice and Home Affairs Council at the EU's interior ministers meeting approved to relocate 1,294 refugees from other member states to Hungary. The referendum question was "Do you want the European Union to be able to mandate the obligatory resettlement of non-Hungarian citizens into Hungary even without the approval of the National Assembly?" The result of the referendum was to reject the plan, with 3,362,224 'No' votes (98.4%) and 56,163 'Yes' votes (1.6%). The voter turnout was 40.4%, which was short of the required 50% threshold stated in the constitution. Government declared result is binding "politically and legally", but the opposition said it was invalid. Mr Orban told EU, it should take a note of the result.<ref>{{cite news |title=Hungary PM claims referendum victory |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-37528325 |work=BBC News |date=3 October 2016}}</ref>

==Developments==
{{Very long section|date=June 2020}}

===Austria===
On 6 August 2015, [[Amnesty International]] Secretary General [[Heinz Patzelt]] inspected the refugee camp ''Bundesbetreuungsstelle'' in [[Traiskirchen]] where more than 4,800 migrants and refugees are housed. Medical expert [[Siroos Mirzaei]] from Amnesty International noted that people had to wait for days to get medical help due to the vast number of people received over a short period of time. The report also stated that only four doctors were present at the refugee camp and showers and other hygienic facilities were in disrepair. Patzelt claimed, "Austria [was] violating human rights and should focus on unattended children and minors".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.amnesty.at/de/traiskirchen-pa2/ |title=Traiskirchen Symptom systematischer Mängel im Umgang mit Asylwerbern |publisher=Amnesty International Österreich |access-date=28 August 2015 |language=de |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150814130015/https://www.amnesty.at/de/traiskirchen-pa2/ |archive-date=14 August 2015 |df=dmy-all }}</ref>

On 27 August 2015, 71 migrants were found dead in an unventilated food truck near [[Vienna]].<ref>see also [[:de:Flüchtlingstragödie bei Parndorf|German Wikipedia]]{{Better source|date=June 2016|reason=[[WP:CIRCULAR]]}}</ref> Austria officially responded by inspecting vehicles for smuggled immigrants entering from Hungary on 31 August 2015, leading to vehicular backups that extended {{Convert|19|km|mi|abbr=}} and train delays for hours.<ref name=StrainedOpenBorders>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/01/world/europe/austria-migrant-crisis-truck.html|title=Migrant Crisis Tests Core European Value: Open Borders |author1=Alison Smale |author2=Melissa Eddy |newspaper=The New York Times |date=31 August 2015 |access-date=1 September 2015}}</ref>

Late on 4 September 2015, Chancellor [[Werner Faymann|Faymann]] of Austria, in conjunction with Chancellor [[Angela Merkel|Merkel]] of Germany, announced that migrants would be allowed to cross the border from Hungary into Austria and onward to Germany. Buses carrying migrants began crossing the Austro-Hungarian border on 5 September 2015.<ref name=AllowedToCross1>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/05/world/europe/migrant-crisis-hungary.html|title=Migrants Cross Austria Border From Hungary |author1=Rick Lyman |author2=Anemona Hartocollis |author3=Alison Smale |newspaper=The New York Times |date=4 September 2015 |access-date=5 September 2015}}</ref><ref name=AllowedToCross2>{{cite web |url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/the-latest-austria-germany-to-accept-bused-migrants/ar-AAdWjak?li=BBgzzfc&ocid=iehp |title=The Latest: Austria, Germany to accept bused migrants |publisher=MSN |access-date=5 September 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151015140038/http://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/the-latest-austria-germany-to-accept-bused-migrants/ar-AAdWjak?li=BBgzzfc&ocid=iehp |archive-date=15 October 2015 |url-status=dead }}</ref> Austria reported that 6,500 migrants had crossed the border by the afternoon of 5 September 2015, with 2,200 already on their way to Germany.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/06/world/europe/migrant-crisis-austria-hungary-germany.html|title=Thousands of Migrants Reach Austria as New Groups Set Off |author1=Alison Smale |author2=Steven Erlanger |newspaper=The New York Times |date=5 September 2015 |access-date=5 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.euronews.com/2015/09/05/relieved-migrants-cross-hungary-austria-border/ |title=Relieved migrants cross Hungary-Austria border |publisher=euronews |date=5 September 2015 |access-date=5 September 2015}}</ref>
[[File:Wien - Westbahnhof, Migranten am 5 Sep 2015.jpg|thumb|Migrants at Vienna's Westbahnhof train station, 5 September 2015]]
On 14 September 2015, Austria followed Germany's example; it instituted border controls of its own and deployed the [[Austrian Armed Forces]] to its border with Hungary.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/15/world/europe/europe-migrants-germany.html|title=Austria, Slovakia and the Netherlands Introduce Border Controls|newspaper=The New York Times|author1=Melissa Eddy |author2=Dan Bilefsky |date=14 September 2015|access-date=14 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/09/14/uk-europe-migrants-austria-idUKKCN0RE0SZ20150914|title=Austria says army will help impose tougher border checks|agency=Reuters UK|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref>

On 19 September 2015, Austria permitted entry to approximately 10,000 migrants arriving from Slovenia and Hungary.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/20/world/europe/thousands-flood-into-austria-as-refugees-are-bounced-around-europe.html|title=Thousands of Migrants Flood into Austria|author1=Sewell Chan |author2=Palko Karasz |newspaper=The New York Times|date=19 September 2015|access-date=20 September 2015}}</ref> Austria took on the role of regulator for the flow of migrants destined for Germany by feeding, housing and providing them health care in transit.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/22/world/europe/austria-takes-on-role-of-distribution-center-for-migrants.html|title=Austria Takes Role of Distribution Center for Germany-Bound Migrants|author1=Palko Karasz |author2=Barbara Surk |newspaper=The New York Times|date=22 September 2015|access-date=22 September 2015}}</ref>

On 28 October 2015, Austria built a 91&nbsp;km long fence along its border with Slovenia<ref name="ld">{{cite web|url=http://www.laenderdaten.de/geographie/grenzen.aspx|title=Staatsgrenzen – Grenzlänge, Küstenlänge und Grenzländer aller Staaten der Welt|work=laenderdaten.de|access-date=8 March 2016}}</ref> to "be able to control the migrants in an orderly manner", said Minister of the Interior [[Johanna Mikl-Leitner]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/austria-build-slovenia-border-fence-control-migrant-flow-081818360.html|title=Austria to build Slovenia border fence to 'control' migrant flow|work=Yahoo News|access-date=28 October 2015}}</ref>

On 20 January 2016, Austria announced it would limit the number of asylum applicants to 37,500 in each of the next four years, compared to the 90,000 applications in 2015.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Austria to slash asylum claims|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-35364768|work=BBC News|date=20 January 2016}}</ref> On 19 February 2016, Austria started putting a daily cap of 80 asylum seekers allowed to enter the country to apply for Austrian asylum, and a maximum of 3,200 allowed daily to transit towards other countries (primarily to Germany). The EU's migration commissioner said the cap was incompatible with Austria's obligations under EU and international law.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Austria asylum cap begins despite EU anger|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35609823|work=BBC News|date=19 February 2016}}</ref> The EU Council of Ministers' legal team however concluded that Austria's moves are not illegal.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.politico.eu/article/asylum-seekers-limit-not-illegal-council-legal-opinion-commission-migration/|title=Council lawyers: Austria's refugee cap not illegal|date=4 March 2016|website=POLITICO}}</ref>

In February 2018, Austrian authorities stopped providing food and accommodation to rejected asylum applicants. The proposed legislation introduced penalties between €5000 to €15000 to those who remained in Austria with those refusing to leave to be detained.<ref name=":5">{{cite web|url=http://www.dw.com/en/austria-plans-tougher-measures-against-refused-asylum-seekers/a-37750857|title=Austria plans tougher measures against refused asylum seekers {{!}} DW {{!}} 28.02.2017|last=(www.dw.com)|first=Deutsche Welle|website=DW.COM|language=en|access-date=2018-04-29}}</ref> According to the interior ministry, application from mainly Afghans, Nigerians and Pakistanis were rejected.<ref name=":5" />

From April 2018, Austrian authorities confiscated mobile phones of migrants in order to use its geographical data to verify how migrants arrived to the country. If migrants were found to have entered via a country covered by the Dublin regulation, they were sent there. To cover the cost of handling the application, 840 euro is demanded.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.france24.com/en/20180418-austria-seize-refugees-mobiles-demand-cash|title=Austria to seize refugees' mobiles and demand cash|date=2018-04-18|work=France 24|access-date=2018-04-29|language=en-US}}</ref>

===Bulgaria===
Bulgaria built a fence along its border with Turkey to prevent migrants from crossing through its territory to reach other EU countries. The fence is equipped with infrared cameras, motion sensors and wire, and is monitored by the army.<ref name="Lyman 2015">{{cite news | last=Lyman | first=Rick | title=Bulgaria Puts Up a New Wall, but This One Keeps People Out | website=The New York Times | date=5 April 2015 | url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/04/06/world/europe/bulgaria-puts-up-a-new-wall-but-this-one-keeps-people-out.html | access-date=28 November 2015}}</ref>

===Croatia===
Croatia received 1,064<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.24sata.hr/svijet/juncker-predstavlja-svoj-plan-u-hrvatsku-ce-1064-izbjeglice-436389|title=Potvrđene najave: Hrvatska će morati primiti 1064 izbjeglice|work=24sata.hr|access-date=19 September 2015|language=hr}}</ref> migrants in 2015{{En dash}}2017 according to the EU plan. Croatia was originally supposed to receive 505 migrants, but decided to accept more—making it the only country in the EU, along with Estonia, to have done so.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://hr.n1info.com/a62086/Svijet/Svijet/Spanjolska-nece-primiti-3000-izbjeglica-dio-ide-u-Hrvatsku.html |title=Španjolska neće primiti 3000 izbjeglica, dio ide u Hrvatsku |work=N1 HR}}</ref> On 29 August 2015 the Croatian daily newspaper ''[[Jutarnji list]]'' published an interview with a "senior government official" who said that the Croatian government formed an interdepartmental working group that worked on a plan to accept migrants. Croatia sent its delegation to the migrants' camps in Italy and Greece in October 2015 to choose immigrants from Syria and Eritrea that Croatia will accept. Criteria for the selection were:

# any kind of connection to Croatia, such as family in Croatia or a diploma from one of the Croatian Universities (while Croatia was a member of [[Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia|Yugoslavia]], many foreigners from [[Non-Aligned Movement]] countries, especially Syrians, came to Croatia to study);
# education in occupations that are in demand in Croatia; and 
# families with small children.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.jutarnji.hr/je-li-hrvatska-spremna-za-izbjeglicki-val--zelimo-skolovane-izbjeglice--najbolje-s-djecom/1406645/|title=JE LI HRVATSKA SPREMNA ZA IZBJEGLIČKI VAL? Želimo školovane izbjeglice, najbolje s djecom |work=jutarnji.hr}}</ref>

Croatia shares a land border with Serbia. As such, there was a risk of a strong influx of migrants from Serbia as Hungary erected a fence on its border with Serbia. Nearly 80 percent of the 527&nbsp;km Serbia-Croatia border consists of the [[Danube]], with the remaining 70 kilometers in [[Syrmia]] dubbed the "Green Border". Parts of the Croatia-Serbia border are known [[minefields in Croatia|minefields]], which represent a considerable threat. According to the Croatian Minister of Interior [[Ranko Ostojić]], "police in the area have enough people and equipment to protect the Croatian border against illegal immigrants".<ref name="auto8">{{cite web|title=Hrvatska na udaru imigranata, krizne točke Bajakovo i Tovarnik|url=http://www.vecernji.hr/hrvatska/bajakovo-i-tovarnik-kriticne-tocke-na-zelenoj-granici-sa-srbijom-kroz-koju-bi-emigranti-mogli-ilegalno-uci-u-hrvatsku-1019618|work=Večernji list}}</ref> Croatian President [[Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović]] and First Deputy Prime Minister [[Vesna Pusić]] rejected the proposal to build a fence on the Croatian border with Serbia.<ref name="auto9">{{cite web|title=Grabar KitaroviĆ: Hrvatska neće graditi zidove prema Srbiji kao Mađarska|url=http://dnevnik.hr/vijesti/svijet/grabar-kitarovic-hrvatska-nece-graditi-zidove-prema-srbiji-kao-madjarska---390052.html|author=T.V.|work=Dnevnik.hr}}</ref><ref name="auto10">{{cite web|title='HRVATSKA NEĆE GRADITI ZIDOVE AKO VAL IZBJEGLICA KRENE PREMA NAMA' Vesna Pusić iskazala prezir prema mađarskom rješenju|url=http://www.jutarnji.hr/-hrvatska-nece-graditi-zidove-ako-val-izbjeglica-krene-prema-nama--vesna-pusic-iskazala-prezir-prema-madarskom-rjesenju/1405895/|work=Jutarnji.hr}}</ref> Grabar-Kitarović accused Merkel of causing "chaos".<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/angela-merkel/11883426/Croatia-president-blames-Angela-Merkel-for-refugee-crisis.html Croatia president blames Angela Merkel for refugee crisis]". ''The Daily Telegraph''. 22 September.</ref> Grabar-Kitarović anticipated a possible new migrant wave that might have come in the winter of 2016 and stated on 21 September 2016 before the UN General Assembly that "if a new migrant wave reache[d] Croatian borders, Croatia would not let migrants pass through its territory" because Croatia needed to protect its territory, adding that it turned out that over 85 percent of them were economic migrants and not genuine refugees.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.index.hr/clanak.aspx?id=920755|title=Kolinda kaže da Hrvatska neće propuštati izbjeglice i da su to ionako većinom ekonomski migranti|website=index.hr}}</ref> Croatian Prime Minister [[Zoran Milanović]] said his country is ready to help refugees coming to Europe, insisting that people fleeing conflict should be given the right to remain in the EU.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.balkaninsight.com/en/article/croatian-pm-offers-help-for-refugees-08-31-2015|title=Croatian PM Pledges Help for Refugees|publisher=balkaninsight.com|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref>

On 15 September 2015, Croatia started to experience the first major waves of refugees, who carved out a new route through Europe after Hungary sealed its borders.<ref name="aljazeera.com" /> On 15 September 2015, Hungary declared it would start arresting people crossing the border illegally, and as of 16 September 2015, Hungary had detained 519 people and pressed criminal charges against 46 for trespassing.<ref name="AlternateCroatia" /> Thousands of migrants were subsequently led to pursue alternative routes through Croatia from Serbia.<ref name="AlternateCroatia">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/17/world/europe/europe-refugee-migrant-crisis.html|title=Migrants Clash With Police in Hungary, as Others Enter Croatia|author1=Rick Lyman |author2=Dan Bilefsky |newspaper=The New York Times|date=16 September 2015|access-date=16 September 2015}}</ref> After Hungary closed its border with Serbia on 15 September, migrants headed towards the Serbian town of [[Šid]], less than 10 kilometers from the Croatian border. Several buses filled with migrants arrived on the Croatian border crossing of [[Tovarnik]], where the Croatian [[Vukovar-Srijem County]] Care and Rescue teams and the [[Croatian Red Cross]] were on standby awaiting migrants.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.index.hr/vijesti/clanak/pogledajte-video-i-fotografije-iz-tovarnika/842208.aspx|title=Ovako je danas bilo u Tovarniku: Preko polja se do Hrvatske probijala i djevojka u kolicima|work=index.hr|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> On 17 September 2015, more than 5,000 migrants arrived in Tovarnik;<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.jutarnji.hr/foto--izbjeglicka-drama-u-hr-u-hrvatsku-uslo-5650-izbjeglica--u-tovarniku-situacija-izmakla-kontroli/1419579/|title=FOTO, VIDEO: SITUACIJA SVE TEŽA Drama u Slavoniji: Vlaka još uvijek nema, a izbjeglice nemaju ni kapi vode! U Dugavama azilant gađao ciglom fotoreportera, s balkona hotela viču: 'Sloboda' |work=jutarnji.hr}}</ref> Ostojić said Croatia was "absolutely full" by the evening. Croatia decided to close its border with Serbia<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34286432|title=Migrant crisis: Croatia closes border crossings with Serbia|work=BBC News|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> and train lines from Serbia via Croatia to Slovenia were closed until further notice.

On 6 October 2015, 125,000 entered Croatia over the course of three weeks.<ref>{{cite news | title=If Germany Stops Receiving Refugees, Croatia Could Close Its Borders|url=http://www.total-croatia-news.com/news/1097-if-germany-stops-receiving-refugees-croatia-could-close-its-borders}}</ref> Between mid-September and mid-October 2015, about 200,000 migrants had passed through Croatia, with most moving on to Hungary.<ref name="HungaryCroatia2" /> On 17 October 2015, Hungary closed its border with Croatia to migrants, forcing migrants to be diverted to Slovenia instead.<ref name="HungaryCroatia2" /> However, Slovenia stated that it would only be able to admit 2,500 people per day with its population of only two million, stranding thousands of migrants in Croatia as well as Serbia and North Macedonia, while new migrants continued to add to the backlog.<ref name="CroatiaSlovenia3">{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/10/17/world/europe/ap-eu-europe-migrants.html|title=Thousands of Migrants Surge into Slovenia in New Route|agency=Associated Press|newspaper=The New York Times|date=18 October 2015|access-date=18 October 2015}}</ref><ref name="CroatiaSlovenia4">{{cite web|url=https://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/thousands-stranded-on-new-migrant-route-through-europe/ar-AAfAX74?li=AAa0dzB&ocid=mailsignout |title=Thousands stranded on new migrant route through Europe |author=Radul Radovanovic |publisher=The Associated Press, MSN |date=18 October 2015 |access-date=18 October 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151117031158/http://www.msn.com/en-us/news/world/thousands-stranded-on-new-migrant-route-through-europe/ar-AAfAX74?li=AAa0dzB&ocid=mailsignout |archive-date=17 November 2015 }}</ref>

In late December 2015, Slovenia erected a razor-wire fence on the border of the western Croatian regions of [[Istria]] and [[Gorski Kotar]], of which the latter is a habitat of the [[Eurasian lynx|lynx]] and the [[Eurasian brown bear|brown bear]], which are both endangered and protected by law in Croatia. Local hunters found deer killed by the fence, which led the [[World Wildlife Fund|WWF]] and the inhabitants of the regions from both sides of the border to protest against the decision to put up the razor-wire fence.<ref name="CroatiaSlovenia5">{{cite news|url=https://news.yahoo.com/slovenias-fence-croatia-border-threatening-wildlife-wwf-203307042.html|title=Slovenia's fence on Croatia border threatening wildlife: WWF|author=Yahoo News|agency=Agence France-Presse|date=18 December 2015|access-date=8 January 2016}}</ref><ref name="CroatiaSlovenia6">{{cite web|url=http://about.hr/news/croatia/istrians-protest-against-razor-wire-fence-croatia-slovenia-border-3925|title=Istrians protest against razor wire fence on Croatia-Slovenia border|author=Croatia|publisher=Hina|date=19 December 2015|access-date=8 January 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160202060746/https://about.hr/news/croatia/istrians-protest-against-razor-wire-fence-croatia-slovenia-border-3925|archive-date=2 February 2016|df=dmy-all}}</ref><ref name="CroatiaSlovenia7">{{cite web|url=http://about.hr/news/europe/protest-rally-against-razor-fence-slovenian-croatian-border-crossing-5450|title=Protest rally against razor fence at Slovenian-Croatian border crossing|author=Croatia|publisher=Hina|date=7 January 2016|access-date=8 January 2016|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160202045306/https://about.hr/news/europe/protest-rally-against-razor-fence-slovenian-croatian-border-crossing-5450|archive-date=2 February 2016|df=dmy-all}}</ref>

On 9 March 2016, Croatia started implementing border restrictions on the border with Serbia in an attempt to reinstate the Schengen rules.<ref name="CroatiaSlovenia8">{{cite web|url=http://www.newkerala.com/news/2016/fullnews-32348.html|title=Slovenia, Croatia, Serbia begin closure of Balkan route|author=New Kerala|date=9 March 2016|access-date=9 March 2016}}</ref> Since November 2016, [[Human Rights Watch]] (HRW) and, using video documentary evidence, notes that Croatia has been found to have forced refugees back to Serbia and Bosnia-Herzegovina in remote border locations, in contravention of the [[EU Charter of Fundamental Rights]] and the [[1951 Refugee Convention]], and subject them to extreme violence, including: pummelling people with fists, kicking them, making them run gauntlets between lines of police officers.<ref name="HRW1">{{cite news |title=EU: Address Croatia Border Pushbacks |url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2019/11/08/eu-address-croatia-border-pushbacks |access-date=19 November 2020 |work=Human Rights Watch |date=8 November 2019 |language=en}}</ref> Refugees also speak of forced stripping down to their underwear, beatings with branches, torture with stun guns, sexual abuse and torn-out toenails at the hands of masked Croatian police officers.<ref name="spiegel-18-11-20">{{cite news |last1=Vögele |first1=Nicole |last2=Lüdke |first2=Steffen |title=Croatia: Video Documents Illegal Refugee Pushbacks - DER SPIEGEL - International |url=https://www.spiegel.de/international/europe/croatia-video-documents-illegal-refugee-pushbacks-a-294b128d-4840-4d6b-9e96-3f879b0e69af |access-date=19 November 2020 |work=[[Der Spiegel]] |date=18 November 2020 |language=en}}</ref> Photos from aid organisations show refugees with bleeding lacerations, broken arms, knocked-out teeth and dark red marks on their backs.<ref name="spiegel-18-11-20"/> 

Although Croatia's foreign minister [[Gordan Grlić-Radman]] denies "all accusations of incorrect behaviour at the border", former director of police and interior minister [[Ranko Ostojić]] notes that video footage from ''[[Der Spiegel]]'' (in co-operation with Lighthouse Reports) suggests the masked policemen are retired police officers who are now part of the reserves;<ref name="spiegel-18-11-20"/> Jack Sapoch, from Border Violence Monitoring Network and a member of an NGO operating in Bosnia, says there is a spectrum of Croatian forces working along the border; "According to our research, these uniforms are consistent with those worn by the Croatian ministry of the interior's intervention police units, who are deployed to the border from police stations all over the country."<ref>{{cite news |title=Croatia denies migrant border attacks after new reports of brutal pushbacks |url=https://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2020/oct/23/croatia-denies-migrant-border-attacks-after-new-reports-of-brutal-pushbacks |access-date=19 November 2020 |work=[[The Guardian]] |date=23 October 2020 |language=en}}</ref> The [[United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees]] (UNHCR), the [[Council of Europe]]'s [[Commissioner for Human Rights]], and other nongovernmental organisations have echoed HRW's concerns.<ref name="HRW1"/> The [[European Commission]] has been accused of [[coverup]] with regard to these crimes, as the [[European Union]] agreed to give Croatia €6.8m to strengthen its border protection programmes with non-EU countries;<ref name="TondoBoffey">{{cite news |last1=Tondo |first1=Lorenzo |last2=Boffey |first2=Daniel |title=EU 'covered up' Croatia's failure to protect migrants from border brutality |url=https://www.theguardian.com/global-development/2020/jun/15/eu-covered-up-croatias-failure-to-protect-migrants-from-border-brutality |access-date=19 November 2020 |work=The Guardian |date=15 June 2020}}</ref> Croatian ministers say that money was handed over to the [[UN High Commission for Refugees]] (UNHCR) and the Croatian Law Centre, although neither organisation says it received any money.<ref name="TondoBoffey"/>

===Czech Republic===
The Czech Republic received 4,306 refugees according to quotas accepted by the [[European Commission]].<ref>{{cite news |title=MAPPED: How many refugees each European country will take under EU plans |url=http://www.express.co.uk/news/world/607349/Migrant-crisis-map-EU-refugee-quota |access-date=23 September 2015 |work=[[Daily Express]] |date=22 September 2015}}</ref> [[Prime Minister of the Czech Republic|Prime Minister]] [[Bohuslav Sobotka]] said the [[European Commission]] had failed in solving the crisis and disagreed with proposed quotas, saying: "We reject the system of quotas. I do not consider it effective, I do not think it would help bring any solution. It makes no sense to discuss any numbers for now". He said Europe needed to complete what the [[European Council]] had agreed upon in the past and to refrain from creating new plans and proposals. He supported the idea of creating hotspots in Italy or Greece.<ref>{{cite news |title=EC failed in solving migration, quotas make no sense – Czech PM |url=http://www.ceskenoviny.cz/news/zpravy/ec-failed-in-solving-migration-quotas-make-no-sense-czech-pm/1255977 |access-date=13 September 2015 |publisher=[[ČTK]] |date=8 September 2015}}</ref> Czech President [[Miloš Zeman]] expressed his dissatisfaction with the mass influx of migrants to Europe on several occasions; in late August 2015, he said in an interview for radio station "Frekvence 1": "The reception of migrants from the Middle East and Northern Africa to the territory of Czech Republic [brought] with it three major risks – spread of infectious diseases, terrorism of the Islamic state and the creation of new ghettos." According to his opinion the majority of refugees are actually economic migrants who are not fleeing war. Zeman also believed that migrants crossing Czech territory to go to Germany will stay in Czech Republic when Germany eventually stops accepting them, "which would then make Czech Republic to defend its boundaries with the police and army".<ref>{{cite web |title=President cites disease, terrorist sleeper cells as causes for concern |url=http://www.praguepost.com/czech-news/49528-zeman-refugees-should-be-promptly-returned |website=The Prague Post |access-date=5 September 2015}}</ref>

Czech Deputy Prime Minister [[Andrej Babiš]] called for [[NATO]] intervention against human trafficking in the Mediterranean.<ref>"[http://www.radio.cz/en/section/news/finance-minister-andrej-babis-calls-on-nato-to-destroy-human-smugglers-ships Finance Minister Andrej Babiš calls on NATO to destroy human smugglers' ships]". Radio Prague. 9 September 2015.</ref> After talks with NATO Secretary General [[Jens Stoltenberg]] on the migrant crisis issue he said: "NATO is not interested in refugees, though Turkey, a NATO member, is their entrance gate to Europe and smugglers operate on Turkish territory".<ref name="CN">"[http://www.ceskenoviny.cz/news/zpravy/czech-minister-babis-criticises-nato-s-stance-on-refugees/1256815 Czech minister Babis criticises NATO´s stance on refugees]". CeskeNoviny.cz. 10 September 2015.</ref> [[Miroslav Kalousek]] from the opposition party [[TOP 09]] said that "confident and wealthy countries such as the [[Czech Republic]] should not be afraid to accept 3,000 refugees" and accused Zeman of inciting hatred against refugees, though he also disagreed with proposed quotas.<ref>{{cite news |title=Kalousek: Sebevědomá země jako Česko by se neměla bát tří tisíc uprchlíků |language=cs |url=http://www.ceskatelevize.cz/ct24/domaci/1582002-kalousek-sebevedoma-zeme-jako-cesko-se-nemela-bat-tri-tisic-uprchliku |access-date=13 September 2015 |publisher=[[ČT24]] |date=10 September 2015}}</ref> Former [[Minister of Foreign Affairs of the Czech Republic|Minister of Foreign Affairs]] [[Karel Schwarzenberg]] said that accepting 80,000 refugees would be suitable.<ref>{{cite news |title=Karel Schwarzenberg: Řveme, jako by nám uprchlíci řezali krky |language=cs |url=http://nazory.euro.e15.cz/rozhovory/karel-schwarzenberg-rveme-jako-by-nam-uprchlici-rezali-krky-1226853 |access-date=15 September 2015 |publisher=Mladá fronta E15 |date=14 September 2015}}</ref> Minister of Human Rights and Equal Opportunities [[Jiří Dienstbier Jr.|Jiří Dienstbier]] said the country was able to accept 7,000 to 15,000 refugees and should express solidarity and help other countries facing the strongest influx of refugees without quotas.<ref>{{cite news |title=Czech Republic can accept 7,000–15,000 refugees now – minister |url=http://www.ceskenoviny.cz/news/zpravy/czech-republic-can-accept-7-000-15-000-refugees-now-minister/1259195 |access-date=16 September 2015 |publisher=[[ČTK]] |date=16 September 2015}}</ref>

===Denmark===
Denmark temporarily closed rail links with Germany and the [[European route E45|E45 Motorway]] in September to stop migrants from illegally entering the country.<ref>"[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34203366 Migrant crisis: Denmark-Germany rail links suspended]". BBC News. 9 September 2015.</ref> Denmark had the second highest amount on asylum seekers among European nations in 2015, compared to [[GDP]] (0.47 percent of GDP, after Sweden at 0.5 percent, followed by Germany and Italy at 0.2 percent, with remaining lower),<ref name=IMFCost>{{cite web | title=The Refugee Surge in Europe: Economic Challenges | website=[[IMF]] | date=16 January 2016 | url=https://www.imf.org/external/pubs/ft/sdn/2016/sdn1602.pdf | access-date=26 December 2015|author1=S. Aiyar |author2=B. Barkbu |author3=N. Batini |author4=H. Berger |author5=E. Detragiache |author-link5= Enrica Detragiache |author6=A. Dizioli |author7=C. Ebeke |author8=H. Lin |author9=L. Kaltani |author10=S. Sosa |author11=A. Spilimbergo |author12=P. Topalova }}</ref> which rose in 2016.<ref name=IMFCost/> In December 2015, the Danish government announced that it would introduce a new law that would allow the government to confiscate cash above 3,000 [[Danish krone|DKK]] (roughly €402) and valuables worth more than 3,000 DKK from asylum seekers to pay the cost of their stay. Items of sentimental value (such as [[wedding ring]]s, personal [[mobile phone]]s and personal [[laptop]]s) would not be taken.<ref name="The Independent DK 2015">{{cite news | title=Denmark has responded to critics of its plan to strip jewellery from refugees | website=The Independent | date=22 December 2015 | url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europerefugee-crisis-denmark-government-defends-plan-to-strip-refugees-valuables-to-pay-for-their-stay-a6782916.html | access-date=22 December 2015|author=Emma Henderson}}</ref> In January 2016, the limit was changed to 10,000 DKK (roughly €1,340) before the law passed.<ref name=TheLocal15>{{cite web | title=As Danes debate, Swiss already seizing refugees' cash | website=The Local | date=15 January 2016 | url=http://www.thelocal.dk/20160115/as-danes-debate-swiss-already-seizing-refugees-cash | access-date=25 January 2016|author=Nina Larson/AFP}}</ref><ref name=TheLocal26>{{cite web | title=Denmark passes controversial bill to take migrants' valuables | website=The Local | date=26 January 2016 | url=http://www.thelocal.dk/20160126/danish-parliament-to-vote-on-controversial-migrant-bill | access-date=26 January 2016|author=Sören Billing/AFP}}</ref> Similar laws already existed in Switzerland (limit 1,000 Swiss francs (roughly €913)),<ref name=TheLocal15/> the Netherlands (limit €5,895)<ref>{{cite web | title=Holland kan også inddrage asylansøgeres værdigenstande | website=Jyllands Posten | date=26 January 2016 | url=http://jyllands-posten.dk/international/europa/ECE8393704/holland-kan-ogsaa-inddrage-asylansoegeres-vaerdigenstande/| access-date=26 January 2016|author=Ritzau}}</ref><ref>{{cite web | title=Netherlands claimed more than £500,000 from refugees in four years | website=The Guardian | date=25 January 2016 | url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jan/25/netherlands-claimed-500000-from-refugees-cost-of-living| access-date=26 January 2016|author=Gordon Darroch}}</ref> and some [[States of Germany|federal states of Germany]] (limit varies, €750 in [[Bavaria]] and €350 in [[Baden-Württemberg]]).<ref>{{cite web | title=Tyskland tager også flygtninges penge | website=Politiken | date=22 January 2016 | url=http://politiken.dk/udland/fokus_int/Flygtningestroem/ECE3028305/tyskland-tager-ogsaa-flygtninges-penge/| access-date=25 January 2016|author=Erik Jensen}}</ref> The law was condemned from several sides, including the UNHCR,<ref name=TheLocal26/><ref name="Channel 4 News 2015">{{cite web | title=Yes, Denmark really wants to strip refugees of jewellery | website=Channel 4 News | date=18 December 2015 | url=http://www.channel4.com/news/yes-denmark-really-wants-to-strip-refugees-of-jewellery | access-date=22 December 2015|quote=The UN refugee agency UNHCR told Channel 4 News the idea "beggars belief.}}</ref> and caused Danish politician [[Jens Rohde]] to defect from the [[Venstre (Denmark)|Venstre]] party to the [[Danish Social Liberal Party|Social Liberal Party]].<ref name="Zawadzki Dec 2015">{{cite web | last=Zawadzki | first=Sabina | title=Danish MEP quits party over plan to take refugee valuables | website=Reuters | date=20 December 2015 | url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-denmark-idUSKBN0U30EE20151220 | access-date=28 March 2016}}</ref> The Danish police said that this could not be enforced<ref name="DW.COM 2015">{{cite web | title=Danish police refuse to seize refugee jewelry and cash – News – 22.12.2015 | website=DW.COM | date=22 December 2015 | url=http://www.dw.com/en/danish-policerefuse-to-seizerefugee-jewelry-and-cash/a-18934564 | access-date=22 December 2015}}</ref> and a review two months after the law came into effect showed that there had been no confiscations.<ref>{{cite web | title=Loven der satte Danmark på alverdens forsider er aldrig blevet brugt | website=nyheder.tv2.dk | date=5 April 2016 | url=http://nyheder.tv2.dk/krimi/2016-04-05-loven-der-satte-danmark-pa-alverdens-forsider-er-aldrig-blevet-brugt | access-date=5 April 2016}}</ref>

On 6 September 2015, large groups of migrants who declined to apply for asylum in Germany began passing the Danish borders, with most heading for Sweden.<ref name=Denm1>{{cite news|url=http://jyllands-posten.dk/politik/ECE8091454/Overblik%3A+Det+skete+da+flygtningestr%C3%B8mmen+n%C3%A5ede+Danmark/ |title=Overblik: Det skete da flygtningestrømmen nåede Danmark |newspaper=[[Jyllands-Posten]] |date=7 October 2015 |access-date=19 November 2015 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151014024126/http://jyllands-posten.dk/politik/ECE8091454/Overblik%3A+Det+skete+da+flygtningestr%C3%B8mmen+n%C3%A5ede+Danmark/ |archive-date=14 October 2015 }}</ref> Initially the Danish police attempted to register all migrants in accordance with EU rules, but many refused, resulting in a fight of about 50 people on 9 September at the [[Padborg station|Padborg rail station]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/10/world/europe/migrants-refugee-tensions-in-europe.html|title=Migrant Tide Bringing Out Europe's Best and Worst |author=Melissa Eddy |newspaper=The New York Times |date=9 September 2015 |access-date=9 September 2015}}</ref><ref name=Denm2>{{cite news |url=http://nyhederne.tv2.dk/krimi/2015-09-09-motorvej-spaerret-i-begge-retninger-flygtninge-gaar-fra-padborg-mod-sverige |title=Motorvej spærret i begge retninger: Flygtninge går fra Padborg mod Sverige |author=Melissa Eddy |newspaper=[[TV 2 (Denmark)|TV2 News Denmark]] |date= 9 September 2015|access-date=19 November 2015 }}</ref>

On 9 September 2015, Denmark suspended all rail and ferry links with Germany for one day. On the same day parts of the [[European route E45|E45]] motorway was closed to vehicles to avoid accidents as hundreds of migrants were walking along it in southern [[Jutland]] towards Sweden;<ref name="Denm2" /> it was reopened a few hours later.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://politiken.dk/udland/fokus_int/Flygtningestroem/ECE2834738/flygtninge-drejer-af-den-soenderjyske-motorvej-er-nu-genaabnet/ |title=Flygtninge drejer af: Den sønderjyske motorvej er nu genåbnet |author=Kristian Corfixen |newspaper=[[Politiken]] |date= 9 September 2015|access-date=19 November 2015 }}</ref> After initial uncertainty surrounding the rules, Denmark decided that migrants continuing onwards to other [[Nordic countries]] and refusing to seek asylum in Denmark would be allowed to pass.<ref name="Denm1" /> In the five weeks following 6 September alone, approximately 28,800 migrants passed the Danish borders. 3,500 of them applied for asylum in Denmark and the rest continued to other Nordic countries.<ref name="Denm3">{{cite news |url=http://nyhederne.tv2.dk/2015-10-12-28800-flygtninge-og-migranter-er-kommet-til-danmark-paa-fem-uger |title=28.800 flygtninge og migranter er kommet til Danmark på fem uger |author=Jonas Hamidavi R. Moestrup |newspaper= [[TV 2 (Denmark)|TV2 News Denmark]] |date= 12 October 2015|access-date=19 November 2015 }}</ref>

When Sweden introduced ID checks at the Danish border to prevent undocumented migrants from coming to Sweden, Denmark reintroduced border controls on the [[Denmark–Germany border|Danish-German border]] in January 2016 to avoid an accumulation of illegal migrants on their way to Sweden.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.politiko.dk/nyheder/regeringen-indfoerer-midlertidig-graensekontrol-til-tyskland|title=Regeringen indfører midlertidig grænsekontrol til Tyskland |website=politiko.dk |access-date=22 January 2016|date=4 January 2016}}</ref> The border control remains as of December 2019.

In October 2017 the Danish migration agency ''Udlændingestyrelsen'' rejected over 600 asylum applications because the applicants had lied about their national identity to receive preferential treatment.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.dr.dk/nyheder/politik/over-600-asylansoegere-faar-afslag-efter-snyd-med-deres-identitet|title=Over 600 asylansøgere får afslag efter snyd med deres identitet|work=DR|access-date=12 October 2017|language=da}}</ref>

===Finland===
{{Main|European migrant crisis (Finland)}}
Many migrants arrived over the land border from Sweden. They were stopped from using ferries by carrier's responsibility rules. On 14 September, former prime minister [[Matti Vanhanen]] noted that the government needed to regain control on who was entering the country and divert asylum seekers to special camps. He did not think that it would be appropriate for asylum seekers to continue freely moving around.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.uusisuomi.fi/kotimaa/113969-matti-vanhanen-suomi-valmistautuu-rajatarkastuksiin-syy-loytyy-pohjois-suomesta|title=Matti Vanhanen: Suomi valmistautuu rajatarkastuksiin – syy löytyy Pohjois-Suomesta |work=Uusi Suomi|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> On the same day, the Minister of the Interior [[Petteri Orpo]], a member of the National Coalition Party, noted that tighter border controls would be imposed on the northern border stations by the end of the week.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.iltasanomat.fi/kotimaa/art-1442202525958.html|title=Orpo: Pohjois-Suomeen tehostettu rajavalvonta|author=STT-IS|work=Ilta-Sanomat|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> On 14 November 2015 Finnish prime minister [[Juha Sipilä]] noted that border controls needed to be tightened and expressed his concern that the Schengen Agreement and freedom of movement was not working. He stressed that border controls would be restored if the Schengen agreement was not amended.
