He also stated that the Finnish National Bureau of Investigation will improve its cyber surveillance.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.iltasanomat.fi/kotimaa/art-1447477033932.html|title=Sipilä: Rajavalvontaa tiivistetään – vapaa liikkuvuus ei toimi|author=IS|work=Ilta-Sanomat}}</ref> On the same day Finnish President [[Sauli Niinistö]] (elected from the National Coalition Party) noted that national solutions needed to be made if the Schengen agreement could not enforced again.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.uusisuomi.fi/kotimaa/139133-presidentti-niinisto-hurjan-ennustuksensa-toteutumisesta-valitettavasti-silla-tiella|title=Presidentti Niinistö hurjan ennustuksensa toteutumisesta: "Valitettavasti sillä tiellä ollaan" |work=Uusi Suomi}}</ref> On 13 September 2015, local authorities reported a daily estimate of 300 asylum seekers entering via the northern land [[Finnish–Swedish border|border from Sweden]] into [[Tornio]], which is the main route of migration flow into [[Finland]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.iltalehti.fi/uutiset/2015091320344649_uu.shtml|title=Turvapaikanhakijoiden määrä räjähti Torniossa: "Satoja tullut tänään" | author=Sami Koski | work=Iltalehti | date=2015-09-13 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref> The total number of asylum seekers for the year was reported to be over 2.6 times the total amount for the whole of 2014.<ref>{{cite web | url=http://www.iltalehti.fi/uutiset/2015091420349291_uu.shtml | title=Viime viikolla ennätyksellinen määrä turvapaikanhakijoita | author=Olli Waris | work=Iltalehti | date=2015-09-14 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref> During October 2015, 7,058 new asylum seekers arrived in Finland. In mid-October the number of asylum seekers entering Finland during 2015 reached 27,000, which is the fourth-largest number in Europe in terms of country size.<ref name=yle>{{cite news | title=Interior Ministry: Finland set to reject two thirds of asylum seekers | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/interior_ministry_finland_set_to_reject_two_thirds_of_asylum_seekers/8446795 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-11-11 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref> In late November, the number passed 30,000.<ref>{{cite news | title=Eurajoki resorting to containers to house asylum seekers | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/eurajoki_resorting_to_shipping_containers_to_house_asylum_seekers/8455009 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-11-13 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref><ref name=yle3>{{cite news | title=Reception centres use containers to house new arrivals | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/reception_centres_use_containers_to_house_new_arrivals/8486826 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-11-28 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref>

More than 60 percent of asylum seekers who arrived during 2015 came from [[Iraq]].<ref name=yle2>{{ cite news | title=Disappointed Iraqis cancel asylum applications | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/disappointed_iraqis_cancel_asylum_applications/8479598 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-11-24 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref> In late October, the Finnish Immigration Service (Migri) changed its guidelines about areas in Iraq which are recognized as safe by the Finnish authorities<ref name=yle2 /> and put Iraqi asylum seekers under closer scrutiny.<ref>{{cite news | title=Finland adopts one-stop approach to slash asylum processing queues | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/finland_adopts_one-stop_approach_to_slash_asylum_processing_queues/8420646 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-11-30 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref> Orpo estimated that two in three asylum seekers came to Finland in hopes of a higher standard of living. In November, the Permanent Secretary of the Interior Ministry stated that approximately 60 to 65 percent of the recent applications for asylum were to be denied.<ref name=yle />

In September, the processing time of an asylum application was estimated to have extended from six months to two years.<ref>{{cite news | title=Turvapaikkahakemusten käsittelyajat venyvät – "Täällä on tuhansia turvapaikanhakijoita monta vuotta" | url=http://yle.fi/uutiset/turvapaikkahakemusten_kasittelyajat_venyvat__taalla_on_tuhansia_turvapaikanhakijoita_monta_vuotta/8295512 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-09-10 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref> In late November, the reception centers were reported to be running out of space, which forced authorities to resort to refurbished [[Intermodal container|shipping containers]] and tents to house new asylum seekers.<ref name=yle3 /> Orpo announced that special repatriation centers would be established. These centers would be inhabited by denied asylum seekers. While he stressed that these camps would not be prisons, he described the inhabitants would be under strict surveillance.<ref>{{cite news|title=Interior Minister: Finland to set up asylum seeker repatriation centres | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/interior_minister_finland_to_set_up_asylum_seeker_repatriation_centres/8502217 | work=[[YLE]] | date=2015-12-03 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref>

In January 2016, [[Yle]], Finland's national public-broadcasting company, reported that a [[Russia]]n border guard had admitted that the Russian [[Federal Security Service]] was enabling migrants to enter Finland.<ref>{{cite news | url=https://yle.fi/uutiset/osasto/news/russian_border_guard_to_stt_russian_security_service_behind_northeast_asylum_traffic/8620174 | title=Russian border guard to STT: Russian security service behind northeast asylum traffic | work=[[YLE]] | date=2016-01-24 | access-date=2017-12-13 }}</ref>

In 2017, hundreds of Muslim asylum seekers from [[Iraq]] and [[Afghanistan]] converted to Christianity after having had their first asylum application rejected by the Finnish Immigration Service (Migri) to re-apply for asylum on the grounds of religious persecution.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://svenska.yle.fi/artikel/2017/10/04/stort-finlandskt-fenomen-hundratals-muslimer-blir-kristna|title=Stort finländskt fenomen – hundratals muslimer blir kristna|date=4 October 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180421104613/https://svenska.yle.fi/artikel/2017/10/04/stort-finlandskt-fenomen-hundratals-muslimer-blir-kristna|archive-date=21 April 2018}}</ref>

===France===
On 23 September 2015, after the Czech Republic, Hungary, Romania and Slovakia voted against a plan to relocate asylum-seekers arriving in Greece, Italy, and Hungary among other member states, French President [[François Hollande|Hollande]] warned the four former [[Eastern Bloc]] countries against rejecting the EU mandatory migrant quotas: "Those who don't share our values, those who don't even want to respect those principles, need to start asking themselves questions about their place in the European Union."<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.ibtimes.co.uk/migrant-crisis-hungarian-pm-viktor-orban-proposes-eu-border-force-patrol-greek-frontier-1520934 |title=Migrant crisis: Hungarian PM Viktor Orban proposes EU border force to patrol Greek frontier |work=[[International Business Times]] |date=23 September 2015}}</ref>
[[File:Migrants at Eastern Railway Station - Keleti, 2015.09.04 (1).jpg|thumb|Migrants in Budapest railway station, with most heading to Germany, 4 September 2015]]

[[File:Calais2015k.jpg|thumb|Sudanese migrants in Calais, October 2015]]
Migrants entering France illegally by train were returned to Italy by French police when border controls were introduced in July 2015.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/07/21/world/europe/migrants-journeys-stall-in-italy-near-the-french-border.html|title=Migrants' Journeys Stall in Italy, Near the French Border|date=22 July 2015|work=The New York Times|access-date=22 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.yahoo.com/top-french-court-approves-border-controls-italy-173759866.html|title=Top French court approves border controls with Italy|date=29 June 2015|work=Yahoo News|access-date=22 January 2016}}</ref> Due to "poor housing", lower social benefits, and a thorough asylum application process, France is not considered attractive enough to seek asylum in.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/france/11880391/Refugees-shun-France-land-of-red-tape-unemployment-and-poor-housing.html|title=EU migrant crisis: Refugees shun France over red tape, unemployment and poor housing – Telegraph|date=21 September 2015|work=Telegraph.co.uk|access-date=22 January 2016|last1=Samuel|first1=Henry}}</ref> As such many of them tried to enter the [[United Kingdom]], resulting in camps of [[migrants around Calais]] where one of the [[Eurotunnel]] entrances is located. In the summer of 2015, at least nine people died in attempts to reach Britain, including falling from trains, being hit by trains, or drowning in a canal at the Eurotunnel entrance.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://time.com/3980758/calais-migrant-eurotunnel-deaths/ |title=Why Thousands of Migrants Are Risking Their Lives at Calais |author=Naina Bajekal/Calais |work=Time |access-date=28 August 2015 |date=1 August 2015}}</ref> Migrants from the camps also attempted to enter trucks bound for the UK, with some truck drivers being threatened by migrants, and cargo being stolen or damaged.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2015/jul/05/calais-lorry-drivers-need-more-protection-migrants|title=Calais drivers need more protection from migrants, says lorry group|author=Haroon Siddique|newspaper=the Guardian|access-date=22 January 2016|date=5 July 2015}}</ref>

In response, a UK-financed fence was built along the A-216 highway in [[Calais]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-33833536|title=Will new mile-long Calais fence stop migrants?|work=BBC News|access-date=22 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/refugee-crisis-hundreds-of-migrants-storm-calais-motorway-attempting-to-board-lorries-heading-to-the-a6775346.html|title=Refugee crisis: Hundreds of migrants storm Calais motorway attempting to board lorries heading to the UK|author=Lizzie Dearden|date=16 December 2015|work=The Independent|access-date=22 January 2016}}</ref> At the camp near Calais, known as the ''[[Calais Jungle|Jungle]]'', riots broke out when authorities began demolishing the illegally constructed campsite on 29 January 2015.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Chrisafis|first1=Angelique|last2=Walker|first2=Peter|last3=Quinn|first3=Ben|title=Calais 'Jungle' camp: clashes as authorities demolish homes|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/feb/29/french-authorities-begin-clearance-of-part-of-calais-jungle-camp|newspaper=The Guardian|access-date=7 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307205334/http://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/feb/29/french-authorities-begin-clearance-of-part-of-calais-jungle-camp|archive-date=7 March 2016|date=1 March 2016}}</ref> Amid the protests, which included hunger strikes, thousands of refugees living in the camp were relocated to France's "first international-standard refugee camp" at the [[La Liniere refugee camp]] in [[Grande-Synthe]] which replaced the previous [[Basroch refugee camp]].<ref>{{cite news|title=Nach Räumung des "Dschungels": Frankreich eröffnet neues Flüchtlingslager am Ärmelkanal|url=http://www.spiegel.de/politik/ausland/grande-synthe-frankreich-eroeffnet-fluechtlingslager-am-aermelkanal-a-1081052.html|newspaper=Spiegel Online|access-date=7 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307210038/http://www.spiegel.de/politik/ausland/grande-synthe-frankreich-eroeffnet-fluechtlingslager-am-aermelkanal-a-1081052.html|archive-date=7 March 2016|language=de|date=7 March 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=France opens new refugee camp, amid protest|url=http://www.euronews.com/2016/03/07/france-opens-new-refugee-camp-amid-protest/|website=euronews.com|access-date=7 March 2016|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307205734/http://www.euronews.com/2016/03/07/france-opens-new-refugee-camp-amid-protest/|archive-date=7 March 2016|date=7 March 2016}}</ref>

===Germany===
{{See also|Asylum in Germany|Angela Merkel#Domestic policy}}
Junior coalition partner, Vice Chancellor [[Sigmar Gabriel]] said that Germany could take in 500,000 refugees annually for the next several years.<ref>"[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34185353 Migrant crisis: Germany 'can take 500,000 asylum seekers a year']". BBC News. 8 September 2015.</ref> German opposition to the government's admission of the new wave of migrants was strong and coupled with a rise in anti-immigration protests.<ref name=Hill>{{cite news |last1=Hill |first1=Jenny |title=Immigration fuels rising tension in Germany |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-33700624 |access-date=18 August 2015 |publisher=BBC |date=30 July 2013}}</ref> [[Pegida]], an anti-immigration movement flourished briefly in late 2014, followed by a new wave of anti-immigration protests in the late summer of 2015.<ref name=Fenton>{{cite news |last1=Fenton |first1=Siobhan |title=Pegida |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/german-farright-extremists-clash-with-police-in-protest-outside-dresden-refugee-camp-10415880.html |access-date=18 August 2015 |work=The Independent |date=25 July 2015 |location=London}}</ref> Merkel insisted that Germany had the economic strength to cope with the influx of migrants and reiterated that there is no legal maximum limit on the number of migrants Germany can take.<ref>{{cite web |title=Germany: 'No Limit' To Refugees We'll Take In |url=http://news.sky.com/story/1547326/germany-no-limit-to-refugees-well-take-in |publisher=Sky News |access-date=6 September 2015 |date=5 September 2015}}</ref> In September 2015, enthusiastic crowds across the country welcomed arriving refugees and migrants.<ref>{{cite web |title=Germans welcome thousands of newly arrived refugees |url=http://www.dw.com/en/germans-welcome-thousands-of-newly-arrived-refugees/a-18696722 |publisher=Deutsche Welle |date=6 September 2015}}</ref>

[[Horst Seehofer]], leader of the [[Christian Social Union in Bavaria]] (CSU){{Em dash}}the sister party of Merkel's [[Christian Democratic Union of Germany|Christian Democratic Union]]{{Em dash}}and then-[[Bavaria]]n Minister President, attacked Merkel's policies,<ref name="auto">{{cite news |title=Merkel splits conservative bloc with green light to refugees |url=http://uk.reuters.com/article/2015/09/06/uk-europe-migrants-germany-criticism-idUKKCN0R60T920150906 |work=Reuters |date=6 September 2015}}</ref> threatened to sue the government in high court, and hinted that the CSU might topple Merkel.{{citation needed|date=July 2019}} Many MPs from Merkel's CDU party also voiced dissatisfaction with Merkel. Seehofer criticised Merkel's decision to allow in migrants, saying that "[they were] in a state of mind without rules, without system and without order because of a German decision."<ref>"[http://www.politico.eu/article/viktor-orban-bavaria-hardline-hero-seehofer-migration-borders/ Viktor Orbán, Bavaria's hardline hero]". ''[[Politico]]''. 23 September 2015.</ref> Seehofer estimated as many as 30 percent of asylum seekers arriving in Germany claiming to be from Syria are in fact from other countries,<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/11891219/Refugee-crisis-Many-migrants-falsely-claim-to-be-Syrians-Germany-says-as-EU-tries-to-ease-tensions.html Refugee crisis: Many migrants falsely claim to be Syrians, Germany says as EU tries to ease tensions]". ''[[The Daily Telegraph]]''. 25 September 2015.</ref> and suggested to reduce EU funding for member countries that rejected mandatory refugee quotas.<ref>"[http://www.dw.com/en/berlin-calls-for-sanctions-on-eu-states-that-reject-refugee-quotas/a-18714957 Berlin calls for sanctions on EU states that reject refugee quotas]". [[Deutsche Welle]]. 15 September 2015.</ref> The Bavarian Interior Minister [[Joachim Herrmann (CSU)|Joachim Herrmann]] (CSU) accused the Berlin government of pushing its policy forward without consulting the federal states, which would have had to cope with the consequences.<ref name="auto"/>

Meanwhile, [[Yasmin Fahimi]], secretary-general of the [[Social Democratic Party of Germany|Social Democratic Party]] (SPD), the junior partner of the ruling coalition, praised Merkel's policy allowing migrants in Hungary to enter Germany as "a strong signal of humanity to show that Europe's values are valid also in difficult times".<ref name="auto"/> [[North Rhine-Westphalia]], Germany's most populous state, was hiring more than 3,600 new teachers to manage the influx of an estimated 40,000 new refugee children in 2015.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/24/world/europe/where-therefugees-pour-into-germany-a-24-hour-window.html|title=Where the Refugees Pour into Germany, a 24-Hour Window|author=Alison Smale|newspaper=The New York Times|date=23 September 2015|access-date=24 September 2015}}</ref>

In November 2015, there were talks inside the governing coalition to stop family unification for migrants for two years, and to establish "Transit Zones" on the border and – for migrants with low chances to get asylum approved – to be housed there until their application is approved. The issues are in conflict between the CSU who favoured those new measures and threatened to leave the coalition without them, and the SPD who opposes them; Merkel agreed to the measures.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dw.com/en/germany-coalition-split-on-transit-zones/av-18824248|title=Germany: Coalition split on transit zones|work=DW.COM|access-date=4 November 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151104013756/http://www.dw.com/en/germany-coalition-split-on-transit-zones/av-18824248|archive-date=4 November 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref> The [[November 2015 Paris attacks]] prompted a reevaluation of German officials' stance on the EU's policy toward migrants.<ref name=ParisAttacksMigrants>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/aponline/2015/11/14/world/europe/ap-eu-germany-migrants-rising-tensions.html|title=Paris Attacks Provoke Fresh Migrant Fears in Europe|author=Eldar Emric, Demetri Nellas, and the Associated Press|newspaper=The New York Times|date=14 November 2015|access-date=14 November 2015}}</ref> There appeared to be a consensus among officials, with the exception of Merkel, that a higher level of scrutiny was needed in vetting migrants with respect to their mission in Germany.<ref name=ParisAttacksMigrants/> However, while not officially limiting the influx numerically, Merkel tightened asylum policy in Germany.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/29/world/europe/merkel-whilerefusing-to-halt-migrant-influx-works-to-limit-it.html?ref=Europe|title=Merkel, While Refusing to Halt Migrant Influx, Works to Limit It|author=Alison Smale|newspaper=The New York Times|date=28 November 2015|access-date=28 November 2015}}</ref>

[[File:Drehscheibe Köln-Bonn Airport - Ankunft Flüchtlinge 5. Oktober 2015-0308.jpg|thumb|Migrants in Germany, October 2015]]
[[Germany]]'s asylum practice is generally based on article 16a of its [[Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany|Basic Law]], as well as international regulations like the [[Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees]]<ref>Deutscher Bundestag: ''Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany'', print version in English, November 2012 ([https://www.bundestag.de/blob/284870/ce0d03414872b427e57fccb703634dcd/basic_law-data.pdf PDF] {{webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304075359/https://www.bundestag.de/blob/284870/ce0d03414872b427e57fccb703634dcd/basic_law-data.pdf |date=4 March 2016 }})</ref> Germany has been the most sought-after final destination in the EU migrant and refugee crisis.<ref name="auto6"/><ref name="auto7"/> Between January and December 2015, 1,091,894 arrivals of asylum seekers were registered in Germany's "EASY" system for the first distribution of asylum seekers among Germany's federal states; however, there were only 476,649 asylum applications in 2015, because many asylum seekers had not formally applied for asylum yet or did not stop in Germany and moved on to other EU states.<ref>{{cite web|title=2015: Mehr Asylanträge in Deutschland als jemals zuvor|url=http://www.bmi.bund.de/SharedDocs/Pressemitteilungen/DE/2016/01/asylantraege-dezember-2015.html|publisher=BMI|date=6 January 2016}}</ref>

Germany has a quota system to distribute asylum seekers among [[States of Germany|all German states]],<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/07/world/german-quota-system-highlights-possible-path-and-pitfalls-for-handling-crisis.html|title=German Quota System Highlights Possible Path and Pitfalls for Handling Crisis |author1=Katrin Bennhold |author2=Melissa Eddy |newspaper=The New York Times |access-date=6 September 2015 |date=6 September 2015}}</ref> but in September 2015 the federal states, responsible for accommodation, criticised the government in [[Berlin]] for not providing enough help to them.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.spiegel.de/politik/deutschland/innenminister-warnen-vor-noch-mehr-fluechtlingen-a-1052575.html |title=Länderinnenminister: "Sie öffnen die Grenzen und lassen uns im Stich" |author=Melanie Amann, Matthias Gebauer und Horand Knaup |newspaper=Der Spiegel |access-date=11 September 2015 |date=11 September 2015 }}</ref>

The Interior Minister announced on 13 September 2015 the introduction of temporary controls on the southern border with Austria and explained the measure with reference to ''security concerns''.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/14/world/europe/germany-emergency-measures-european-migrant-crisis.html|title=Germany Announces Emergency Border Controls Amid Migrant Crisis|author1=Melissa Eddy |author2=Alison Smale |newspaper=The New York Times |access-date=13 September 2015 |date=13 September 2015}}</ref>
The restrictions incorporated a temporary suspension of rail travel from Austria and allowed spot checks on automobiles.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.euronews.com/2015/09/13/germany-introduces-temporary-controls-along-austrian-border/|title=Germany introduces 'temporary' controls along Austrian border|publisher=euronews|date=13 September 2015|access-date=13 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/14/world/europe/germany-emergency-measures-european-migrant-crisis.html|title=Germany Orders Curbs at Border in Migrant Crisis|author1=Melissa Eddy |author2=Rick Lyman |author3=Alison Smale |newspaper=The New York Times|date=13 September 2015|access-date=13 September 2015}}</ref> In September 2019, following the rise in the number of migrants reaching Italy after having been rescued from drowning by activists, Interior Minister Horst Seehofer said that Germany would accept one in four migrants previously rescued and brought to Italy.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.tagesspiegel.de/politik/verteilung-von-fluechtlingen-in-europa-bundesregierung-pocht-auf-langfristige-solidarische-loesung/25021288.html|title=Bundesregierung pocht auf langfristige "solidarische" Lösung|access-date=16 September 2019|website=Tagesspiegel}}</ref>

On 5 October, the German [[Tabloid journalism|tabloid]] [[Bild]] claimed to possess a secret document stating that the number of asylum seekers would increase to 1.5 million by the end of 2015. This report was immediately disclaimed by the German ministry of the interior which restated its own estimate of 800,000 applicants.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.bild.de/politik/inland/fluechtlingskrise/fluechtlingskrise-deutsche-behoerden-warnen-vor-zusammenbruch-der-versorgung-42892328.bild.html|title=Behörden warnen in der Flüchtlingskrise: Zusammenbruch der Versorgung droht|author=FRANZ SOLMS-LAUBACH und PETER TIEDE|work=Bild|access-date=8 October 2015}}</ref> Germany has followed a policy of treating migrants under 18 years of age as "children first and refugees second," giving them − according to the [[Convention on the Rights of the Child]] − mostly the same rights as German children.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/10/29/world/europe/distinguishing-minors-from-adults-in-a-tide-of-young-migrants.html?ribbon-ad-idx=29&rref=world&module=Ribbon&version=origin&region=Header&action=click&contentCollection=World&pgtype=article|title=Distinguishing Minors From Adults in a Tide of Young Migrants|author=Katrin Bennhold|newspaper=The New York Times|date=28 October 2015|access-date=29 October 2015}}</ref> In late October 2015, the small village of [[Sumte]], population 102, was told by [[Lower Saxony, Germany|Lower Saxony]] officials that it would receive 750 asylum-seekers.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/11/01/world/europe/german-village-of-102-braces-for-750-asylum-seekers.html|title=German Village of 102 Braces for 750 Asylum Seekers|author=Andrew Higgins|newspaper=The New York Times|date=31 October 2015|access-date=31 October 2015}}</ref>

In February 2016, the German government admitted that it had lost track of around 13 percent of the 1.1 million people registered as asylum seekers on arrival in 2015, because they never arrived at the refugee accommodation they were assigned. The German government said that many of the missing asylum seekers probably went to other European countries, while others continued to live illegally in Germany.<ref>[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/germany/12174803/Germany-admits-130000-asylum-seekers-lost-raising-fears-over-crime-and-terrorism.html Germany admits 130,000 asylum seekers 'lost' raising fears over crime and terrorism] J. Huggler, The Daily Telegraph, 26 February 2016</ref> Merkel's immigration policies were criticised by CSU's Seehofer.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://www.spiegel.de/politik/deutschland/fluechtlinge-horst-seehofer-unterstellt-angela-merkel-herrschaft-des-unrechts-a-1076528.html|title=Streit über Flüchtlingspolitik: Seehofer unterstellt Merkel "Herrschaft des Unrechts" – SPIEGEL ONLINE – Politik|first=SPIEGEL ONLINE, Hamburg|last=Germany|newspaper=Spiegel Online|date=9 February 2016}}</ref>

In October 2016, Merkel travelled to [[Mali]] and [[Niger]]. The diplomatic visit took place to discuss how their governments could improve conditions which caused people to flee those countries and how illegal migration through and from these countries could be reduced.<ref name="spiegel_10.10.2016">{{cite magazine|title=Hunderte Millionen gegen die Flucht|url=http://www.spiegel.de/politik/ausland/angela-merkel-in-niger-hunderte-millionen-gegen-die-flucht-a-1116005.html|access-date=13 October 2016|magazine=[[Der Spiegel]]|date=10 October 2016}}</ref>

In November 2016 Germany security officials cracked down on the militant [[Salafi movement|salafist]] organisation ''Die Wahre Religion'' as their preachers targeted newly arrived migrants with their violent form of Islam.<ref name="nyt19november2016">{{cite news|title=Germany Cracks Down on Salafists to Shield Refugees|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/11/20/world/europe/germany-salafists-refugees.html|access-date=24 February 2017|newspaper=New York Times|date=19 November 2016}}</ref>

The migrant crisis spurred right-wing electoral preferences across Germany with the Alternative for Germany (AfD) gaining 12% of the vote in the [[2017 German federal election]]. These developments prompted debates over the reasons for increased right-wing populism in Germany. Literature argued that the increased right-wing preferences are a result of the European migrant crisis which has brought thousands of people, predominantly from Muslim countries to Germany, and spurred a perception among a share of Germans that refugees constitute an ethnic and cultural threat to Germany.<ref>{{cite journal|last1=Lucassen|first1=Geertje|last2=Lubbers|first2=Marcel|title=Who Fears What? Explaining Far-Right-Wing Preference in Europe by Distinguishing Perceived Cultural and Economic Threats|journal=Comparative Political Studies|date=2012|volume=45|issue=5|doi=10.1177/0010414011427851|s2cid=145071392}}</ref>

The German Federal Office for Migration has recently prioritized the newly adopted Orderly Return Law (Geordnete- Ruckkehr-Gresetz). The Orderly Return Law is a second round of legal actions taken when the person of foreign origin is denied citizenship and is then obligated to leave.<ref>“German Parliament Passes ‘Orderly-Return-Law.’” European Council on Refugees and Exiles (ECRE), www.ecre.org/germany-parliament-passes-orderly-return-law/</ref> The law allows for detention of the asylum seeker when they do not cooperate with law enforcement in the deportation process. Due to this law, the law enforcement authority given the responsibility for carrying out the deportations are given the right to access the asylum seekers apartments without any preexisting judicial orders. Given this authority, law enforcement is also subject to the responsibility of bringing the person to be deported to the airport or border for the purpose of deportation.<ref>“Germany: A Controversial Law Package Passes the Parliament.” Germany: A Controversial Law Package Passes the Parliament | Asylum Information Database, www.asylumineurope.org/news/14-06-2019/germany-controversial-law-package-passes-parliament-1</ref> The scope of the law is to increase the proportion of successful deportations to 188,000 (double what was previously possible).<ref>Mischke, Judith. “Germany Passes Controversial Migration Law.” POLITICO, POLITICO, 7 June 2019, www.politico.eu/article/germany-passes-controversial-migration-law/</ref> In reality in 2019, 22.097 individuals were deported from Germany.<ref>[https://www.bpb.de/gesellschaft/migration/flucht/zahlen-zu-asyl/265765/abschiebungen-in-deutschland "Abschiebungen in Deutschland"] [[Federal Agency for Civic Education]] 9 June 2020, Retrieved 18 September 2020</ref>

In a research report posted by the German Federal Office for Migration and Refugees,<ref>“startseite_node.” BAMF, 11 Dec. 2019, www.bamf.de/EN/Startseite/startseite_node.html</ref> the StarthilfePlus program found that most refugees, who had opted to go back with BAMF assistance, wished to return to their homelands, rejoining their friends and family. In support of this, Germany has given financial assistance to those wishing to return as a means of helping them with economic uncertainties they may face during the transition.<ref>Schmitt, Martin, et al. Assisted Return from Germany: Motives and Reintegration. Bundesamt Für Migration Und Flüchtlinge, 2019, pp. 1–8</ref> When this support has been given to those who accepted the financial aid, there was a 70% satisfaction rate with their lives at their place of origin.

===Greece===
[[File:Refugees on a boat crossing the Mediterranean sea, heading from Turkish coast to the northeastern Greek island of Lesbos, 29 January 2016.jpg|thumb|Migrants crossing the [[Aegean Sea]] from Turkey to the Greek island of [[Lesbos]], January 2016]]
[[File:20151213 Syrians refugees from Turkey plastic boat airport area of Lesvos Greece.ogv|thumb|upright=1.3636364|A group of Syrian refugees arrive by boat from Turkey to airport area of Mytilini, Lesvos island, Greece, 13 December 2015]]
[[File:Arbeitsbesuch Mazedonien (20270358044).jpg|thumb|Migrants at the Greece–North Macedonia border near [[Gevgelija]], 24 August 2015]]

Migrants arriving from the Middle East made a {{convert|4|mi|km|0|order=flip|adj=on}} water crossing to the [[Greek islands]] of [[Chios]], [[Kos]], [[Lesbos]], [[Leros]], [[Kastellorizo]], [[Agathonisi]], [[Farmakonisi]], [[Rhodes]], [[Samos]], [[Symi]] and other islands close to Turkey, which acts as a quick and accessible border into Europe.<ref name=Yeginsu>{{cite news |last1=Yeginsu |first1=Ceylan |title=Amid Perilous Mediterranean Crossings, Migrants Find a Relatively Easy Path to Greece |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/08/17/world/europe/turkey-greece-mediterranean-kos-bodrum-migrants-refugees.html|access-date=16 August 2015 |work=The New York Times |date=16 August 2015}}</ref><ref name=Neely>{{cite news |last1=Neely |first1=Bill |title=Migrants Crisis: Refugees Attempt to Reach Greek Island of Lesbos |url=https://www.nbcnews.com/storyline/europes-border-crisis/migrants-crisis-refugees-attempt-reach-greek-island-lesbos-n409011 |access-date=14 August 2015 |publisher=NBC News |date=13 August 2015}}</ref><ref name=Daley>{{cite news |last1=Daley |first1=Suzanne |title=On Island of Lesbos, a Microcosm of Greece's Other Crisis: Migrants |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/08/05/world/europe/lesbos-greece-migrant-refugee-crisis.html |access-date=14 August 2015 |work=The New York Times |date=4 August 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Refugees and migrants outnumber Kastelorizo's residents|url=http://en.protothema.gr/refugees-and-migrants-outnumber-kastelorizos-residents/|access-date=24 February 2016|work=Protothema|date=20 February 2016}}</ref> Some arrived via the [[Evros (regional unit)|Evros]] border crossing from Turkey. As of June 2015, 124,000 migrants had arrived in Greece, a 750 percent increase from 2014, constituted mainly of refugees stemming from the wars in Syria, Iraq, and Afghanistan. Greece appealed to the European Union for assistance while the [[United Nations Commission on Human Rights|UNCHR]] European Director Vincent Cochetel said facilities for migrants on the Greek islands were "totally inadequate" and the islands were in "total chaos".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-33818193 |title=Migrant 'chaos' on Greek islands – UN refugee agency |work=BBC News |access-date=28 August 2015 |date=7 August 2015}}</ref>

Frontex's Operation Poseidon, aimed at patrolling the [[Aegean Sea]], was underfunded and undermanned, with only 11 coastal patrol vessels, one ship, two helicopters, two aircraft, and a budget of €18 million.<ref name=PopFrontexGreece>{{cite news |last1=Pop |first1=Valentina |title=Greek Government Holds Emergency Meeting Over Soaring Migrant Arrivals |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/greek-government-holds-emergency-meeting-over-soaring-migrant-arrivals-1438959148 |access-date=19 August 2015 |work=The Wall Street Journal |date=7 August 2015}}</ref>

Human traffickers charged illegal immigrants $1,000 to $1,500<!-- Dollars or Euros? --> for the 25-minute boat ride from [[Bodrum]], Turkey to Kos.<ref name=Yeginsu /> In August 2015, "hundreds" of boats carried illegal immigrants across every night.<ref name=Yeginsu /> The migrants travelled onward to [[Thessaloniki]] in the mainland of Greece with a monetary estimate of €3,000 to €4,000 to reach Germany, and €10,000 to €12,000 to reach Britain.<ref name=Yeginsu /> Desperate migrants brawled over places in boats leaving Bodrum for Kos.<ref name=KilledbyFumes>{{cite news |title=40 migrants 'killed by fumes' in hold of boat off Libya |url=http://www.independent.ie/world-news/africa/40-migrants-killed-by-fumes-in-hold-of-boat-off-libya-31453815.html |access-date=17 August 2015 |work=Irish Independent |date=15 August 2015}}</ref>

Airlines charged passengers usually less than $400 for one-way economy class tickets from Turkey to Germany or Britain,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.turkishairlines.com/|title=Turkish Airlines ® – Flights to 110+ countries from İstanbul|website=turkishairlines.com}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.britishairways.com/travel/home/public/en_us|title=Book Flights, Holidays & Check In Online – British Airways|website=britishairways.com}}</ref> but a rule in the [[Schengen Agreement]] required airlines to check that all passengers have a visa or are exempted from carrying one.<ref>[http://eur-lex.europa.eu/legal-content/EN/TXT/HTML/?uri=CELEX:42000A0922(02)&from=EN The Schengen acquis] See Article 26</ref>

In September 2015, photos of the [[Death of Alan Kurdi|deceased 3-year-old Alan Kurdi]], who drowned when he and his family were in a small inflatable boat which capsized shortly after leaving Bodrum trying to reach the Greek island of Kos, made headlines worldwide. Konstantinos Vardakis, the top EU diplomat in [[Baghdad]], told ''The New York Times'' that at least 250 Iraqis per day had been landing on Greek islands between mid-August and early September 2015.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/09/world/middleeast/iraq-migrants-refugees-europe.html |title=A New Wave of Migrants Flees Iraq, Yearning for Europe |author=Tim Arango |newspaper=The New York Times |date=7 September 2015 |access-date=7 September 2015}}</ref>

On 27 January 2016, the European Commission accused Greece of neglecting its obligations under the Schengen agreement to carry out external border controls, reporting that a visit by EU inspectors in November 2015 found that Greece failed to identify and register arrivals properly, to fingerprint everyone, and to check travel documents for authenticity and against security databases.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: EU threatens Greece over border controls|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35416741|work=BBC News|date=27 January 2016}}</ref> On 12 February, the EU gave Greece a three-month deadline to fix its border controls, or other member states could be authorized to extend border controls for up to two years instead of the standard six months.<ref>{{cite news|title=EU issues deadline for Greece to remedy migration 'deficiencies'|url=http://www.dw.com/en/eu-issues-deadline-for-greece-to-remedy-migration-deficiencies/a-19044686|work=Deutsche Welle|date=12 February 2016}}</ref>

On 11 February, NATO announced that it would deploy ships in the Aegean Sea to deter smugglers taking migrants from Turkey to Greece; the first 3 ships were the [[Royal Canadian Navy]]'s {{HMCS|Fredericton|FFH 337}}, [[Turkish Naval Forces]]'s {{TCG|Barbaros|F-244}} and [[German Navy]]'s [[Berlin-class replenishment ship|''Bonn'' (A1413)]] from NATO's [[Standing NATO Maritime Group 2|SNMG2]]. NATO chief [[Jens Stoltenberg]] said the mission would not be about "stopping or pushing back refugee boats", but about intelligence gathering and sharing information with NATO allies Turkey and Greece.<ref>{{cite news|title=Migrant crisis: Nato deploys Aegean people-smuggling patrols|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35549478|work=BBC News|date=11 February 2016}}</ref>

On 1 March 2016, the Greek government asked the EU for €480 million in emergency funds to shelter 100,000 refugees.<ref>{{cite news|title=Europe Migrant crisis: Greece seeks emergency funds from EU to shelter refugees |url=http://www.balkanews.org/index.php/2016/03/01/europe-migrant-crisis-greece-seeks-emergency-funds-from-eu-to-shelter-refugees/ |work=First Post |date=1 March 2016 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160307140022/http://www.balkanews.org/index.php/2016/03/01/europe-migrant-crisis-greece-seeks-emergency-funds-from-eu-to-shelter-refugees/ |archive-date=7 March 2016 }}</ref>

North Macedonia closed its border with Greece on 9 March 2016 where 12,000 to 13,000 migrants were stuck at [[Idomeni]] on the Greek side, while the total number of migrants throughout Greece were estimated to be more than 50,000.<ref>{{cite news|title=More than 50,000 migrants and refugees stranded in Greece|url=http://www.ekathimerini.com/207172/article/ekathimerini/news/more-than-50000-migrants-and-refugees-stranded-in-greece|access-date=28 March 2016|publisher=Η ΚΑΘΗΜΕΡΙΝΗ|date=21 March 2016}}</ref>

After the [[2016 Turkish coup d'état attempt]] Greek authorities on a number of [[Aegean islands]] called for emergency measures to curtail a growing influx of refugees from Turkey; the number of migrants and refugees willing to make the journey across the [[Aegean Sea|Aegean]] had increased noticeably. At Athens officials voiced concerns that Turkish monitors overseeing the deal in Greece abruptly pulled out after the failed coup with little sign of them being replaced.<ref>{{cite news|title=Aegean islands alarm as refugee numbers rise after Turkey coup attempt|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2016/jul/30/refugee-numbers-rise-greece-aegean-turkey-coup-attempt|work=The Guardian|language=en}}</ref> The [[Association of Greek Tourism Enterprises]] (SETE) warned about the prospect of another flare-up in the refugee/migrant crisis due to the political instability in Turkey.<ref>{{cite web|title=Sector group: Coup attempt in Turkey to negatively affect Greek tourism|url=http://www.naftemporiki.gr/story/1133579/sector-group-coup-attempt-in-turkey-to-negatively-affect-greek-tourism|publisher=naftemporiki|language=en|year=2016}}</ref>

In September 2016, Greek volunteers of the "[[Hellenic Rescue Team]]" and human rights activist Efi Latsoudi were awarded the [[Nansen Refugee Award]] by the UNHCR "for their tireless volunteer work" in helping refugees arrive in Greece during the 2015 refugee crisis.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.unhcr.org/news/press/2016/9/57cdec884/greek-volunteers-share-unhcr-nansen-refugee-award.html|title=Greek Volunteers share UNHCR Nansen Refugee Award|first=United Nations High Commissioner for|last=Refugees}}</ref>

In December 2017, the Hellenic Rescue Team received the "Mother Teresa" award from the Harmony Foundation. They were rewarded for their "heroic actions" and effort to save human lives while risking their own during the migrant and refugee crisis.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.balkaneu.com/mother-teresa-award-goes-to-the-hellenic-rescue-team |title="Mother Teresa" award goes to the Hellenic Rescue Team|website=balkaneu.com|date=26 October 2017}}</ref>

===Hungary===
Hungary finished phase one of the construction of a [[Hungarian border barrier|fence]] on its southern border with Serbia in late August 2015, according to the Hungarian Ministry of Defence. The fence consists of three strands of NATO razor wire spanning 175 kilometers long. The next phase involved building a wire fence approximately 4 meters high. In August, Minister of the Prime Minister's Office [[János Lázár]] described Hungary as being "under siege from human traffickers" and announced that the government would "defend this stretch of [their] borders with force", deploying 9,000 police to keep out undocumented migrants.<ref name=BorderHunters>{{cite news |last1=Feher |first1=Margit |title=Hungary Deploys 'Border Hunters' to Keep Illegal Immigrants Out |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/hungary-unleashes-border-hunters-to-keep-illegal-immigrants-out-1439916449 |access-date=18 August 2015 |work=The Wall Street Journal |date=18 August 2015}}</ref>

Hungary's Prime Minister [[Viktor Orbán|Orbán]] wrote in the ''[[Frankfurter Allgemeine Zeitung]]'': "Europe's response is madness. We must acknowledge that the European Union's misguided immigration policy is responsible for this situation".<ref>{{cite news| title=Migration crisis: Hungary PM says Europe in grip of madness |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/03/migration-crisis-hungary-pm-victor-orban-europeresponse-madness |work=[[The Guardian]]|date=3 September 2015}}</ref> Orbán also demanded an official EU list of "safe countries" to which migrants can be returned.<ref>"[https://news.yahoo.com/hungary-pm-rejects-merkels-moral-imperialism-refugee-crisis-130722708.html Hungary PM rejects Merkel's 'moral imperialism' in refugee crisis]". Yahoo News. 23 September 2015.</ref> He said that "the moral, human thing is to make clear: 'Please don't come. Why do you have to go from Turkey to Europe? Turkey is a safe country. Stay there. It's risky to come'".<ref>"[https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/hungarys-leader-to-migrants-please-dont-come/2015/09/03/d5244c6d-53d8-4e82-b9d7-35ec41ca2944_story.html 'People in Europe are full of fear' over refugee influx]". ''The Washington Post''. 3 September 2015.</ref> Hungary adopted a list of countries deemed safe for transiting purposes: if an asylum seeker had passed through those countries, it is assumed that they could have found asylum there, and therefore would be ineligible for asylum in Hungary.<ref>{{cite news|title=Hungary adopts list of safe countries of origin and safe third countries|publisher=asylumineurope.org|url=http://www.asylumineurope.org/news/23-07-2015/hungary-adopts-list-safe-countries-origin-and-safe-third-countries}}</ref> Orbán spoke at the [[United Nations General Assembly]] and called for a "global quota" system to distribute refugees to all countries.<ref>"[http://www.ndtv.com/world-news/hungary-pm-tells-us-australia-to-take-some-of-europes-migrants-1225399 Hungary PM Tells US, Australia to Take Some of Europe's Migrants]". [[NDTV]]. 2 October 2015.</ref> [[File:P31 L.É. Eithne Operations 28 June 2015.jpg|thumb|Rescued male migrants are brought to southern Italian ports, 28 June 2015]]

Migrants taking the Western Balkan route crossed into the [[Schengen Area]] first in Greece. In June 2015, Hungary said it was contemplating countermeasures against the influx of illegal immigrants from Serbia, a non-EU and non-Schengen state.<ref>{{cite news |url=http://hosted.ap.org/dynamic/stories/E/EU_HUNGARY_MIGRATION |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150621171147/http://hosted.ap.org/dynamic/stories/E/EU_HUNGARY_MIGRATION |archive-date=21 June 2015 |title=Hungary seeks to tighten south border, hold illegal migrants |agency=Associated Press |author=Pablo Gorondi |date=9 June 2015 |access-date=28 August 2015}}</ref>

On 17 June 2015, the Hungarian government announced the construction of a {{convert|4|m|ft|adj=mid|-high}}, {{convert|175|km|mi|adj=mid|-long}} fence along its southern border with Serbia.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/2015/06/17/us-hungary-immigration-idUSKBN0OX17I20150617 |title=Hungary to fence off border with Serbia to stop migrants |work=Reuters |access-date=28 August 2015 |date=17 June 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=http://hosted.ap.org/dynamic/stories/E/EU_HUNGARY_BORDER_FENCE |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150621171828/http://hosted.ap.org/dynamic/stories/E/EU_HUNGARY_BORDER_FENCE |archive-date=21 June 2015 |title=Hungary's leader says Hungary will protect Europe's borders |agency=Associated Press |author=Pablo Gorondi |date=19 June 2015 |access-date=28 August 2015}}</ref> The [[European Commission]] warned EU members against steps that contravene EU obligations and urged members like Hungary to find other ways to cope with an influx of illegal migrants.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.rferl.mobi/a/european-commission-hungary-serbia-wall-fence-illegal-migrants/27079829.html |title=EU Warns Against New 'Walls' As Hungary Plans Fence on Serbia Border |publisher=RadioFreeEurope/RadioLiberty |access-date=28 August 2015}}</ref> The first phase of the construction was completed at the end of August and Orbán announced that it would be fully completed by the end of 2015.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://mno.hu/hatarontul/orban-nyar-vegere-megepul-a-kerites-1297022 |title=Orbán: Nyár végére megépül a kerítés |publisher=mno.hu |access-date=28 August 2015}}</ref>

On 3 September 2015, Orbán defended the country's management of the migrant situation internally, notwithstanding chaos at Budapest's [[Budapest Keleti railway station|main international rail station]], while criticising Germany and Europe overall for not dissuading migrants from entering Europe.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/04/world/europe/hungary-train-station-migrant-crisis.html|title=Hungary Defends Handling of Migrants Amid Chaos at Train Station |author1=Anemona Hartocollis |author2=Dan Bilefsky |author3=James Kanter |newspaper=The New York Times |access-date=3 September 2015 |date=3 September 2015}}</ref> On the same day, Hungarian police allowed migrants aboard a train in Budapest heading west before stopping it in [[Bicske]]. The police tried to transport migrants to a registration camp there, but the migrants refused to cooperate and remained on the train, which did not travel further west.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.yahoo.com/migrants-lay-train-tracks-hungary-seeking-passage-west-114937335.html |title=Migrants cling to Hungarian train west, lawmakers debate sealing border |agency=Reuters |access-date=3 September 2015 |date=3 September 2015}}</ref>

[[File:Syrian refugees strike in front of Budapest Keleti railway station. Refugee crisis. Budapest, Hungary, Central Europe, 3 September 2015.jpg|thumb|Migrants in a [[hunger strike]] in front of the [[Budapest Keleti railway station]], 3 September 2015]]
On 4 September 2015, about a thousand of the migrants at Railway Station East (Keleti Pályaudvar) set off by foot toward Austria and Germany.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.yahoo.com/hungary-train-migrants-stand-firm-face-off-police-104257639.html |title=Over 1,000 migrants leave Budapest train station on foot for Austria |agency=Agence France-Presse |date=4 September 2015 |access-date=4 September 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/05/world/europe/migrant-crisis-hungary.html|title=Blocked by Rail, Migrants Set Out for Germany on Foot |author=Dan Bilefsky |newspaper=The New York Times |date=4 September 2015 |access-date=4 September 2015}}</ref> On the same night, the Hungarian government decided to send buses to transport illegal migrants to [[Hegyeshalom]], on the border with Austria.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-34159780 |title=Migrant crisis: Hungary to bus migrants to Austria border |work=BBC News |date=4 September 2015 |access-date=4 September 2015}}</ref>

On 14 September 2015, Hungarian police reportedly blocked the route from Serbia and heavily manned the regular entry point with officers, soldiers, and helicopters.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dw.com/en/refugee-crisis-live-updates/a-18712845|title=+++ Refugee crisis – live updates +++|work=DW.COM|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> They sealed the border with razor wire and detained migrants crossing the border illegally with the threat of arrest and criminal charges.<ref name=Wire1>{{cite web|url=http://www.euronews.com/2015/09/15/hungary-seals-border-with-razor-wire/|title=Hungary seals border with razor wire|publisher=euronews|date=15 September 2015|access-date=15 September 2015}}</ref><ref name="Wire2">{{cite news|author1=Helene Bienvenu|author2=Dan Bilefsky|date=15 September 2015|title=Hungary Detains Migrants in Border Crackdown|newspaper=The New York Times|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/09/16/world/europe/hungary-detains-migrants-in-border-crackdown.html|access-date=15 September 2015}}</ref> On 15 September 2015, Hungary sealed its border with Serbia. Several hundred migrants broke the fence between Hungary and Serbia twice on Wednesday, 16 September 2015, and threw chunks of concrete and water bottles over the fence. Hungarian police retaliated with tear gas and water cannons at [[Horgoš]] 2 border crossing. [[Belgrade]] protested these actions. A 20-year-old [[Iraqi refugee]] was sentenced to deportation and a one-year entry ban in Hungary, as well as €80 in court fees, according to the new law put into action a few days before.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.index.hr/vijesti/clanak/kaos-na-madjarskoj-granici-izbjeglice-probili-ogradu-cuje-se-pucnjava-policija-mlati-ljude/842284.aspx#lightbox[galerija]/0/|title=Kaos na mađarskoj granici: Izbjeglice probili ogradu, čula se pucnjava, policija mlatila ljude|work=index.hr|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> On 18 September, Hungary started building another fence along the border with Croatia, a fellow EU member state, but not part of the Schengen Area.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.jutarnji.hr/policija-zatvorila-granicu-prema-srbiji--izbjeglice-do-daljnjega-ostaju-kod-nas/1420334/|title=UŽIVO: SUZAVAC PRIMIRIO IZBJEGLICE NA GRANICI KOD ZAPREŠIĆA! Hrvatski policajci izbačeni s vlaka u Mađarskoj: 'Nisu razoružani, samo su ih evidentirali. Ništa dramatično se nije dogodilo...' |work=jutarnji.hr|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref> Within two weeks, tens of thousands of refugees crossed from Croatia into Hungary, most of whom went to the Austrian border.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://bbj.hu/politics/more-than-24000-refugees-enter-hungary-over-weekend_104760|title=More than 24,000 refugees enter Hungary over weekend|access-date=30 September 2015}}</ref>

On 16 October 2015, Hungary announced that it would close its [[green border]] with Croatia to migrants,<ref name=HungaryCroatia2/> and from 17 October onward, thousands of migrants were diverted to Slovenia instead every day.<ref name=SloveniaCroatia2>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/10/18/world/europe/hungary-closes-border-changing-refugees-path.html|title=Hungary Closes Border, Changing Refugees' Path|author1=Barbara Surk |author2=Stephen Castle |newspaper=The New York Times|date=17 October 2015|access-date=17 October 2015}}</ref>

On 9 March 2016 Hungary declared a state of emergency for the entire country and deployed 1500 soldiers to its borders.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://hungarytoday.hu/news/breaking-news-hungary-declares-state-emergency-migrant-crisis-turns-unpredictable-96001|title=Breaking News: Hungary Declares State Of Emergency As Migrant Crisis Turns Unpredictable|work=Hungary Today|access-date=21 March 2016|date=9 March 2016}}</ref><ref>[http://www.novinite.com/articles/173459/Hungary+Declares+State+of+Emergency+Over+Migrants Hungary Declares State of Emergency Over Migrants] (novinite.com 9 March 2016)</ref> In August 2017 the state of emergency was extended to March 2018.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://wtop.com/europe/2017/08/hungary-extends-state-of-emergency-due-to-migrant-crisis/|title=Hungary extends state of emergency due to migrant crisis|date=30 August 2017|work=WTOP|access-date=30 August 2017|language=en-US|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170831085120/http://wtop.com/europe/2017/08/hungary-extends-state-of-emergency-due-to-migrant-crisis/|archive-date=31 August 2017|url-status=dead}}</ref>

In December 2015, Hungary challenged the EU's plans to share asylum seekers across EU states at the European Court of Justice.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35158769 |title=Migrant crisis: One million enter Europe in 2015 |author=no by-line. |date=22 December 2015 |website=BBC News |publisher=BBC |access-date=22 December 2015}}</ref> The border closed 15 September 2015, with razor wire fence along its southern borders, particularly Croatia, and travel by train was blocked.<ref name="Noack">{{cite news |last=Noack |first=Rick |date=22 December 2015|title=Over a million refugees and migrants arrived in Europe this year. Here is what you need to know. |url=https://www.chicagotribune.com/news/nationworld/ct-million-refugees-migrants-europe-20151222-story.html |newspaper=Chicago Tribune |location=Chicago, USA |access-date=24 December 2015}}</ref> The government believed that "illegal migrants" are job-seekers, threats to security, and likely to "threaten our culture".<ref>{{cite web |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35162515 |title=Migrant crisis: Hungary denies fuelling intolerance in media |last=Thorpe |first=Nick |date=22 December 2015 |website=BBC News |publisher=BBC |access-date=24 December 2015}}</ref> There have been cases of immigrants and ethnic minorities being attacked. In addition, Hungary has conducted wholesale deportations of refugees, who are generally considered to be allied with [[ISIL]].<ref name="matthewweaver1">{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/live/2015/sep/15/refugee-crisis-hungary-launches-border-crackdown-live-updates|title=Refugee crisis: Hungary rejects all asylum requests made at border – as it happened|author=Matthew Weaver|newspaper=the Guardian|date=15 September 2015}}</ref> Refugees are outlawed and almost all are ejected.<ref name="matthewweaver1" />

===Italy===
{{Main|Lampedusa immigrant reception center|Immigration to Italy}}
Some Italian towns and cities disobeyed instructions from the national government to house migrants.<ref name=Legorno>{{cite news |last1=Legorno |first1=Giovanni |title=Italian Towns Push Back on Growing Burden of Europe's Migrant Crisis |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/italian-towns-push-back-on-growing-burden-of-europes-migrant-crisis-1430085784 |access-date=18 August 2015 |work=[[The Wall Street Journal]] |date=28 April 2015}}</ref> The [[Mafia Capitale investigation]] revealed that the [[Organized crime in Italy|Italian Mafia]] profited from the migrant crisis and exploited refugees.<ref>"[http://www.ft.com/cms/s/0/0d0371d0-31f4-11e5-8873-775ba7c2ea3d.html Italy's Mafia learns to profit from the migration crisis]". ''[[Financial Times]]''. 24 July 2015</ref><ref>"[http://www.abc.net.au/radionational/programs/latenightlive/how-the-mafia-profits-from-the-mediterranean-migrant-crisis/6573084 'Bigger than drugs': how the Mafia profits from the Mediterranean migrant crisis]". ABC News. 29 June 2015</ref> [[Pope Francis]] thanked the [[Italian navy]] for their migrant rescue effort.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/18/pope-thanks-italy-for-migrant-rescue-effort-says-huge-numbers-means-europe-must/|title=Pope thanks Italy for migrant rescue effort, says huge numbers means Europe must pitch in more|publisher=Fox News Channel|access-date=19 September 2015|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150925172832/http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/18/pope-thanks-italy-for-migrant-rescue-effort-says-huge-numbers-means-europe-must/|archive-date=25 September 2015|url-status=dead|df=dmy-all}}</ref>

The [[murder of Ashley Ann Olsen]] in her Italian apartment by an illegal immigrant from [[Senegal]] rapidly acquired political significance in the context of the European migrant crisis. The police chief of [[Florence]] addressed safety concerns and "assur[ed] the public that Florence remained safe" in the wake of the Olsen murder.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Pianigiani |first1=Gaia |title=Italy Arrests Suspect in Death of American Woman|url= https://www.nytimes.com/2016/01/15/world/europe/ashley-ann-olsen-italy-arrest.html |work=New York Times |date=14 January 2016 |access-date=2019-12-31}}</ref>

Since 2014, thousands of migrants have tried every month to cross the Central Mediterranean to Italy, risking their lives on unsafe boats including fishing trawlers.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/apr/24/libyas-people-smugglers-how-will-they-catch-us-theyll-soon-move-on |title=Libya's people smugglers: inside the trade that sells refugees hopes of a better life &#124; World news |newspaper=The Guardian |access-date=2018-06-28}}</ref> Many of them were fleeing poverty-stricken homelands or war-torn countries and sought economic opportunity within the EU.<ref name="Boatsform Libya">{{cite news |last1=Scammell |first1=Rosie |title=Mediterranean migrant crisis: number of arrivals in Italy in 2015 passes 50,000 |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/jun/07/mediterranean-migrant-arrivals-italy-passes-50000 |access-date=14 August 2015 |work=The Guardian |date=7 June 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/italy/11549216/The-EU-migrant-crisis-explained-in-90-seconds.html |title=Video: The EU migrant crisis explained in 90 seconds – Telegraph |date=22 April 2015 |work=The Daily Telegraph |access-date=28 August 2015 |location=London |first=Joe |last=Daunt}}</ref> Italy, and, in particular, its southern island of [[Lampedusa]], received enormous numbers of Africans and Middle-Easterners transported by smugglers and NGOs operating along the ungoverned coast of the [[failed state]] of Libya.<ref name="Boatsform Libya" /><ref name=MappingBBC>{{cite news |title=Mapping Mediterranean migration |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-24521614 |access-date=14 August 2015 |publisher=BBC |date=15 September 2014}}</ref>

[[File:Boat People at Sicily in the Mediterranean Sea.jpg|thumb|left|Migrants arrived in [[Lampedusa]] ]]

In 2014, 170,100 migrants arrived in Italy by sea, a 296 percent increase compared to 2013. 141,484 of the travellers were ferried over from Libya. Most of the migrants had come from [[Syria]], [[Eritrea]], and various countries in [[West Africa]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Analisi: Paolo Gentiloni |url=https://pagellapolitica.it/dichiarazioni/analisi/5221/paolo-gentiloni |work=Pagella Politica |date=22 February 2015}}</ref>

From January to April 2015, about 1600 migrants died on the route from Libya to Lampedusa, making it the deadliest migrant route in the world.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/about-700-believed-dead-in-shipwreck-off-libya-says-unhcr-1429432174? |title=Hundreds of Migrants Believed Dead in Shipwreck Off Libya, Says UNHCR |access-date=19 April 2015 |work=The Wall Street Journal |date=19 April 2015}}</ref> As a consequence of the April 2015 Libya [[List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea|migrant shipwrecks]], the EU launched a military operation known as [[EU Navfor Med|Operation Sophia]]. More than 13,000 migrants had been rescued from the sea in the course of the operation as of April 2016.<ref name="auto11">"[http://www.dw.com/en/on-the-mediterranean-refugee-patrol-with-the-bundeswehr/a-19209234 On the Mediterranean refugee patrol with the Bundeswehr]". [[Deutsche Welle]]. 22 April 2016.</ref>

There were 153,842 Mediterranean sea arrivals to Italy in 2015, 9 percent less than the previous year; most of the refugees and migrants came from [[Eritrea]], [[Nigeria]], and [[Somalia]], whereas the number of Syrian refugees sharply decreased, as most of them took the Eastern Mediterranean route from Turkey to Greece.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.libertaciviliimmigrazione.interno.it/dipim/site/it/documentazione/statistiche/servizi_civili/2016/1_2016_Statistiche_2015_sbarchix_esiti_domande_di_asilo_e_posti_in_strutture_accoglienza.html |title=Statistiche immigrazione |publisher=Italian Ministry of the Interior |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160328233432/http://www.libertaciviliimmigrazione.interno.it/dipim/site/it/documentazione/statistiche/servizi_civili/2016/1_2016_Statistiche_2015_sbarchix_esiti_domande_di_asilo_e_posti_in_strutture_accoglienza.html |archive-date=28 March 2016 }}</ref>
[[File:Messina1.jpg|thumb|[[Eritrea]]n migrants in [[Messina]], October 2015]]
The first three months of 2016 saw an increase in the number of migrants rescued at sea being brought to southern Italian ports.<ref>"[https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-eu-idUSKCN0XA1EO EU sees 'alarming' migrant buildup in Libya, warns Italy]". Reuters. 13 April 2016.</ref><ref>"[https://www.wsj.com/articles/eu-wants-austria-to-explain-threat-to-close-border-with-italy-1460719198 Tensions Mount Between Austria and Italy as Migrant Numbers Rise]". ''[[The Wall Street Journal]]''. 15 April 2016.</ref><ref>"[http://navaltoday.com/2016/03/17/german-warship-rescues-615-from-the-mediterranean/ German warship rescues 615 from the Mediterranean]". ''Naval Today.'' 17 March 2016.</ref> In April 2016, nearly 6,000 mostly sub-Saharan African migrants landed in Italy in four days.<ref>"[http://qz.com/663014/photos-in-the-last-four-days-6000-migrants-have-arrived-to-sicily-by-boat-from-libya/ In the last four days, 6,000 migrants have arrived in Sicily by boat]". ''[[Quartz (publication)|Quartz]].'' 16 April 2016.</ref> In June 2016, over 10,000 migrants were rescued in four days.<ref name="DW">"[http://www.dw.com/en/italian-coastguard-and-navy-rescue-3300-migrants-off-coast-of-libya/a-19358699 Italian coastguard and navy rescue 3,300 migrants off coast of Libya]". ''[[Deutsche Welle]]''. 27 June 2016.</ref>

In 2016, 181,100 migrants arrived in Italy by sea.<ref>"[https://www.thelocal.it/20170106/italys-boat-migrant-numbers-surged-20-in-2016 Italy boat migrant numbers surge 20% in 2016]". ''[[The Local]]''. 6 January 2017.</ref> In April 2017, more than 8,000 migrants were rescued near Libya and brought to Italy in three days.<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/2017/04/18/8000-migrants-rescued-mediterranean-brought-italy-easter-long/ More than 8,000 migrants rescued in Mediterranean and brought to Italy over Easter long weekend ]". ''[[The Daily Telegraph]]''. 18 April 2017.</ref> Based on UN data, about 80,000 refugees were registered at Italian refugee centers in the first half of 2017, an increase of 14 percent when compared to the same time period in 2016. In June 2017, 10,000 asylum seekers were picked up in the Mediterranean sea by the Italian coastguard and other naval vessels in a couple of days. EU ambassador Maurizio Massari expressed concern about the uptake of refugee arrivals on Italy's coastline, which would have reached 200,000 in 2017. As a result, foreign aid vessels docking in Italian ports were no longer able to do so because of stricter admission policies and exceeded limits in Italian asylum centers.<ref>
[https://www.blick.ch/news/ausland/das-land-droht-mit-krassen-massnahmen-gegen-fluechtlinge-hilfeschrei-aus-italien-id6919283.html Hilfeschrei aus Italien!] Das Land droht mit krassen Massnahmen gegen Flüchtlinge (in German). ''Blick – Ausland''. Retrieved 29 June 2017.</ref> In February 2017 the Italian government fund Libyan coast guard; since then many migrants were forced to go back to Libya.<ref name="auto12"/>

In July 2017, Italy drew up a code of conduct for NGO rescue vessels delivering migrants to Italian ports. These rules included:
* A prohibition from entering the [[territorial waters]] of Libya, except in situations of imminent danger.
* A prohibition from switching off the [[Automatic identification system|Automatic Identification System]] (AIS) and [[Long-range identification and tracking (ships)|LRIT]] transponders if they are installed on the ship.
* A prohibition from signaling human traffickers with flares or radio to coordinate with them when to send out their [[Dinghy|dinghies]].
* A prohibition from transferring those rescued onto other vessels.
* A commitment to having a policeman to travel on board whenever requested in order to identify and prosecute human traffickers among the migrants.

The Human Rights Watch and Amnesty International criticised the code of conduct and some NGOs like [[Médecins Sans Frontières|MSF]] refused to sign. Italian authorities feared that rather than saving lives, the NGO operations encouraged more people to use the dangerous passage facilitated by human traffickers.<ref name=":2">{{Cite news|url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-msf-idUSKBN1AS0L1|title=MSF suspends Mediterranean rescues as migrant dispute mounts|date=12 August 2017|work=Reuters|access-date=13 August 2017}}</ref><ref name=":3">{{cite web|url=http://www.euronews.com/2017/08/03/text-of-italys-code-of-conduct-for-ngos-involved-in-migrant-rescue|title=Italy's code of conduct for NGOs involved in migrant rescue: text|date=3 August 2017|website=euronews|access-date=13 August 2017}}</ref> NGO ships disobeying the code could be refused access to Italian ports.<ref name=":2" /><ref name=":3" />

After the NGO code was enforced, arrivals decreased by 52.5 percent in July 2017 when compared to the same month in 2016 (from 23,552 to 11,183 arrivals),<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.ilsole24ore.com/art/notizie/2017-07-31/migranti-luglio-si-inverte-trend-sbarchi-dimezzati-133105.shtml?uuid=AEZMsb6B&refresh_ce=1|title=Migranti, si inverte il trend: a luglio sbarchi dimezzati|date=31 July 2017|website=ilsole24ore.com|access-date=16 September 2017|language=it}}</ref> and in August 2017 arrivals decreased by 85 percent (from 21,294 to 3,914).<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.interno.gov.it/sites/default/files/cruscotto_giornaliero_14_settembre_2017.pdf|title=Cruscotto giornaliero 14 settembre 2017|date=14 September 2017|website=interno.gov.it|access-date=16 September 2017|language=it|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170916225451/http://www.interno.gov.it/sites/default/files/cruscotto_giornaliero_14_settembre_2017.pdf|archive-date=16 September 2017|df=dmy-all}}</ref> All NGOs except for Sos Méditerranée withdrew their ships from the Mediterranean.

From January to November 2017, approximately 114,600 migrants arrived in Italy by sea.<ref>"[http://english.alarabiya.net/en/News/north-africa/2017/11/23/Italy-says-1-100-migrants-from-Libyan-coast-rescued-in-one-day.html Italy: 1,100 migrants rescued from Libyan coast in one day]". Al Arabiya. 23 November 2017.</ref> Approximately 5,000 African migrants were rescued in waters off the coast of Libya between 18–20 May 2017.<ref>"[http://www.aljazeera.com/news/2017/05/5000-refugees-rescued-route-italy-libya-170520134511012.html 5,000 refugees rescued on route to Italy from Libya]". Al Jazeera. 20 May 2017.</ref>

Since 2013, Italy took in over 700,000 migrants,<ref>{{cite web |title=What will Italy's new government mean for migrants? |url=https://www.thelocal.it/20180521/what-will-italys-new-government-mean-for-migrants |website=The Local |date=21 May 2018}}</ref> mainly from sub-Saharan Africa.<ref>{{cite news |title=African migrants fear for future as Italy struggles with surge in arrivals |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-italy-migrants-africa/african-migrants-fear-for-future-as-italy-struggles-with-surge-in-arrivals-idUSKBN1A30QD |work=Reuters |date=18 July 2017}}</ref>

===Latvia===
Latvia decided to receive 250 migrants for two years according to the EU plan,{{When|date=May 2020}} which the [[National Alliance (Latvia)|National Alliance party]] disapproved. On 4 August 2015 around 250 activists gathered in [[Riga]] to protest against the government's decision on receiving migrants.

===Lithuania===
Lithuania decided to receive 325 migrants, although after the increase of migrant flow in August 2015, its government did not discount the possibility of accepting a greater number of migrants later in the same year.<ref name=DELFI>{{cite news |title=PM says Lithuanian government not considering to accept more refugees |url=http://en.delfi.lt/lithuania/politics/pm-says-lithuanian-government-not-considering-to-accept-morerefugees.d?id=68893804 |access-date=3 September 2015 |work=BNS |date=2 September 2015}}</ref>

===Malta===
{{Main|Demographics of Malta#Immigration}}

Prime Minister [[Joseph Muscat|Muscat]] called the crisis "an ugly period" for Europe, and said that Malta will take in 75 migrants from Italy and Greece.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Sansone|first1=Kurt|title=Migrant wall will not stop problem, Joseph Muscat says|url=http://www.timesofmalta.com/articles/view/20150913/local/migrant-wall-will-not-stop-problem-joseph-muscat-says.584315|access-date=13 September 2015|work=[[The Times (Malta)|The Times]]|date=13 September 2015}}</ref> He also called for a "global system of refugee quotas".<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/hungary/11903664/Hungary-and-Malta-call-for-global-migrant-quotas-to-ease-Europe-burden.html Hungary and Malta call for 'global migrant quotas' to ease Europe burden]". ''The Daily Telegraph''. 1 October 2015.</ref>

Between 2008 and 2012, Malta received the highest number of [[asylum seekers]] on average compared to its national population: 21.7 applicants per 1,000 inhabitants.<ref name="UNHCR">{{cite web|url=http://unhcr.org/asylumtrends/UNHCR%20ASYLUM%20TRENDS%202012_WEB.pdf |title=UNHCR |access-date=18 October 2015}}</ref>{{rp|13}} In 2011, most of these asylum applications were submitted by Somalian, Nigerian, Eritrean, and Syrian nationals;<ref name="UNHCR"/>{{rp|26}} in 2012, more than half of the requests were by Somalian nationals alone.<ref name="UNHCR"/>{{rp|45}} In a 2013 news story, ''The Guardian'' reported, "Before Malta joined the EU in 2004, immigration levels were negligible. Because it is located close to north Africa, it has now become a gateway for migrants seeking entry to Europe."<ref>"[https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/2013/aug/04/malta-needs-eu-help-immigration-crisis Malta needs EU help to cope with its immigration crisis]". ''[[The Guardian]]''. 4 August 2013.</ref> Following the arrival of asylum seekers, Malta was unable to cope with accommodating asylum seekers in a manner which was congruent with EU standards on the reception of asylum seekers, particularly standards related to housing.{{citation needed|date=November 2017}}

In 2015, fewer migrants arrived in Malta compared to previous years as most of those rescued were taken to [[Italy]]. In September, 78 migrants rescued by the [[Armed Forces of Malta]] refused to be brought to Malta.<ref>{{cite news|title=Rescued migrants refusing to be brought to Malta|url=http://www.timesofmalta.com/articles/view/20150926/local/rescued-migrants-refusing-to-be-brought-to-malta.585856|access-date=26 September 2015|work=[[The Times (Malta)|The Times]]|date=26 September 2015}}</ref> They insisted on going to Italy and were eventually taken there.<ref>{{cite news|title=It-78 immigrant li ma riedux jidħlu f'Malta se jittieħdu l-Italja|url=http://www.tvm.com.mt/mt/news/it-78-immigrant-li-ma-riedux-jidhlu-fmalta-se-jittiehdu-l-italja/|access-date=27 September 2015|work=[[TVM (Malta)|TVM]]|date=27 September 2015|language=mt}}</ref>

Malta has been criticized for showing lack of compassion towards destitute migrants escaping from poverty, while selling Maltese passports - and EU citizenship - to paying millionaires.<ref>https://daphnecaruanagalizia.com/2016/08/germanys-der-spiegel-today-citizenship-rich-maltas-billion-dollar-trade-eu-passports/</ref>

===Norway===
{{See also|Norway–Russia border barrier}}
The number of migrants crossing from [[Russia-Norway border|Russia into Norway]] increased from a handful in the first half of 2015 to 420 asylum seekers crossing by bicycle in September 2015 alone.<ref name=ArcticRoute>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2015/10/10/world/europe/bypassing-the-risky-sea-refugees-reach-europe-through-the-arctic.html?hpw&rref=world&action=click&pgtype=Homepage&module=well-region&region=bottom-well&WT.nav=bottom-well&_r=0|title=Avoiding Risky Seas, Migrants Reach Europe With an Arctic Bike Ride|author=Andrew Higgins |newspaper=The New York Times|date=9 October 2015|access-date=9 October 2015}}</ref> As of 11 December 2015 over 4,000 migrants had crossed the Northern border, and the Norwegian government vowed to send all migrants with Russian residence visas back to Russia even if they were from countries experiencing conflicts such as [[Norwegian Army#War in Afghanistan|Afghanistan]].<ref name="no-ru-limbo-local">{{cite news|work=[[The Local]]|title=Russia sends denied migrants back to Norway|url=http://www.thelocal.no/20151130/norway-irked-as-russia-sends-back-asylum-seekers|date=30 November 2015}}</ref> In 2016, 5,500 [[asylum-seeker]]s illegally entered Norway from Russia.<ref name="NYTimesFence"/><ref name="PancevskyColdShoulder">{{cite news|last1=Pancevsky|first1=Bojan|title=Norway builds Arctic border fence as it gives migrants the cold shoulder|url=http://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/norway-builds-arctic-border-fence-as-it-gives-migrants-the-cold-shoulder-hf37jlwqq|access-date=6 September 2016|newspaper=[[The Times of London]]|date=4 September 2016}}</ref> Norway defied Amnesty International and sent migrants back to conflict-torn countries of origin, such as Afghanistan. The number of migrants returned from Europe to Afghanistan between 2015–16 nearly tripled from 3290 to 9460.<ref>{{cite news|url=http://time.com/4968868/eu-betraying-afghanistan-dangerous-aid-policy/|title=Europe is Betraying Afghanistan By Sending Its Refugees Home|website=Time}}</ref> Because it is illegal to drive from Russia to Norway without proper legal permission, and crossing on foot is prohibited, migrants made the crossing on bicycles.<ref name="Osborne">{{cite news|last1=Osborne|first1=Samuel|title=Norway to build border fence with Russia to keep out refugees|url=https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/norway-border-fence-russia-refugees-refugee-crisis-schengen-syria-war-a7208806.html|newspaper=[[The Independent]]|date=25 August 2016}}</ref><ref name="HovlandArcticRoute">{{cite news|last1=Hovland|first1=Kjetil Malkenes|title=Syrian Refugees Take Arctic Route to Europe More than 150 refugees have entered Norway from Arctic Russia this year|url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/syrian-refugees-take-arctic-route-to-europe-1441273767|access-date=6 September 2016|newspaper=Wall Street Journal|date=3 September 2015}}</ref> In 2016 the Norwegian government planned a barrier located at the [[Storskog]] border crossing.<ref name="NYTimesFence"/> It is made of steel and stands {{convert|660|ft|m}} long and {{convert|11|ft|m}} to {{convert|12|ft|m}} high.<ref name="NYTimesFence"/> Norwegian officials aimed to complete the barrier before winter temperatures hardened the ground.<ref name="NYTimesFence">{{cite news|title=Norway Will Build a Fence at Its Arctic Border With Russia|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2016/08/25/world/europe/russia-norway-border-fence-refugees.html|access-date=6 September 2016|agency=Reuters|newspaper=New York Times|date=24 August 2016}}</ref>

In 2018, Statistics Norway reported that out of recently arrived [[Syrians in Norway|migrants from Syria]], 67% had only basic education (Norwegian: ''Grunnskole'').<ref>{{cite book |title=Innvandrere og norskfødte med innvandrerforeldre fra Syria |date=26 June 2018 |publisher=[[Statistics Norway]] |page=26 |url=https://www.ssb.no/befolkning/artikler-og-publikasjoner/_attachment/355170?_ts=1645efbce30 |access-date=14 July 2018}}</ref>

===Slovakia===
The government of Slovakia stated that it would help with migration into Europe by receiving 200 migrants according to the EU plan on the condition that the migrants were [[Christianity|Christians]].<ref name=Troianoski /> Slovakian Prime Minister [[Robert Fico]] said: "I have only one question: who bombed Libya? Who caused problems in North Africa? Slovakia? No!" The Prime Minister proposed temporary refuge in his country for 500 migrants who submitted requests for asylum in Austria, whose accommodation for refugees was overfilled, but like the 200 migrants that Slovakia would receive according to the EU plan, he required that these 500 were also Christian. On 15 September 2015, Fico was reported saying that all persons found crossing the border illegally would be detained.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.rt.com/news/315293-schengen-border-control-toughened/|title=End of Schengen? EU countries toughen border control|work=RT English|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref>{{Deprecated inline}} He rejected the European Commission's plan to distribute migrants among EU member states, saying: "As long as I am prime minister, mandatory quotas will not be implemented on Slovak territory."<ref>"[https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/eu/11887390/This-East-West-split-over-EU-refugee-quotas-will-have-long-lasting-consequences.html This East-West split over EU refugee quotas will have long-lasting consequences]". ''[[The Daily Telegraph]].'' 24 September 2015.</ref> The [[Progressive Alliance of Socialists and Democrats|S&D]] Group leader has proposed to suspend Fico's [[Direction – Social Democracy|SMER]] party from the [[Party of European Socialists]] (PES).<ref>"[http://www.euractiv.com/sections/justice-home-affairs/refugee-crisis-reveals-fundamental-splits-european-political-parties Refugee crisis reveals fundamental splits in European political parties]". EurActiv. 24 September 2015.</ref>

===Slovenia===
{{See also|Slovenian border barrier}}
[[File:Ministrica obiskala pripadnike Slovenske vojske in URSZR, ki pomagajo v nastanitvenem centru in na meji 01.JPG|thumb|Migrants in Slovenia, November 2015]]
