Slovenia established temporary controls on the otherwise unsupervised border with Hungary to the northeast on 17 September 2015, following Germany and Austria's similar actions.<ref>{{cite web|title = Slovenia Reinstating Controls at Border with Hungary|url = http://www.sloveniatimes.com/slovenia-reinstating-controls-at-border-with-hungary|publisher = sloveniatimes.com|access-date = 19 September 2015}}</ref> On 18 September, Slovenia experienced the first of many illegal border crossings, coming mostly from Croatia, which was already overwhelmed by the large influx of migrant groups.

On the evening of 18 September, the Slovenian riot police used [[pepper spray]] on a bridge at the [[Harmica]] border to prevent migrants and activists from illegally crossing the border from Croatia.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://news.yahoo.com/latest-un-agency-calls-joint-european-response-113758508.html|title=Slovenian police pepper spray migrants at border|publisher=Yahoo!|date=19 September 2015|access-date=19 September 2015}}</ref>

By midday of 19 September, the country had registered around 1,500 migrants, with all of them being accommodated in temporary reception camps or asylum centres. The largest traffic was seen at the [[Obrežje, Brežice|Obrežje border crossing]], [[Dobova|Dobova border crossing]] and [[Brežice]]. Prime Minister [[Miro Cerar]] visited the reception centre in Brežice on Saturday, stressing that Slovenia had the situation under control, while criticising the Croatian government for being uncooperative.<ref>{{cite web|title = Slovenia Admits Some 1,500 Refugees, Some Proceed to Austria|url = http://www.sloveniatimes.com/slovenia-admits-some-1-500-refugees-some-proceed-to-austria|publisher = sloveniatimes.com|access-date = 19 September 2015}}</ref>
[[File:Slovenska vojska pri reševanju migrantske situacije z več zmogljivostmi 01.jpg|alt=large group of migrants moving along a road, being directed by the army and police|left|thumb|Arrival of migrants in Dobova, Slovenia]]
There were also various humanitarian and non-governmental organisations, mostly from Slovenia, Croatia and Austria, aiding the migrants on the border.<ref>{{cite web|title = Begunce z Obrežja pospešeno odvažajo v notranjost države|url = http://www.dolenjskilist.si/2015/09/19/140941/novice/novice_splosno/Begunce_z_Obrezja_pospeseno_odvazajo_v_notranjost_drzave/|website = Dolenjski list|access-date = 19 September 2015}}</ref>

On 18 October 2015, the country began receiving large numbers of refugees, which soon exceeded the upper admission limit of 2,500. On 22 October, the police reported 12,600 migrant arrivals in 24 hours, more than Hungary had ever received. The Slovenian government passed a law giving the army more powers and asked the EU for aid. The latter responded by sending the commissioner for migration to Slovenia and announced a "mini EU summit".<ref>{{cite web|title = Slovenia calls for EU help amid record influx of refugees|url = http://www.euronews.com/2015/10/22/slovenia-calls-for-eu-help-amid-record-influx-of-refugees/|website = euronews|access-date = 24 October 2015|date = 22 October 2015}}</ref> On the same day the Slovenian government accused the Croatian police of leading migrants through cold waters in an effort to bypass the Slovene controls by crossing the green border, and released a night time thermovision video allegedly showing the events the night before.<ref>{{cite web|title = Slovenian police helicopter films Croatian police officers directing migrants to Slovenia across the green border and the Sotla river|url = http://www.policija.si/eng/index.php/component/content/article/13-news/1739-slovenian-police-helicopter-films-croatian-police-officers-directing-migrants-to-slovenia-across-the-green-border-and-the-sotla-river|website = policija.si|access-date = 24 October 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title = Šefic: Croatian travesty on inhuman Slovenians :: Prvi interaktivni multimedijski portal, MMC RTV Slovenija|url = https://www.rtvslo.si/news-in-english/sefic-croatian-travesty-on-inhuman-slovenians/376964|website = rtvslo.si|access-date = 24 October 2015}}</ref>

By 24 October, Slovenia reported more than 56,000 total migrant arrivals.<ref>{{cite web|title = V ŽIVO: Pretep v sprejemnem centru Brežice, policija je uporabila plinski razpršilec|url = http://www.24ur.com/novice/slovenija/samo-vceraj-in-danes-je-preko-zelene-meje-pri-rigoncah-v-slovenijo-vstopilo-okoli-13-000-tujcev.html|publisher = 24ur.com|access-date = 24 October 2015}}</ref>

On 10 November, Cerar announced that Slovenia would impose temporary technical hurdles to control migrants, but that the country would not close border crossings.<ref>{{cite web|title = Slovenia to impose "hurdles" on border to control migrant flow :: Prvi interaktivni multimedijski portal, MMC RTV Slovenija|url = http://www.rtvslo.si/news-in-english/slovenia-to-impose-hurdles-on-border-to-control-migrant-flow/378324|website = rtvslo.si|access-date = 11 November 2015}}</ref> On 11 November, Slovenian military personnel began building a razor wire fence.<ref>{{cite web|title = Slovenian troops start erecting border fence :: Prvi interaktivni multimedijski portal, MMC RTV Slovenija|url = http://www.rtvslo.si/news-in-english/slovenian-troops-start-erecting-border-fence/378397|website = rtvslo.si|access-date = 11 November 2015}}</ref> The Austrian minister of the interior [[Johanna Mikl-Leitner]] expressed full support for the Slovenian government's action on the border with Croatia.<ref>{{Cite news|url = http://orf.at/stories/2309111/2309109/|title = ORF|access-date = 11 November 2015|language = de}}</ref>

On 23 February 2016, German media noted that Slovenia decided to deploy its army on the border with Croatia to assist the police. The bill did not approve military action, but authorised the army to use force in case of an emergency.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.dw.com/en/slovenia-deploys-army-to-schengen-zone-border-to-tackle-refugee-influx/a-19066844|title=Slovenia deploys army to Schengen zone border to tackle refugee influx|work=DW.COM|access-date=23 February 2016}}</ref>

===Spain===
From 2000 until at least 2016, Spain developed a purportedly efficient plan to manage irregularly arriving migrants on the Spanish [[Canary Islands]]; it consisted of four aspects:
*Strengthening bilateral ties and close cooperation with local actors in all origin and transit countries
*Establishing bilateral partnership agreements with those countries
*Security, intelligence and policy strategies and joint actions
*Legal avenues and resettlement policies through agreements with those countries.<ref>[http://www.iris-france.org/80796-eu-spain-and-the-refugee-crisis/ 'EU, Spain and the refugee crisis']. Interview with refugee expert Patricia Lisa, Research Fellow at [[Elcano Royal Institute|Real Instituto Elcano]], October 2016, on IRIS (Institut de Relations Internationales et Stratégiques, a French think tank). Retrieved 26 March 2019.</ref>

In 2017, [[Spain]] saw a large increase in the number of asylum applicants and was catching up to Italy and Greece in terms of popularity as a destination country, with nearly 8300 people trying to enter in the first half of the year.{{citation needed|date=June 2018}}

The International Organization for Migration recorded a 217 percent increase in the first seven months of 2017 compared with the same period in 2016, when more than 8,000 migrants arrived throughout the year.<ref name=hrw2017>{{Cite news|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2017/07/31/spain-migrants-held-poor-conditions|title=Spain: Migrants Held in Poor Conditions|date=31 July 2017|work=Human Rights Watch|access-date=5 November 2017|language=en}}</ref> Authorities believed that Spain was ill-equipped to handle the surging numbers of migrants. Deaths were recorded daily in 2017, both at the destination and during the journey.<ref name=hrw2017/>

====Melilla and Ceuta====
{{Main|Morocco–Spain border|Melilla border fence|Ceuta border fence}}
[[Melilla]] and [[Ceuta]], two autonomous Spanish cities on the north coast of Africa bordering [[Morocco]], are the only EU territories to share a land border with an African country.<ref>"[https://theweek.com/articles/572833/spanish-city-africa-become-hugely-symbolic-europes-migrant-crisis This Spanish city in Africa has become hugely symbolic of Europe's migrant crisis]". ''[[The Week]]''. 21 August 2015.</ref> The number of undocumented migrants hoping to reach the EU via Melilla or Ceuta grew in 2014.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://m.euronews.com/en/293928/ |title=euronews – Over 100 migrants attempt to storm Melilla enclave |publisher=euronews.com |access-date=28 August 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150726000233/http://m.euronews.com/en/293928/ |archive-date=26 July 2015 |url-status=dead |df=dmy-all }}</ref> Between January and September 2015, only 100 people out of 3700 managed to cross the Melilla border fence, down from 2100 people from 19,000 attempts the previous year.<ref name="Morel 2015">{{cite web | last=Morel | first=Sandrine | title=Uneasy calm descends over Melilla, Spain's heavily fortified African enclave | website=The Guardian | date=8 September 2015 | url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/sep/08/melilla-fences-spain-morocco-migration-europe | access-date=29 November 2015}}</ref> In October 2015, 165 people were rescued from fourteen attempts to cross the [[Strait of Gibraltar]] to reach Ceuta.<ref name="Edwards 2015">{{cite web | last=Edwards | first=Sam | title=A decade of violence at Spain's forgotten African border shows why Europe's new fences alone are bound to fail | website=El País | date=21 November 2015 | url=http://blogs.elpais.com/trans-iberian/2015/11/a-decade-of-violence-at-spains-forgotten-african-border-shows-why-europes-new-fences-alone-are-bound.html | access-date=29 November 2015}}</ref>

In a report published on 17 November 2015, [[Amnesty International]] called on Spain to cease cooperation with Morocco on immigration matters because of alleged human rights abuses on the Melilla and Ceuta borders. Amnesty said it had "photographs, images and evidence" of "blows with sticks, feet and stones" on migrants attempting to get to Spain.<ref name="Bloul 2015">{{cite web | last=Bloul | first=Scheherazade | title=Amnesty International Calls for Spain to Cease Cooperation with Morocco on Migration Policy | website=Morocco World News | date=17 November 2015 | url=http://www.moroccoworldnews.com/2015/11/172878/amnesty-international-calls-on-spain-to-cease-cooperation-with-morocco-on-migration-policy/ | access-date=29 November 2015}}</ref> Other reports accused Spain of using rubber bullets and tear gas to prevent migrants from reaching Spanish territory. The Spanish government said that it has now banned its border guards from using rubber bullets to repel migrants.<ref name="The Local.es Dec 2015">{{cite web | title=Two dead as migrants storm Spain's African border at Ceuta | website=The Local | date=25 December 2015 | url=http://www.thelocal.es/20151225/two-dead-as-migrants-storm-spanish-border | access-date=27 March 2016}}</ref>

In May 2015, an 8-year-old boy from the [[Ivory Coast]] was found in a suitcase being smuggled into Ceuta. When the police opened the case, they found him in a "terrible state".<ref name="BBC News Ceuta 2015">{{cite web | title=Ivory Coast boy smuggled to Spain inside suitcase | website=BBC News | date=8 May 2015 | url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-africa-32660135 | access-date=2 January 2017}}</ref> In December 2016, one migrant was found in a suitcase, carried by a Moroccan woman, trying to get into Ceuta.<ref name="BBC News Ceuta 2017">{{cite web | title=Spain Ceuta: Migrants found hidden in car and suitcase | website=BBC News | date=2 January 2017 | url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-38490868 | access-date=2 January 2017}}</ref> On 1 January 2017, there was an attempt by 1100 migrants to cross the Ceuta border fence. 50 Moroccans and five Spanish border guards prevented them from crossing the fence, but one border guard lost an eye during the attempt.<ref name="BBC News Ceuta 2017" />

===Sweden===
As of 26 November 2015, Sweden had received 146,000 asylum seekers in 2015, with a record of 39,000 applications in October. Most asylum seekers were Afghan, followed by Syrians and Iraqis.<ref name=dn1>[http://www.dn.se/nyheter/sverige/manga-flyktingar-soker-sig-till-sverige-trots-nya-atgarder/ Många flyktingar söker sig till Sverige – trots nya åtgärder] {{in lang|sv}} Dagens Nyheter, 27 October 2015</ref> In the beginning of November, the authorities warned they could no longer offer housing to all asylum seekers and on 12 November temporary border control was enacted (on the Swedish side) to reduce the number of migrants, though they could still apply for asylum.<ref name=dn1/> On 26 November 2015, Prime Minister [[Stefan Löfven]] said the system for welcoming migrants was about to collapse and that the cabinet would propose major new restrictions and measures to reduce the influx of migrants. He called on other European countries to take more responsibility.<ref>David Crouch (24 November 2015) [https://www.theguardian.com/world/2015/nov/24/sweden-asylum-seekers-refugees-policy-reversal Sweden slams shut its open-door policy towards refugees] ''The Guardian''.</ref> In December the government introduced "carrier's responsibility" for trains and buses on the [[Öresund bridge]] which would introduce Swedish border controls on the Danish side.<ref>{{cite web |title= Särskilda åtgärder vid allvarlig fara för den allmänna ordningen eller den inre säkerheten i landet |url=https://www.regeringen.se/rattsliga-dokument/proposition/2015/12/prop.-20151667/ |language=sv}}</ref>

In 2016, there were reports that multiple [[We Are Sthlm sexual assaults|sexual harassment incidents]] occurred at the [[We Are Sthlm]] festival over the course of several years.<ref>{{cite news|title=Swedish police probe 'cover-up of migrant sex assaults'|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-35285086|work=BBC News|date=11 January 2016}}</ref> During all of 2015, migration authorities reported 500 cases of suspected terrorism links or war criminals to [[Swedish Security Service]].<ref name="sydsvenskan_5juli2016">{{cite news|title=Migrationsverket anmäler allt fler terrorhot|url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/2016-07-05/migrationsverket-anmaler-allt-fler-terrorhot|access-date=20 August 2016|newspaper=Sydsvenskan|date=5 July 2016}}</ref> Twenty individuals were denied asylum in 2015 due to [[war crimes]].<ref name="sydsvenskan_5juli2016" />

In November 2015, Sweden reintroduced border controls for arrivals, including the [[Öresund Bridge]]. This did not reduce the number of asylum seekers as they had the right to apply for asylum once they were on Swedish ground. In December 2015, Sweden passed a temporary law that allowed the government to oblige all transport companies to check that their passengers carried valid photographic identification before crossing the border. The new law came into effect on 21 December 2015 and was valid until 21 December 2018.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.riksdagen.se/sv/Dokument-Lagar/Utskottens-dokument/Betankanden/Arenden/201516/JuU24/|title=Särskilda åtgärder vid allvarlig fara för den allmänna ordningen eller den inre säkerheten i landet – riksdagen.se|author=Riksdagsförvaltningen|access-date=22 January 2016}}</ref> It led to the mandatory train change and passage through border control at [[Copenhagen Airport, Kastrup Station|Copenhagen Airport station]] for travellers between Copenhagen and Sweden; service frequency was reduced.<ref>[https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-35159183 Migrant crisis: Sweden operator cancels trains on bridge link] BBC News website. Retrieved 23 December 2015<!-- News sites have somewhat misunderstood the thing. Direct trains are cancelled but it will be possible to travel with a train change, although SJ cancel all their operations. This info has to be reassessed in January 2016. --></ref>

On the first day of border control the number of migrants arriving to southern Sweden was reduced from the hundreds to dozens.<ref name=sds_5jan2016>{{cite news|title=Bara 48 asylsökande till Skåne under måndagen|url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/sverige/bara-48-asylsokande-till-skane-under-mandagen/|access-date=5 January 2016|work=[[Sydsvenskan]]|date=5 January 2016}}</ref> Within hours of Swedish border control becoming effective, Denmark created a border control between Denmark and Germany.<ref name=sds_4Jan2016>{{cite news|title=Färre än 100 nobbade på Kastrup|url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/sverige/inga-koer-vid-kritiserade-kontrollen/|access-date=5 January 2016|work=[[Sydsvenskan]]|date=4 January 2016}}</ref> The migration pattern also changed with the majority of those arriving by ferry from Germany to [[Trelleborg]] instead of by train to [[Hyllie]] station,<ref name=sds_5jan2016/> which bypassed the border control between Denmark and Germany.<ref name=sds_4Jan2016/> Migrants started taking taxis in greater numbers over the Öresund Bridge to evade identification.<ref name=sds_7jan2016>{{cite news|title=Papperslösa tar taxi över Bron|url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/sverige/papperslosa-tar-taxi-over-bron/|access-date=8 January 2016|work=[[Sydsvenskan]]|date=7 January 2016}}</ref> Three days later,{{When|date=May 2020}} a Danish cab driver was arrested for human trafficking near the Øresund Bridge.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.dr.dk/nyheder/udland/dansk-taxachauffoer-anholdt-menneskesmugling-til-sverige|title=Dansk taxachauffør anholdt for menneskesmugling til Sverige|website=DR}}</ref> In January 2016 the newspaper [[Sydsvenskan]] reported that the rate of migration led to an increase of [[MRSA]] infections in [[Skåne]] province where many migrants are received: from 160 cases in 2005 to more than 635 cases in 2015.<ref name="ssd_2Jan2016">{{cite news|title=Flyktingström bakom stor ökning av MRSA |url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/sverige/flyktingstrom-bakom-stor-okning-av-mrsa/ |access-date=7 February 2016 |newspaper=[[Sydsvenskan]] |date=2 January 2016 |url-status=dead |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160129114648/http://www.sydsvenskan.se/sverige/flyktingstrom-bakom-stor-okning-av-mrsa/ |archive-date=29 January 2016 }}</ref> In January 2016 interior minister [[Anders Ygeman]] said that Sweden was rejecting about 45 percent of asylum applications, which meant that around 60,000–80,000 of the 160,000 asylum-seekers who applied for asylum in 2015 could be deported in the coming years.<ref name="telegrah_28Jan2016">{{cite news|title=Sweden and Finland plan to expel up to 100,000 failed asylum seekers|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/worldnews/europe/sweden/12126599/Sweden-plans-to-expel-up-to-80000-failed-asylum-seekers.html|access-date=21 February 2016|work=The Daily Telegraph|date=28 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Sweden to deport up to 80,000 asylum-seekers|url=https://www.cbsnews.com/news/sweden-to-deport-up-to-80000-asylum-seekers/|agency=Associated Press|date=28 January 2016}}</ref>

According to the Swedish [[National Board of Health and Welfare (Sweden)|National Board of Health and Welfare]] in 2016, an estimated 20 to 30 percent of asylum seekers suffered from [[mental disorder]]s.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.socialstyrelsen.se/nyheter/2016/detstoraantaletasylsokandeharpaverkatvardochtandvard|title=Det stora antalet asylsökande har påverkat vård och tandvård |website=socialstyrelsen.se |language=sv|access-date=2017-12-28|quote=Belastningen har också ökat inom psykiatrin, 20–30 procent av de asylsökande uppskattas vara drabbade av psykisk ohälsa.}}</ref>

Of the 162,000 who migrated to Sweden in 2015, by May 2016 only 500 had found employment, where employment constituted more than 1 hour of work per week or state-subsidised schemes.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.svt.se/nyheter/inrikes/162-000-kom-till-sverige-500-fick-jobb|title=162.000 kom till Sverige – 500 fick jobb|last=Nyheter|first=SVT|date=2016-05-31|work=SVT Nyheter|access-date=2018-05-11|language=sv}}</ref>

In late June 2016 the [[Riksdag|Swedish parliament]] voted for more restrictive policy with a large majority in favour. As a result, residence permits were temporary and immigration of family members were curtailed, along with higher demands of proof to be able to support immigrating relatives. These measures were valid for three years.<ref name="dn_21June2016">{{cite news|title=Ny skärpt asyllag klubbad|url=http://www.dn.se/nyheter/politik/ny-skarpt-asyllag-klubbad/|access-date=21 June 2016|newspaper=[[Dagens Nyheter]]|date=21 June 2016}}</ref> The law applied retroactively on everyone who arrived on 24 November 2015 at the earliest and came into effect 20 July 2016. These measures put Sweden in line with the minimum line of requirements mandated by the EU.<ref name="ssd_20July2016">{{cite news|title=Skärpt asyllag träder i kraft|url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/2016-07-20/skarpt-asyllag-trader-i-kraft|access-date=20 July 2016|newspaper=[[Sydsvenskan]]|date=20 July 2016}}</ref> Thirty individuals were denied asylum January–June 2016 due to [[war crimes]].<ref name="sydsvenskan_5juli2016"/>

In August 2016 four workers at asylum centres for refugee children were reported to have been infected by [[tuberculosis]] and health services reported an increase in tuberculosis infections due to the crisis.<ref name="ssd_18augusti2016">{{cite news|title=Anställda på flyktingboenden smittade av tuberkulos|url=http://www.sydsvenskan.se/2016-08-17/anstallda-pa-flyktingboenden-i-malmo-smittade-av-tuberkulos|access-date=20 August 2016|newspaper=[[Sydsvenskan]]|date=18 August 2016}}</ref> In 2015 an increase of 22 percent of cases from the previous year was noted; this was largely attributed to an increased influx of migrants over that year.<ref name="dn_2016-02-28">{{cite news|title=Tuberkulos ökar kraftigt i Sverige|url=http://www.dn.se/nyheter/sverige/tuberkulos-okar-kraftigt-i-sverige/|access-date=21 August 2016|newspaper=Dagens Nyheter|date=28 February 2016}}</ref> 90 percent of people infected with tuberculosis were born abroad.<ref name="dn_2016-02-28"/>

In October 2016 a leaked internal memo from the cabinet showed that spending cuts to all public services had become necessary due to the escalating costs of the migration crisis.<ref name="svd_25October2016">{{cite news|title=Internt mejl visar: Nya besparingar krävs|url=http://www.svd.se/internt-mejl-visar-nya-besparingar-kravs/om/flykten-till-europa|access-date=27 November 2016|newspaper=Svenska Dagbladet|date=25 October 2016}}</ref>

In January 2017 police described gangs of recently arrived youth making the central shopping mall of Gothenburg unsafe at night with muggings and violence over drug deals between gangs of Moroccan, Afghan, and Syrian origin. Police work was made difficult by the [[Swedish Migration Agency]] which neglected to identify arriving migrants leading to an arrested individual's fingerprint matching a handful of identities. When offered help from social services the youth declined and preferred a life on the streets supporting themselves with crime.<ref name="expr14jan2017">{{cite news|title=Brottsplats Nordstan – så ser vardagen ut|url=http://www.expressen.se/gt/droger-och-valdsbrott--ny-vardag-i-nordstan/|access-date=18 January 2017|newspaper=Expressen|date=14 January 2017}}</ref>

In May 2017 border police reported that it had been possible to verify the identities of 77 migrants from [[Morocco]] using fingerprint matches checked against the Moroccan fingerprint database. It was found that out of the 77, 65 had lied about their identity and of the 50 claiming to be underage, all but two were adults.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.svd.se/falska-identiteter-vanliga-hos-ensamkommande-fran-marocko|title=Falsk identitet vanligt bland asylsökande från Marocko|last=frida.svensson@svd.se|first=Frida Svensson {{!}}|work=SvD.se|access-date=29 May 2017|language=sv}}</ref>

In May 2017 the [[Swedish National Board of Forensic Medicine]] started aiding the [[Swedish Migration Agency]] in determining the age of migrants claiming to be underage. The first batch of 518 investigations indicated that 442 were likely adults. Of the 442, 430 were men and 12 women.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rmv.se/aktuellt/de-forsta-medicinska-aldersbedomningarna-klara/|title=De första medicinska åldersbedömningarna klara – Rättsmedicinalverket|work=Rättsmedicinalverket|access-date=31 May 2017|language=sv-SE}}</ref>

Up until 2017, the [[Swedish Migration Agency]] awarded [[Temporary resident|temporary residence permits]] also to people considered [[War crime|war criminals]] and [[Terrorism|security threats]]. This allowed these individuals to claim [[welfare]] benefits and [[Healthcare in Sweden|healthcare]] from the state of Sweden.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.svt.se/nyheter/inrikes/migrationsverket-4|title=Så ska Sverige stoppa misstänkta terrorister|last=Nyheter|first=SVT|work=SVT Nyheter|access-date=4 July 2017|language=sv}}</ref>

In [[Falkenberg]], [[Falkenberg Municipality|the municipality]] created gender-segregated housing for [[unaccompanied minor]]s, as the boys would sexually harass the girls and the girls previously did not dare to go out into the communal areas of the accommodations without wearing the veil. With segregated housing, the girls were able to make better use of the facilities.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.svt.se/nyheter/lokalt/halland/uppdelat-boende-ska-starka-ensamkommande-flickor|title=sv: Uppdelat boende ska stärka ensamkommande flickor|work=Sydsvenskan|access-date=19 July 2017}}</ref>

In June 2017, the [[Supreme Administrative Court of Sweden]] (HFD) ruled that illegal immigrants, such as those who stay in hiding after their asylum applications had been rejected in order to evade deportation, had no right to welfare benefits. A woman was denied welfare benefits (''sv:socialbidrag'') by the council of [[Vännäs]] and she took the council to court. The first instance (sv:''förvaltningsrätten)'' ruled in the woman's favour, but the council took the case to the highest court HFD which ruled in favour of the council.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.dagensjuridik.se/2017/06/papperslosa-som-haller-sig-undan-utvisning-har-inte-ratt-till-bidrag-dom-fran-hfd|title="Papperslösa" som håller sig undan utvisning har inte rätt till bidrag – dom från HFD|work=Dagens Juridik|access-date=10 November 2017|language=sv}}</ref>

In July 2017 [[Swedish Radio]] reported that few recently-arrived migrants who had low education were willing to improve their schooling; about 3 to 4 percent are taking classes two years after receiving a residence permit. Migrants are not generally aware that in order to find steady employment in the job market of Sweden, completed [[Education in Sweden#Secondary school|secondary education]] is a frequent requirement.<ref name="sr19July2017">{{cite news|title=sv: Få lågutbildade nyanlända vill studera|url=http://sverigesradio.se/sida/artikel.aspx?programid=83&artikel=6738611|access-date=23 July 2017|publisher=Swedish Radio|date=19 July 2017}}</ref>

In September 2017 staff at the [[Swedish Migration Agency]] reported rising levels of death threats and harassment from migrants applying for residence. The nature of the threats changed when staff members were being stalked or received threatening messages on private phones or social media.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.svt.se/nyheter/lokalt/stockholm/anstallda-pa-migrationsverket-hotas-ofta|title=Personal på Migrationsverket utsätts för hot under asylprocessen|last=Nyheter|first=SVT|work=SVT Nyheter|access-date=13 September 2017|language=sv}}</ref>

In November 2017, [[Swedish Public Employment Service]] statistics showed that of the 24,034 recently arrived migrants in Stockholm, 9,324 were women of whom 3 percent had found non-subsidised employment and 14,710 were men, of whom 7 percent had found non-state-subsidised employment.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.dn.se/sthlm/mycket-fa-nyanlanda-kvinnor-far-jobb/|title=Mycket få nyanlända kvinnor får jobb – DN.SE|date=2017-11-08|work=DN.SE|access-date=2018-04-01|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180323104603/https://www.dn.se/sthlm/mycket-fa-nyanlanda-kvinnor-far-jobb/|archive-date=23 March 2018|language=sv-se}}</ref>

In March 2018, researcher Pernilla Andersson Joona at Stockholm University found that 50 percent of recently arrived migrants had less than the Swedish 9-year basic education (Swedish: ''grundskolekompetens'').<ref>{{cite web|url=http://arbetsmarknadsnytt.se/forskare-lattast-fa-nyanlanda-i-arbete-med-subventionerade-anstallningar/|title=Forskare: Lättast få nyanlända i arbete med subventionerade anställningar|website=arbetsmarknadsnytt.se|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180330161753/http://arbetsmarknadsnytt.se/forskare-lattast-fa-nyanlanda-i-arbete-med-subventionerade-anstallningar/|archive-date=30 March 2018|access-date=2018-03-31}}</ref>

===Switzerland===
As a non-EU member country but full participant in the [[Schengen Agreement]], the [[Swiss Confederation]] was directly affected by the migrant crisis with most of the refugees arriving from [[Italy]] at border crossings in the Southern cantons of [[Ticino]] and [[Valais]]. In 2015, almost 40,000 asylum seekers applied for refugee status. Compared to 2015, this number dropped by 31 percent in 2016 and 70 percent in the first quarter of 2017. Most of the asylum seekers arriving in Switzerland come from [[Eritrea]] (49 percent), followed by [[Afghanistan]] (30 percent) and [[Syria]]. Despite relative restrictive admission policies and increased patrolling of illegal border crossings, the Swiss attempted to admit refugees throughout the course of the migrant crisis, and distributed those asylum seekers to the appropriate cantons and city states.

Refugees first received a temporary residence permit "N" valid for 6 months while they waited for approval of their status. Asylum seekers who are not admitted but cannot return to their home country because of health or safety considerations receive a residence permit "F" that allows them to stay in Switzerland. Persons receiving a "B" permit are admitted refugees according to the [[Geneva Convention]] with a full residence allowance for 12 months and possible extensions. Almost 50 percent of the asylum seekers receive residence permits or are allowed to stay, and about 10 percent of those rejected can be placed in another Schengen country.

With 3.4 asylum seekers per 1000 inhabitants in 2016, Switzerland processed more asylum applications than the European average of 2.5. About 2.5 percent of asylum seekers in Switzerland are employed; the numbers are higher at 30 percent for those with temporary permits and at 24 percent for admitted refugees.<ref>Sermîn Faki, Priska Wallimann (April 2017). [http://www.blick.ch/news/politik/blick-erklaert-asylland-schweiz-in-zahlen-id6551880.html "Asylland Schweiz in Zahlen"](in German). Blick News Politik. Retrieved 21 April 2017.</ref>

In 2016, 85.8 percent of refugees in Switzerland received [[welfare]] payments.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.srf.ch/news/schweiz/neue-sozialhilfestatistik-80-prozent-der-asylbewerber-und-fluechtlinge-beziehen-sozialhilfe|title=SRF News: Neue Sozialhilfestatistik – 80 Prozent der Asylbewerber und Flüchtlinge beziehen Sozialhilfe|last=hesa|first=SRF 4 News 11:00 Uhr/sda/bfs/schubeca/kurn|work=Schweizer Radio und Fernsehen (SRF)|access-date=2017-12-25|language=de-CH}}</ref>

===Poland===
In 2015, just before the [[2015 Polish parliamentary election|parliamentary elections]] that were to happen that year, government officials with then-Prime Minister [[Ewa Kopacz]] stated that the country was ready to take 2,000 refugees.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://msw.gov.pl/en/news/909,Preparations-for-taking-2000-refugees.html |title=Preparations for taking 2,000 refugees |author=JSK Internet |work=Ministry of the Interior}}</ref>  However, after the [[Law and Justice]] party won the elections, the rhetoric changed. Both the government of Poland and President [[Andrzej Duda]] rejected the European Union's proposal of compulsory migrant quotas. Duda stated: "I won't agree to a dictate of the strong. I won't back a Europe where the economic advantage of the size of a population will be a reason to force solutions on other countries regardless of their national interests".<ref>"[https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2015-09-08/polish-president-blasts-eu-dictate-of-the-strong-on-migrants Poland's Duda Blasts EU `Dictate of the Strong' on Migrants]". Bloomberg. 8 September 2015.</ref>

===Portugal===
Portugal willing to offer shelter to 1,500 of the refugees coming to Europe from the Mediterranean Sea.{{When|date=May 2020}} A source told Diário de Notícias that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs had already presented its counter-proposal to the European Commission (EC), which wanted Portugal to take in 2,400 refugees.<ref>{{cite web |title=Portugal prepares for migrants |url=http://theportugalnews.com/news/portugal-prepares-for-migrants/35809 |publisher=theportugalnews.com |access-date=6 September 2015}}</ref>

===Romania===
The European Commission asked Romania to accept 6,351 refugees under an EU quota scheme. The EurActiv reported that "Romanian Prime Minister [[Victor Ponta]] said that his country will request admission to the EU's [[Schengen Area|Schengen borderless area]] if mandatory quotas to accept refugees are decided by the Union".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.euractiv.com/sections/justice-home-affairs/romania-accept-refugees-if-admitted-schengen-317426 | title=Romania to accept refugees if admitted to Schengen |publisher=EurActiv |date=8 September 2015}}</ref>

===United Kingdom===
British Home Secretary [[Theresa May]] said that it was important to help people living in war zone regions and refugee camps, "not the ones who are strong and rich enough to come to Europe".<ref>"[http://www.spiegel.de/international/germany/refugee-policy-of-chancellor-merkel-divides-europe-a-1053603.html Mother Angela: Merkel's Refugee Policy Divides Europe]". ''[[Der Spiegel]].'' 21 September 2015.</ref> British [[UKIP]] politician [[Nigel Farage]] stated that the exodus from Libya was caused by the [[Libyan Crisis (2011–present)|civil war in Libya]] due to [[2011 military intervention in Libya|NATO military intervention]] approved by [[David Cameron]] and [[Nicolas Sarkozy]].<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/news/politics/nigel-farage/11548171/Nigel-Farage-David-Cameron-directly-caused-Libyan-migrant-crisis.html |title=Nigel Farage: David Cameron 'directly caused' Libyan migrant crisis |work=The Daily Telegraph |date=19 April 2015 |author=Holehouse, Matthew |location=London}}</ref> UK media began reporting a new "unfolding crisis" of people attempting to cross the Channel in small boats in August 2020.<ref>{{Cite news|last=correspondent|first=Jamie Grierson Home affairs|date=2020-08-11|title=UK and France working 'at pace' on plan to halt migrant Channel crossings|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2020/aug/11/dover-mp-natalie-elphicke-tories-invading-migrants-letter-channel-crossings|access-date=2020-10-05|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> The UK's response to this has been criticised as chaotic.<ref>{{Cite news|last=correspondent|first=Jamie Grierson Home affairs|date=2020-08-11|title=UK and France working 'at pace' on plan to halt migrant Channel crossings|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2020/aug/11/dover-mp-natalie-elphicke-tories-invading-migrants-letter-channel-crossings|access-date=2020-10-05|issn=0261-3077}}</ref> Home Secretary Priti Patel reportedly considered making the Channel crossing "unviable" (though it was not specified what this entailed), as well as sending asylum seekers to a volcanic island in the South Atlantic.<ref>{{Cite news|last=correspondent|first=Jamie Grierson Home affairs|date=2020-08-11|title=UK and France working 'at pace' on plan to halt migrant Channel crossings|language=en-GB|work=The Guardian|url=https://www.theguardian.com/uk-news/2020/aug/11/dover-mp-natalie-elphicke-tories-invading-migrants-letter-channel-crossings|access-date=2020-10-05|issn=0261-3077}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=2020-09-29|title=Priti Patel looked at idea of sending asylum seekers to South Atlantic|url=http://www.theguardian.com/politics/2020/sep/30/priti-patel-looked-at-idea-of-sending-asylum-seekers-to-south-atlantic|access-date=2020-10-05|website=the Guardian|language=en}}</ref>

===Arrivals===
====2014====
According to the [[International Organization for Migration]] (IOM), up to 3,072 people died or disappeared in the Mediterranean Sea while trying to migrate to Europe in 2014.<ref name="auto1">{{cite news |url=http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/15/migrant-boat-capsizes-off-libya-400-feared-dead/ |title=Migrant boat capsizes off Libya, 400 feared dead |publisher=[[Fox News Channel]] |date=15 April 2015 |access-date=19 April 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150930071234/http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/04/15/migrant-boat-capsizes-off-libya-400-feared-dead/ |archive-date=30 September 2015 |url-status=dead |df=dmy-all }}</ref> Overall, it is estimated that over 22,000 migrants died between 2000 and 2014.<ref>{{cite web|title=IOM Releases New Data on Migrant Fatalities Worldwide: Almost 40,000 Since 2000|url=https://www.iom.int/statements/iom-releases-new-data-migrant-fatalities-worldwide-almost-40000-2000|website=IOM – International Organization for Migration|publisher=International Organization for Migration|access-date=15 June 2017|date=29 September 2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Brian|first1=Tara|last2=Laczko|first2=Frank|title=Fatal Journeys. Tracking Lives Lost during Migration|url=https://publications.iom.int/system/files/pdf/fataljourneys_countingtheuncounted.pdf|website=IOM online bookstore|publisher=IOM – International Organization for Migration|access-date=15 June 2017|page=12|date=2014}}</ref>

In 2014, around [[#Migrant arrivals versus "illegal" border crossings|252,000 new migrants]] arrived "irregularly" in the European Union, often coming from Syria, Somalia or Eritrea, often having travelled oversea from Libya.<ref name="auto1" /> 220,194 migrants crossed EU sea borders in the Central, Eastern and Western Mediterranean (a 266 percent increase compared to 2013); half of them had come from Syria, Eritrea and Afghanistan.<ref name="FrontexARA2015">{{cite web |url=http://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annual_Risk_Analysis_2015.pdf#page=59 |title=Annual Risk Analysis 2015 |page=57 |publisher=[[Frontex]] |date=27 April 2015}}</ref>

Of those arriving in Southern Europe in 2014, the vast majority (170,664, a 277 percent increase compared to 2013) arrived in Italy through Libya, whereas a minority (50,834, a 105 percent increase) arrived in Greece through Turkey.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annual_Risk_Analysis_2015.pdf#page=21 |title=Annual Risk Analysis 2015 |page=59 |publisher=[[Frontex]] |date=27 April 2015}}</ref> 62,000 applied for [[Right of asylum|asylum]] in Italy, but most Syrians and Eritreans, who constituted almost half of the arrivals in Italy in 2014, did not stop in Italy but instead continued moving towards northern Europe, particularly to Germany and Sweden.<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.unhcr.org/5592bd059.html#14 |title=The sea route to Europe: The Mediterranean passage in the age of refugees |page=14 |publisher=[[UNHCR]]}}</ref>

====2015====
[[File:Number of migrants in Hungary per week.pdf|thumb|Number of migrants in Hungary per week, May–September 2015]]
IOM and [[United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees|UNHCR]] estimated that 1,005,504 migrants and refugees arrived in Europe from 1 January to 21 December 2015, three to four times more than in 2014.<ref name="Miles One Million 2015">{{cite news | last=Miles | first=Tom | title=EU gets one million migrants in 2015, smugglers seen making $1 billion | work=Reuters | date=22 December 2015 | url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-europe-migrants-idUSKBN0U50WI20151222 | access-date=22 December 2015}}</ref> 3 percent (34,215) arrived to Bulgaria and Greece by land; the rest arrived in Greece, Italy, Spain, Cyprus and Malta by sea. The vast majority arrived by sea in Greece (816,752); 150,317 arrived by sea in Italy, with a slight drop from 170,000 in 2014. Half of the migrants crossing the Mediterranean were from Syria, 20 percent were from Afghanistan and 7 percent from Iraq. IOM estimated that a total of 3,692 migrants and refugees lost their lives in the Mediterranean in 2015 – over 400 more than in 2014 – of whom 2,889 died in the Central Mediterranean and 731 died in the Aegean sea.<ref>{{cite news|title=Irregular Migrant, Refugee Arrivals in Europe Top One Million in 2015: IOM |url=https://www.iom.int/news/irregular-migrant-refugee-arrivals-europe-top-one-million-2015-iom|publisher=IOM|date=22 December 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=A million refugees and migrants flee to Europe in 2015|url=http://www.unhcr.org/567918556.html|work=UNHCR|date=22 December 2015}}</ref>

In 2015, Greece overtook Italy as the primary point of arrival and surpassed 2014's numbers in the first six months of 2015: 67,500 people arrived in Italy, mainly coming from [[Eritrea]] (25 percent), [[Nigeria]] (10 percent) and [[Somalia]] (10 percent), whereas 68,000 arrived on the islands of Greece, mainly coming from [[Syria]] (57 percent) and [[Afghanistan]] (22 percent).<ref>{{cite web |url=http://www.unhcr.org/5592bd059.html#11 |title=The sea route to Europe: The Mediterranean passage in the age of refugees |page=11 |publisher=[[UNHCR]]}}</ref> In total, 137,000 migrants crossed the Mediterranean into Europe in the first six months of 2015.<ref name=MediterraneanCrisis2015>{{cite news |title=Mediterranean Crisis 2015 at six months: refugee and migrant numbers highest on record |url=http://www.unhcr.org/5592b9b36.html |access-date=14 August 2015 |publisher=UNHCR |date=1 July 2015}}</ref>

From 1 January to 17 April 2015, 21,191 migrants reached the Italian coast, with a decrease during the month of March due to bad weather conditions, and a surge since 10 April, bringing the number of arrivals in line with the number recorded in the same period in 2014. However, the death toll in the first four months of 2014 was 96, compared to 500 in the same period in 2015; this number excluded the victims of the [[April 2015 Libya migrant shipwrecks|shipwrecks on 13 and 19 April]].<ref>{{cite news |title=IOM Applauds Italy's Weekend Rescue at Sea of 2,800 Migrants |url=http://www.iom.int/cms/en/sites/iom/home/news-and-views/press-briefing-notes/pbn-2015/pbn-listing/iom-applauds-italys-weekend-resc.html |publisher=International Organization for Migration |date=13 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Migrant Deaths Soar in Mediterranean |url=http://www.iom.int/cms/en/sites/iom/home/news-and-views/press-briefing-notes/pbn-2015/pbn-listing/migrant-deaths-soar-in-mediterra.html |publisher=International Organization for Migration |date=17 April 2015}}</ref><ref>{{Cite journal|last=Cameron|first=Bobby Thomas|date=2015|title=Migration in the Mediterranean Region and Policy Implications|url=https://thercs.org/blogsnews-and-blognews-and-blog/news-and-blog/migration-in-the-mediterranean-region-and-policy-implications/|journal=Commonwealth Voices|publisher=Royal Commonwealth Society}}</ref>

In early August 2015, the UNHCR said that 250,000 migrants had arrived in Europe by sea so far in 2015, 124,000 in Greece and 98,000 in Italy.<ref name=BBCnavyrescues>{{cite news |title=European migrant crisis: Italy navy rescues 50 from dinghy |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-33882177 |access-date=14 August 2015 |publisher=BBC |date=12 August 2015}}</ref> According to [[Frontex]], July was estimated to have 107,500 migrants enter the EU.<ref name=JulySetsRecord>{{cite news |title=European Union border agency: Number of migrants entering EU hits new monthly record in July |url=http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/08/18/european-union-border-agency-number-migrants-entering-eu-hits-new-monthly/ |access-date=18 August 2015 |agency=Associated Press |publisher=Fox News Channel |date=18 August 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150925110912/http://www.foxnews.com/world/2015/08/18/european-union-border-agency-number-migrants-entering-eu-hits-new-monthly/ |archive-date=25 September 2015 |url-status=dead |df=dmy-all }}</ref>

Frontex detected 615,492 illegal EU-border-crossings in the third quarter of 2015 and 978,338 in the fourth quarter,<ref>{{cite web|title=FRAN Quarterly – Quarter 4 (2015)|url=http://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/FRAN_Q4_2015.pdf|publisher=Frontex}}</ref> bringing the number of observed illegal EU-border-crossings in 2015 to 1.82 million (872,938 in Greece, 764,038 in Hungary and Croatia, and 153,946 in Italy). However, in 2015 there were only an estimated one million individuals irregularly entering the EU: most migrants following the Western Balkan route were double-counted as "illegally crossing an EU border": first when arriving in Greece, and again when entering the EU for the second time through Hungary or Croatia.<ref name="Frontex2016">{{cite web|title=Risk analysis for 2016|url=http://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annula_Risk_Analysis_2016.pdf|publisher=Frontex}}</ref>

====2016====
In January and February 2016, over 123,000 migrants landed in Greece, compared to about 4,600 in the same period of 2015.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2016/03/11/world/europe/europe-tries-to-shut-down-routes-as-migrant-flow-intensifies.html|title=Europe Tries to Shut Down Routes as Migrant Flow Intensifies|author1=LARRY BUCHANAN |author2=SERGIO PEÇANHA |newspaper=The New York Times|date=11 March 2016|access-date=13 March 2016}}</ref> In March, following North Macedonia's closure of the Western Balkan route and the enforcement of the EU–Turkey deal on 20 March, the number of migrants arriving in Greece decreased to 26,460, less than half the figure recorded in February. Syrians, Afghans and Iraqis continued to account for the largest share of the migrants arriving in Greece.<ref name="FrontexMarch2016">{{cite news|title=Number of migrants arriving in Greece dropped in March|url=http://frontex.europa.eu/news/number-of-migrants-arriving-in-greece-dropped-in-march-aInDt3|work=Frontex|date=18 April 2016}}</ref> This downward trend continued in April when only 2,700 migrants arrived in Greece, a 90 percent decrease when compared to the previous month.<ref name="FrontexApril2016">{{cite news|title=Number of migrants arriving in Greece dropped 90 per cent in April|url=http://frontex.europa.eu/news/number-of-migrants-arriving-in-greece-dropped-90-in-april-6e7oBw|work=Frontex|date=13 May 2016}}</ref>

Due to improved weather conditions, the number of mainly African migrants [[Immigration to Italy|crossing the sea to Italy]] doubled between February and March, reaching nearly 9,600 in March 2016, compared to 2,283 in March 2015.<ref name=":6">{{cite web|url=http://migration.iom.int/docs/Q3_Overview_Arrivals_to_Europe.pdf|title=Migration Flows to Europe – Quarterly Overview|date=October 2017|publisher=International Organisation of Migration|access-date=4 November 2017}}</ref><ref name="FrontexMarch2016"/> In April, the number of migrants arriving in Italy (8,370) dropped by 13 percent compared to the previous month and by 50 percent when compared to the same month in 2015; despite this, Italy exceeded the totals for Greece for the first time since June 2015.<ref name="FrontexApril2016"/> On 16 April, a [[List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea|shipwreck]] of a large boat between Libya and Italy was reported, in which as many as 500 people may have died.<ref>{{cite news|title=Massive loss of life reported in latest Mediterranean tragedy|url=http://www.unhcr.org/57178bcf6.html|publisher=UNHCR|date=20 April 2016}}</ref>

The mass influx of migrants into Europe was not seen as favourable in many EU countries. Many citizens disapproved of how EU handled the migrant crisis, with 94 percent of Greeks and 88 percent of Swedes disapproving of the measures taken, among other countries with similar disapproval rates.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.pewglobal.org/2016/06/07/euroskepticism-beyond-brexit/pm_2016-06-07_brexit-03/|title=Overwhelming majorities unhappy with EU's handling of refugees|date=6 June 2016}}</ref> These findings contributed to the creation and implementation of the [[European Union–Turkey relations#EU-Turkey deal on migrant crisis|EU–Turkey Refugee Agreement]], which was signed in March 2016; the numbers of refugees entering Greece decreased afterwards. In February 2016, 57,066 migrants arrived in Greece from the sea. From that point on, discounting March, the highest number of migrants reaching Greece by sea was 3,650 in April.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://data.unhcr.org/mediterranean/country.php?id=83|title=UNHCR Refugees/Migrants Response – Mediterranean|first=United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees|last=(UNHCR)}}</ref> While there is no direct connection to the implementation of the EU–Turkey deal, the number of migrants arriving in Italy in that same time period increased. From March 2016 to October 2016, 140,358 migrants arrived in Italy by sea and averaged 20,051 migrants per month.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://data.unhcr.org/mediterranean/country.php?id=105|title=UNHCR Refugees/Migrants Response – Mediterranean|first=United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees|last=(UNHCR)}}</ref> Overall the number of migrants arriving into the EU dropped, but the EU still worked to create agencies and plans to mitigate the crisis. In addition to the EU–Turkey Refugee Agreement, the European Border and Coast Guard Agency was launched on 6 October 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://frontex.europa.eu/news/european-border-and-coast-guard-agency-launches-today-CHIYAp|archive-url=https://wayback.archive-it.org/all/20171009193452/http://frontex.europa.eu/news/european-border-and-coast-guard-agency-launches-today-CHIYAp|url-status=dead|archive-date=2017-10-09|title=Frontex – News – European Border and Coast Guard Agency launches today}}</ref>

====2017====
Data released by the IOM for the third quarter of 2017 recorded a total of 146,287 arrivals to Europe, of which 137,771 were by sea, which is less than half the total recorded by the end of September 2016. The greatest decrease in influx was noted on the Eastern Mediterranean route. Despite an 86 percent drop in the number of migrant and refugee arrivals in September 2017 when compared to September 2016, Greece observed a steady increase in the number of migrants from September 2016. While Italy also noted lower numbers of arriving migrants in 2017, there was a significant jump in the number of migrants reaching Spain, with over 16,000 having arrived in the country. In 2017, ease of access via the West Mediterranean route had boosted migrant numbers from Africa, with preference being given to Spain over Italy or Greece as a landing point.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.express.co.uk/news/politics/826766/Migrant-crisis-EU-new-challenge-arrivals-Spain|title=EU's migrant nightmare: Arrivals in Spain rocket as smugglers slash crossing price to £800|work=Daily Express|access-date=4 November 2017}}</ref>

Like Spain, the island-nation of Cyprus reported an approximately 8-fold increase in the number of migrants arriving in 2016 and 2017.<ref name=":6" /><ref name=":7">{{cite web|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/pdfscache/13562.pdf|title=Asylum Quarterly Report – explained|website=EC Europa|access-date=4 November 2017}}</ref>

Closure of segments of some traffic-heavy routes such as the Central and Eastern Mediterranean is responsible for the marked decrease in the number of migrants from the Middle East in 2017. However, the Western Mediterranean route was still in full use to facilitate the growing number of illegal immigrants from Africa. Nigerians topped the list of illegal immigrants into Italy in 2017 and formed 16 percent of arrivals there.<ref name=":7" />

In February 2017 the Italian government agreed to fund the Libyan coast guard. Since then many migrants were forced to go back to Libya.<ref name="auto12">{{cite web|url=https://www.irishtimes.com/news/world/migrants-deaths-in-mediterranean-reach-record-percentage-1.3652139|title=Migrants deaths in Mediterranean reach record percentage|first=Sally|last=Hayden|website=The Irish Times}}</ref>

In 2017, approximately 825,000 persons acquired citizenship of a member state of the European Union, down from 995,000 in 2016.<ref>{{cite web |title=Acquisition of citizenship in the EU – EU Member States granted citizenship to over 800 thousand persons in 2017 – Moroccans, Albanians and Indians were the main recipients |url=http://europa.eu/rapid/press-release_STAT-19-1550_en.htm |website=europa.eu |publisher=European Commission}}</ref> The largest groups were Moroccan, Albanian, Indian, Turkish and Pakistani nationals.<ref>{{cite web |title=Acquisition of citizenship statistics |url=https://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/Acquisition_of_citizenship_statistics |website=ec.europa.eu |publisher=Eurostat}}</ref>

====2018====
On 7 October 2018 at least 10 migrants are believed to have died in a boat off the coast of [[Morocco]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/video/migrants-in-mediterranean-sea-face-rescue-delays-1312356931718|title='The potential for loss of life is a lot higher now' in Mediterranean Sea|website=NBC News}}</ref> Helena Maleno, founder of the group Walking Borders, told the reporters the migrants constantly appealed for help from [[Spain]] and Morocco before they died.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/dozens-migrants-feared-dead-mediterranean-sea-morocco-n916121|title=Dozens of migrants feared dead after waiting 36 hours for rescue|website=NBC News}}</ref>

====2019====
In August 2019, more than 270 Europe-bound migrants were rescued by the Libyan coast guard from Tripoli's Mediterranean coast; they were travelling in four different boats.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.660citynews.com/2019/08/17/libya-intercepts-boats-with-over-270-europe-bound-migrants/|title=Libya intercepts boats with over 270 Europe-bound migrants|access-date=17 August 2019|website=660 News}}</ref> According to a UN report, more than 45,000 migrants had reached Europe by sea by August, of whom 859 had reportedly died in transit.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://haberlutfen.com/un-45000-refugees-enter-europe-in-2019/|title=UN: 45,000+ refugees enter Europe in 2019|access-date=23 August 2019|website=haberlutfen}}</ref> In September 2019, the Libyan Cost Guard intercepted another 108 Europe-bound migrants off the Mediterranean coast; 13 were women, and seven children.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.mymotherlode.com/news/middle-east/839021/libyas-coast-guard-intercepts-108-europe-bound-migrants.html|title=Libya's coast guard intercepts 108 Europe-bound migrants|access-date=3 September 2019|website=My Mother Lode}}</ref> On 8 October, Italian authorities rescued 22 Europe-bound migrants from a boat carrying around 50 people. At the time of the rescue, the bodies of 13 women were also allegedly found, and it was later revealed that others were still missing. On 16 October, Italian authorities found the bodies of at least 12 people who had died in the incident.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://twnews.co.uk/gb-news/bodies-of-migrants-who-died-at-sea-located-by-italian-authorities|title=Bodies of migrants who died at sea located by Italian authorities|access-date=16 October 2019|website=The World News}}</ref> In November, Italian coast guards rescued 149 Europe-bound migrants after their boat capsized. Italian coast guards found five dead bodies afterwards and confirmed that the death toll from the incident totalled at least 18.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.heraldonline.com/news/nation-world/world/article237939289.html|title=Italy recovers 5 more bodies from sunken migrant boat |access-date=1 December 2019|website=The Herald}}</ref>

====2020====
In late September 2020, [[Cyprus]] authorities were reported to have abandoned 200 migrant workers at sea without fuel and food. The migrants alleged that their asylum claims were ignored and were instead beaten in some cases by the [[Greek Cypriots|Greek Cypriot]] marine police officers. The [[United Nations]] peacekeepers reported that during their rescue in Lebanon, at least 13 people had either died or been lost at sea.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.hrw.org/news/2020/09/29/cyprus-asylum-seekers-summarily-returned|title=Cyprus: Asylum Seekers Summarily Returned|access-date=29 September 2020|website=Human Rights Watch}}</ref>

====2014====
According to [[Eurostat]], [[Member state of the European Union|EU member states]] received 626,065 asylum applications in 2014, the highest number since the 672,000 applications received in 1992. The main countries of origin of asylum seekers, accounting for almost half of the total, were [[Syria]] (20 percent), [[Afghanistan]] (7 percent), [[Kosovo]] (6 percent), [[Eritrea]] (6 percent) and [[Albania]].<ref>{{cite web|title=The number of asylum applicants in the EU jumped to more than 625 000 in 2014|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/6751779/3-20032015-BP-EN.pdf/35e04263-2db5-4e75-b3d3-6b086b23ef2b|publisher=EUROSTAT}}</ref>

In 2014, decisions on asylum applications in the EU made in the first instance{{Clarify|reason=|date=May 2020}} resulted in more than 160,000 asylum seekers being granted protection status, while a further 23,000 received protection status on appeal. The rate of recognition of asylum applicants was 45 percent at the first instance and 18 percent on appeal. The main beneficiaries of protection status, accounting for more than half of the total, were Syrians (68,300, 37 percent), Eritreans (14,600, 8 percent) and Afghans (14,100, 8 percent).<ref name="auto5">{{cite web |title=EU Member States granted protection to more than 185 000 asylum seekers in 2014 |url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/6827382/3-12052015-AP-EN.pdf/6733f080-c072-4bf5-91fc-f591abf28176 |publisher=EUROSTAT}}</ref>

Four countries – Germany, Sweden, Italy and France – received around two-thirds of the EU's asylum applications and granted almost two-thirds of the applicants protection status in 2014. Sweden, Hungary and Austria were among the top recipients of EU asylum applications ''per capita'', when adjusted for their own populations, with 8.4 asylum seekers per 1,000 inhabitants in Sweden, 4.3 in Hungary, and 3.2 in Austria.<ref name="auto6">{{cite web |url=http://m.euronews.com/en/304485/ |title=euronews – Data raises questions over EU's attitude towards asylum seekers |publisher=euronews.com |access-date=28 August 2015 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160328233348/http://m.euronews.com/en/304485/ |archive-date=28 March 2016 |url-status=dead |df=dmy-all }}</ref><ref name="auto7">{{cite news |url=https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/08/28/world/europe/countries-under-strain-from-european-migration-crisis.html|title=Which Countries Are Under the Most Strain in the European Migration Crisis? |newspaper=The New York Times |date=28 August 2015 |access-date=28 August 2015}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |title=Asylum in the EU |url=http://ec.europa.eu/dgs/home-affairs/e-library/docs/infographics/asylum/infographic_asylum_en.pdf |publisher=European Commission}}</ref>

====2015====
In 2015, EU member states received 1,255,640 first-time asylum applications, more than double that of the previous year. The highest number of first-time applicants was registered in Germany (with 441,800 applicants, or 35 percent of all applicants in EU states), followed by Hungary (174,400, 14 percent), Sweden (156,100, 12 percent), Austria (85,500, 7 percent), Italy (83,200, 7 percent) and France (70,600, 6 percent). Compared with the population, the highest number was registered in Hungary (with 17.7 asylum seekers per 1,000 inhabitants), Sweden (16), Austria (10), Finland (5.9), and Germany (5.4). The three main countries of citizenship of asylum applicants, accounting for more than half of the total, were Syria (362,800 or 29 percent), Afghanistan (178,200, 14 percent), and Iraq (121,500, 10 percent), followed by Kosovo (5 percent), Albania (5 percent), Pakistan (4 percent), Eritrea (3 percent), Nigeria (2 percent), and Iran (2 percent).<ref name="asylum2015">{{cite web|title=Record number of over 1.2 million first time asylum seekers registered in 2015|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/7203832/3-04032016-AP-EN.pdf/790eba01-381c-4163-bcd2-a54959b99ed6|publisher=EUROSTAT}}</ref>

[[File:Top recipients of asylum applications in the EU-28 (2015).png|left|thumb|upright=1.364|Number of first time asylum applications received by the top ten recipients in the EU-28, January–December 2015. The top ten recipients account for more than 90 percent of the asylum applications received in the EU-28.<ref>{{cite web|title=Asylum and first time asylum applicants by citizenship, age and sex Monthly data (rounded)|url=http://appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu/nui/show.do?dataset=migr_asyappctzm|publisher=Eurostat}}</ref>]]
333,350 asylum applicants were granted protection in the EU in 2015 after their asylum applications were accepted. The main beneficiaries of protection status were citizens of Syria (50 percent of persons granted protection in the EU), Eritrea (8 percent), Iraq (7 percent), Afghanistan (5 percent), Iran (2 percent), Somalia (2 percent) and Pakistan (2 percent). The EU countries who granted protection to the highest number of asylum seekers were Germany (who granted protection to 148,200 people), Sweden (34,500), Italy (29,600) and France (26,000). The rate of recognition{{Em dash}}the share of positive decisions in the total number of decisions{{Em dash}}was 52 percent for first-instance decisions in the EU and 14 percent for decisions on appeal. The citizenships with the highest recognition rates at first instance were Syria (97.2 percent), Eritrea (89.8 percent), Iraq (85.7 percent), Afghanistan (67 percent), Iran (64.7 percent), Somalia (63.1 percent) and Sudan (56 percent).<ref>{{cite news|title=EU Member States granted protection to more than 330 000 asylum seekers in 2015|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/7233417/3-20042016-AP-EN.pdf/34c4f5af-eb93-4ecd-984c-577a5271c8c5|work=Eurostat|date=20 April 2016}}</ref>

From January to March 2015, the number of new asylum applicants in the EU was 184,800, an 86 percent increase when compared with the same quarter in the previous year. More than half applied for [[asylum in Germany]] (40 percent) or Hungary (18 percent). The main nationalities of the applicants were Kosovo (48,875 or 26 percent), Syria (29,100 or 16 percent), and Afghanistan (12,910 or 7 percent).<ref name="asylumQ1">{{cite web|title=185 000 first time asylum seekers in the EU in the first quarter of 2015|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/6887997/3-18062015-CP-EN.pdf/4457b050-26f9-4cf1-bf27-9ffb73ff8c7b|publisher=EUROSTAT|date=18 June 2015}}</ref> In the second quarter of 2015, 213,200 people applied for asylum in the EU, a 15 percent increase compared with the previous quarter. 38 percent applied for asylum in Germany, followed by Hungary (15 percent) and Austria (8 percent). The main countries of citizenship of asylum seekers, accounting for more than half of the total, were Syria (21 percent), Afghanistan (13 percent), Albania (8 percent), Iraq (6 percent), and Kosovo (5 percent).<ref name="asylumQ2">{{cite web|title=Over 210 000 first time asylum seekers in the EU in the second quarter of 2015|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/6996925/3-18092015-BP-EN.pdf/b0377f79-f06d-4263-aa5b-cc9b4f6a838f|publisher=EUROSTAT|date=18 September 2015}}</ref> From July to September 2015, EU countries received 413,800 first-time asylum applications, almost double the number registered from April to June 2015. Germany and Hungary were the top recipients, with 26 percent each of total applicants. One-third of asylum seekers were Syrians (33 percent), followed by Afghans (14 percent), and Iraqis (11 percent).<ref name="asylumQ3">{{cite web|title=More than 410 000 first time asylum seekers registered in the third quarter of 2015|url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/documents/2995521/7105334/3-10122015-AP-EN.pdf/04886524-58f2-40e9-995d-d97520e62a0e|publisher=Eurostat}}</ref> In the fourth quarter of 2015, there were 426,000 first-time applicants, mainly Syrians (145,130), Afghans (79,255), and Iraqis (53,585). The top recipients were Germany (38 percent), Sweden (21 percent), and Austria (7 percent).<ref name="Asylum quarterly report">{{cite web |title=Asylum quarterly report |url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/statistics-explained/index.php/Asylum_quarterly_report |publisher=EUROSTAT}}</ref>

In August 2015, the German government announced that it expected to receive 800,000 asylum applications by the end of the year.<ref>{{cite news |title=Europe migrant crisis: Germany 'will cope with surge' |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-33992563 |work=BBC News |date=19 August 2015}}</ref> Data released by Germany's Federal Office for Migration and Refugees (BAMF) in January 2016 showed that Germany received 476,649 asylum applications in 2015, mainly from Syrians (162,510), Albanians (54,762), Kosovars (37,095), Afghans (31,902), Iraqis (31,379), Serbians (26,945), Macedonians (14,131), Eritreans (10,990), and Pakistanis (8,472). In 2015, Germany made 282,762 decisions on asylum applications; the overall asylum recognition rate was 49.8 percent (140,915 applicants were granted protection). The most successful applicants were Syrians (101,419 positive decisions; 96% recognition rate), Eritreans (9,300 positive decisions; 92.1% recognition rate) and Iraqis (14,880 positive decisions; 88.6% recognition rate).<ref>{{cite web|title=476.649 Asylanträge im Jahr 2015|url=http://www.bamf.de/SharedDocs/Meldungen/DE/2016/201610106-asylgeschaeftsstatistik-dezember.html|publisher=BAMF|date=6 January 2016}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=Asylgeschäftsstatistik 12/2015|url=http://www.bamf.de/SharedDocs/Anlagen/DE/Downloads/Infothek/Statistik/Asyl/201512-statistik-anlage-asyl-geschaeftsbericht.html?nn=1367522|publisher=BAMF|date=6 January 2016}}</ref>

Sweden received 162,877 asylum applications in 2015, mainly from Syrians (51,338), Afghans (41,564), Iraqis (20,857), Eritreans (7,231) and Somalis (5,465).<ref name=sma2015>{{cite web|title=Applications for asylum received, 2015|url=http://www.migrationsverket.se/download/18.7c00d8e6143101d166d1aab/1451894593595/Inkomna+ans%C3%B6kningar+om+asyl+2015+-+Applications+for+asylum+received+2015.pdf|publisher=[[Swedish Migration Agency]]}}</ref> In 2015, Sweden granted protection to 32,631 asylum applicants and rejected 9,524 applications (a 77% approval rate). The main beneficiaries of protection were Syrians (18,523 positive decisions; 100% recognition rate), Eritreans (6,542 positive decisions; 100% recognition rate) and Afghans (1,088 positive decisions; 74% recognition rate).<ref>{{cite web|title=Asylum decisions, 2015|url=http://www.migrationsverket.se/download/18.7c00d8e6143101d166d1aad/1451894587413/Avgjorda+asyl%C3%A4renden+2015+-+Asylum+desicions+2015.pdf|publisher=[[Swedish Migration Agency]]}}</ref>

In 2016, according to Eurostat, most of the non-EU 28 asylum seekers in EU 28 originated from Syria. Syria, Afghanistan and Iraq together constituted 50 percent of all asylum seekers.<ref name="Asylum 2016">{{cite news |title=Asylum applicants in the EU |url=http://ec.europa.eu/eurostat/news/themes-in-the-spotlight/asylum2016|work=Eurostat|access-date=13 June 2018}}</ref>

====2017====
The second quarter of 2017 recorded a 54 percent decrease in the number of first-time asylum applicants compared to April–June 2016, and 11 percent fewer applicants than January–March 2017. The greatest number of applications were from Syria, Afghanistan, and Nigeria. However, the number of Syrians and Afghans was less than that of the same time in 2016, suggesting that the peak of this crisis had passed. The increasing number of illegal immigrants from Africa suggests that the direction of the crisis changed. While Germany recorded the highest number of first-time applicants (over 49,000), Spain saw a 30 percent increase in the number of asylum seekers, along with Cyprus and Bulgaria.<ref name="Asylum quarterly report" />

=== Migrant arrivals versus "illegal" border crossings ===
The [[European Union|EU]] [[European Border and Coast Guard Agency|Border and Coast Guard Agency (Frontex)]] uses the terms "illegal" and "irregular" border crossings for crossings of an EU external border but not at an official [[Border checkpoint|border-crossing point]] (BCP).<ref name=Frontex2016,p.22>{{cite web |url=https://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annual_Risk_Analysis_2016.pdf#page=24 |page=22 |title=Risk Analysis for 2016 |publisher=[[Frontex]] |date=March 2016}}</ref> These include the crossings of people rescued at sea and brought to land by EU citizens.<ref name=Frontex2016,p.20>{{cite web |url=https://frontex.europa.eu/assets/Publications/Risk_Analysis/Annual_Risk_Analysis_2016.pdf#page=22 |page=20 |title=Risk Analysis for 2016 |publisher=[[Frontex]] |date=March 2016}}</ref> The total number of illegal EU external border crossings can be higher than the number of migrants newly illegally arriving in the EU in a year, especially for the years 2015 and 2016 (see table below). News media sometimes misrepresent these figures as given by Frontex.<ref name="auto1" />

=== Border crossings ===
[[File:Migrants in Hungary 2015 Aug 003.jpg|thumb|Migrants along the Western Balkan route crossing from Serbia into Hungary, 24 August 2015]]
In September 2015, Europol estimated there were 30,000 suspected migrant smugglers, which rose to 55,000 in 2016 and increased to 65,000 in 2017. 63 percent of smugglers were from Europe, 14 percent from the Middle East, 13 percent from Africa, nine percent from Asia excluding the Middle East and one percent from the Americas.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://citizen.co.za/news/news-africa/1879124/europe-migrants-smugglers/|title=EU tracking 65,000 migrant smugglers: Europol|last=CARMICHAEL/AFP|first=by Lachlan|work=The Citizen|access-date=2018-04-29|language=en}}</ref>

Frontex tracks and publishes data on numbers of crossings along the main six routes twice a year. The following table shows the data for the period up to and including the year 2016:
